# Refactor Map — proxybroker2 (Python) → proxybroker-rs (Rust)

> **The primary deliverable.** A refactor without an old→new map is a rewrite gambling
> that the new code will resemble the old code's intent. This turns that gamble into a
> checklist.

> Designed by 11 parallel agents, each reading the full Python source of its module plus
> the verified `research.md`, then reviewed by an adversarial critic (§Critique).
> Assembled deterministically from schema-validated JSON.

**11 modules · 276 mapped items · 110 dropped · 107 deliberate deviations · 59 open questions**

## New structure
```
proxybroker-rs/
  Cargo.toml            single crate, lib + bin. default = cli, server, geo, geo-bundled
  rust-toolchain.toml   pinned stable — a crates.io lib needing nightly is unusable
  LICENSE               Apache-2.0 (derivative of proxybroker2)
  NOTICE                attribution + statement of changes, Apache-2.0 §4(b)
  LICENSE-DATA          CC BY 4.0, covers data/ only
  data/
    dbip-country-lite.mmdb   DB-IP Country Lite, NOT MaxMind GeoLite2
  src/
    error.rs              ← 
    utils.rs              ← 
    negotiator.rs         ← 
    proxy.rs              ← 
    judge.rs              ← 
    checker.rs            ← 
    broker.rs             ← 
    bin/proxybroker.rs    ← 
    resolver.rs           ← 
    geo.rs (ported from proxybroker/resolver.py, 558 LOC)← 
    server/mod.rs         ← 
    server/pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)← 
    provider/mod.rs       ← 
    provider/spec.rs      ← 
    provider/registry.rs (+ provider/custom/*.rs)← 
```

## Deliberate deviations from Python

Behaviour that intentionally differs. Each is a decision, not an accident — recorded
here so it can be reviewed rather than discovered later.

| Module | Deviation | Why |
|---|---|---|
| `error.rs` | `ProxyRecvError` and `ProxySendError` collapse into a single `ProxyError::Reset`. | Both carry `errmsg = "connection_is_reset"` (errors.py:21, :25), so Python's counter already merges them — stats output is byte-identical. No call site distinguishes them: checker.py:212-213 and server.py:418-419 catch them in the same tuple; server.py:507 catches only ProxyRecvError but server._stream writes with `writer.write`/`drain`, never `proxy.send`, so ProxySendError cannot arise there. What is lost is a type-level distinction nobody consumed; the send/recv direction survives in the tracing message exactly as it did in Python's separate `msg` argument. |
| `error.rs` | The Rust type named `ProxyError` includes `BadStatus`, `BadResponse`, `BadStatusLine`, `ErrorOnStream` and `Resolve`, which in Python are NOT subclasses of `ProxyError` (they subclass bare `Exception`, errors.py:12/36/40/44/48). `issubclass(BadStatusError, ProxyError)` was False; the Rust equivalent is True. | The Python hierarchy tracks nothing real — the split is between "raised in proxy.py" and "raised elsewhere", not between kinds of failure. Every consumer already unions them (checker.py:210-216, server.py:415-423). Name reuse is deliberate: `ProxyError` is the honest name for "a per-proxy failure", and the Python base class it displaces was never raised. Flagging because `tests/test_public_contracts.py:308-318` asserts the old hierarchy — that assertion has no Rust analogue and will not be ported. |
| `error.rs` | Bug fix: the latent `AttributeError` in `proxy.log(err=...)` is made unrepresentable. | `ProxyError`, `NoProxyError` and `ResolveError` have no `errmsg` (errors.py:4-13), so `proxy.py:333`'s `self.stat["errors"][err.errmsg] += 1` raises `AttributeError` for any of them. Today it never fires only because no call site happens to pass one — nothing enforces that. `as_str(&self)` is a total match; the class of bug is deleted rather than avoided. |
| `error.rs` | Bug fix: `server.py:433`'s `"Timeout" in repr(e)` becomes `failure.cause == ProxyError::Timeout`. | Python detects a wrapped ProxyTimeoutError by substring-matching the repr of an ErrorOnStream. That is a false positive on any nested exception whose repr contains "Timeout" for unrelated reasons (an `asyncio.TimeoutError` from the OTHER branch of server.py:503-510, or a proxy message containing the word), and a false negative if the repr format ever changes. The wrong answer here silently mis-attributes a successful EOF as a proxy failure — it is the exact case the comment at server.py:434-436 is trying to special-case. Typed cause, `==`. |
| `error.rs` | `ProxyError::Resolve` gains a Display string "resolve_failed" that has no Python counterpart, but is deliberately NOT incremented into the errors histogram. | Python's `ResolveError` has no `errmsg` at all. A variant needs a Display string, so one is invented. Counting it would ADD a new key to the user-visible stats contract — and would be impossible anyway on the path that matters: at `api.py:443` the resolve fails before the `Proxy` object (and therefore its `stat` dict) exists. The histogram key set stays exactly {connection_failed, connection_is_reset, connection_timeout, empty_response, bad_status, bad_response, error_on_stream}. Recorded because if we ever DO want resolve failures in the stats, that is a contract change needing sign-off, not a refactor. |
| `error.rs` | `ProxyError` implements `Display`/`Error` by hand instead of deriving `thiserror::Error` as research.md:920-930 sketches. | Deviation from the research sketch, not from Python. Per-variant `#[error("connection_failed")]` attributes would duplicate the string table that `as_str()` must own anyway (serde needs `&'static str`, and `Display::to_string()` allocates — unacceptable for a hot counter key). One table, two thin impls. `Error` still uses thiserror, where `#[from]`/`#[source]`/`#[error(transparent)]` do real work. |
| `error.rs` | `Error::Config` makes an explicitly-named bad provider config FATAL, where `provider_utils.py:575` logs and returns `None` for every config path. | Locked decision 7 makes providers a config edit rather than a recompile, which makes config the main user-authored surface. Silently skipping a file the user explicitly pointed at means their edit does nothing and they get zero feedback. Directory SCANS keep the Python log-and-skip behavior (one typo must not kill 37 working providers) — only the named-path case errors. |
| `error.rs` | A bad `--geo-db` path returns `Error::GeoDb` instead of crashing at import. | Python opens the mmdb at module import and lets the failure escape as an unhandled maxminddb error. Locked decision 3 requires supporting a user-supplied path, which makes "you gave me a file that is not an mmdb" a routine user error deserving a named error, not a stack trace. Per-lookup misses stay non-fatal, matching resolver.py:106's swallow (and maxminddb 0.29 returns `Ok(None)` for a miss anyway, research.md:569). |
| `negotiator.rs` | TLS SNI / server name for HttpsNgtr is the JUDGE hostname (`target.host`), not the proxy's IP address. | PYTHON BUG. `HttpsNgtr.negotiate` calls `self._proxy.connect(ssl=True)`, which passes `server_hostname=self.host` — `self` there is the **Proxy**, so the SNI is the proxy's own IP literal, while the TLS session is actually with the judge behind the CONNECT tunnel. It goes unnoticed because the default context is `check_hostname=False, verify_mode=CERT_NONE` and CPython omits SNI for IP-literal server names. Consequence: judges on SNI-required shared hosting (e.g. `https://www.proxy-listen.de/azenv.php`) can get the wrong vhost or a handshake failure, and every HTTPS proxy checked against them is falsely marked dead. Rust sends the correct SNI. Effect: more proxies will pass HTTPS checks than Python reports. Needs sign-off — it changes measured results. |
| `negotiator.rs` | Certificate verification is a custom rustls `ServerCertVerifier` that ALWAYS returns Ok but records the presented chain, instead of Python's blanket `CERT_NONE` context. | research.md's recommendation. Same accept-everything outcome (mandatory — we are deliberately connecting through MITM-capable intermediaries), but the chain is captured, which is how a proxy MITM-ing TLS gets detected: a signal Python throws away. The `verify_ssl=True` opt-in path stays (real platform verification). NOTE: the verifier is constructed in checker.rs and passed in as `&TlsConnector`; negotiator.rs does not decide policy. Sign-off needed on carrying the extra signal at all — it implies a field on the check outcome. |
| `negotiator.rs` | One timeout budget for the whole negotiation (caller-applied `tokio::time::timeout`), instead of Python's per-recv `asyncio.wait_for(..., timeout=self._timeout)`. | Python applies the full timeout to EACH `recv` independently, so a SOCKS5 handshake (2 recvs + 1 more for domain-ATYP replies) can legitimately consume 2-3x the configured timeout, and Connect25 (head + 3-byte banner) up to 2x. That is unintentional — the timeout reads as a per-attempt budget everywhere it is documented. Rust makes the budget mean what it says. Effect: some very slow proxies that Python eventually accepts will now time out and be retried/dropped. Sign-off needed: it tightens the accept threshold. Cheap alternative if the lead disagrees: wrap each read in its own timeout to reproduce Python exactly. |
| `negotiator.rs` | A short/truncated SOCKS handshake read is classified as a per-proxy failure ('bad_response'/'empty_response') instead of crashing the check task with an IndexError. | PYTHON BUG. `Proxy._recv(length=N)` catches `IncompleteReadError` and returns `e.partial`. `Proxy.recv` then only rejects a fully EMPTY buffer. So a proxy that sends exactly 1 byte to the SOCKS5 greeting reaches `resp[1]` => IndexError — which is NOT in checker.py's `except (...)` tuple, so it escapes `_check` entirely and kills the check for that proxy with an unhandled exception (and, being raised inside the gathered task, is easy to miss). Same hole at `header = await self._proxy.recv(4)` / `header[3]`. tokio-socks surfaces it as `Io(UnexpectedEof)` and we classify it. Effect: a malicious/broken proxy can no longer take out a check task. |
| `negotiator.rs` | The CONNECT status line is parsed by splitting the line on whitespace, not by slicing fixed byte offsets [9:12]. | Python's `get_status_code` assumes the response starts exactly `HTTP/1.x ` (9 bytes). Preserves behavior for every well-formed HTTP/1.0 and HTTP/1.1 reply (all real proxies), but differs on malformed/unusual first lines: e.g. `HTTP/1.1 200` (double space) parses to 200 in Rust and to 400=>BadStatusError in Python; a proxy replying `HTTP/2 200` likewise. Both directions are strictly more-correct in Rust and vanishingly rare, but they are behavior changes. The failure ERROR VARIANT is unchanged (BadStatus). |
| `negotiator.rs` | tokio-socks' 23 reply-code error variants are collapsed onto Python's error-histogram keys (all protocol variants => 'bad_response'; Io/UnexpectedEof => 'empty_response'; other Io => 'connection_is_reset'), with the precise variant retained only as the error source for tracing. | Keeps `Proxy.stat['errors']` — which is user-visible via `as_json()`/`error_rate` and is a documented API surface — key-for-key identical to Python. The richer classification is available in logs and to the error `#[source]` chain. Sign-off: if the lead wants the 23 variants promoted into the stats histogram (better data, but a breaking change to the JSON output vs proxybroker2), say so now — the mapping fn is the single place it changes. |
| `negotiator.rs` | `negotiate` takes `Stream` by value and returns `Result<Stream, _>` rather than mutating `&mut Option<Stream>` via `Option::take` as the brief specified. | Not a behavior deviation — a deviation from the brief's prescribed mechanics, flagged for sign-off per instructions. Both tokio-socks (`connect_with_socket(socket, target)`) and tokio-rustls (`TlsConnector::connect(sni, stream)`) consume the transport, so consuming ownership is the natural signature; the Option slot would exist only to be `take()`n and refilled on every path. The error path drops the stream = closes it, which is exactly Python's per-attempt `finally: proxy.close()` (checker.py never reuses a connection after a failed negotiation — verified in both `_check` and `_check_conn_25`). If Proxy must keep holding the stream across the call, `Option::take`/`mem::replace` at the CALL SITE reproduces the brief with the same internals. |
| `negotiator.rs` | `read_head` caps the CONNECT response head at a fixed byte/line limit; Python's `_recv` loop is bounded only by the wall-clock timeout. | A hostile proxy can stream headers forever at just-fast-enough a rate; Python's only defense is the timeout, and the buffer grows unbounded in the meantime (one attacker-controlled allocation per in-flight check, times `max_conn`). Exceeding the cap => `BadResponse`. Effect on honest proxies: none (a CONNECT reply head is < 1 KiB). |
| `proxy.rs` | error_rate() and avg_resp_time() return unrounded values; the 2dp rounding moves to Serialize and Display. | Python rounds inside the property, so server.py:119's `proxy.error_rate > self._max_error_rate` compares a ROUNDED number: at 503 errors / 1000 requests the Python computes 0.5 and keeps the proxy, Rust computes 0.503 and drops it. Boundary shifts by <0.005. Rounding a value that is about to be compared, not printed, is a bug; JSON output stays byte-identical because the rounding still happens at the wire boundary. Sign-off needed: this changes which proxies a long-running server pool evicts, at the margin. |
| `proxy.rs` | timeout and verify_ssl are no longer Proxy fields/constructor params; they live in ConnectOpts owned by the Checker. | They are run policy, not proxy identity. A public `Proxy::new(addr, types, timeout, verify_ssl)` would freeze them into the yielded record forever. Breaks source-compat with anyone constructing `Proxy(host, port, timeout=15)` — but this is a new crate with no API contract to keep. |
| `proxy.rs` | host is IpAddr, so the legacy leading-zero IPv4 form ("127.0.0.001") is REJECTED. | resolver.py:66-89's host_is_ip deliberately normalizes octets with leading zeros, with a comment saying provider feeds in the wild emit that form and historical proxybroker accepted it (CPython rejects it since 3.9.5 / CVE-2021-29921). `"127.0.0.001".parse::<IpAddr>()` fails. Without a lenient parser in resolver.rs we silently drop those proxies. Note the CVE: leading-zero octets are ambiguous (octal vs decimal) and were a real SSRF vector — 'be liberal in what you accept' is exactly how that bug happened. Recommend porting the normalization ONLY as `resolver::parse_ip_lenient` used at provider-parse time (never on user input), or accepting the drop. See open questions. |
| `proxy.rs` | send() maps any io::Error to ProxyError::Reset; Python catches only ConnectionResetError and lets every other OSError escape uncaught. | An EPIPE/ETIMEDOUT on write propagates out of `Proxy.send` past checker.py's except-list (which catches ProxySendError, not OSError) and out of `Checker.check`, killing the check task with an unclassified exception. Rust classifies it as a per-proxy failure, which is what it is. Bug fix. |
| `proxy.rs` | recv_exact() returns Err(EmptyRecv) on a short read; Python returns the partial bytes. | proxy.py:472-473 catches IncompleteReadError and returns `e.partial`. The SOCKS5 negotiator then does `resp[0]`/`resp[1]` on a possibly-1-byte buffer -> IndexError, which no `except` in checker.py catches -> the whole check task dies on a truncated SOCKS greeting. Rust surfaces it as the per-proxy error it is. Bug fix. |
| `proxy.rs` | recv_head() bounds the header buffer (proposed 64 KiB) and errors with BadResponse past it. | Python's `while not self.reader.at_eof(): resp += line` has no cap. A hostile or broken proxy that streams headers forever grows the buffer until the connect timeout fires — memory bounded only by bandwidth x timeout, x max_conn concurrent checks. We are by definition talking to untrusted hosts. Bug fix; the cap is a new constant with no Python equivalent. |
| `proxy.rs` | The proxy log stores a structured Event enum; messages are not truncated to 60 chars at store time. | Python truncates on store, so the stored log is lossy for display's sake, and api.py then classifies proxies by substring-matching those truncated strings. Display for Event reproduces the exact strings (verbose output unchanged) and api.rs matches on variants. A downstream consumer reading `get_log()[i][1]` as a string gets an `Event` instead — deliberate. |
| `proxy.rs` | A runtime is excluded from the response-time average by event kind, not by `'timeout' not in msg`. | proxy.py:334 sniffs the message text. Any message containing the substring 'timeout' anywhere — e.g. `Request: GET /timeout HTTP/1.1` against a judge with that path — is silently excluded from the average. Rare, but it is a text search standing in for a type check. Bug fix. |
| `proxy.rs` | geo is Option<Geo>, populated by the Broker after construction rather than in the constructor. | Python's `__init__` calls a module-global mmdb reader opened at import time (resolver.py:24). Locked #3 makes the geo DB a user-supplyable, feature-gated, Broker-owned resource; there is no global to call. Also means `Proxy::new` is infallible and does no I/O. |
| `proxy.rs` | Proxy.create() no longer logs `log.error(...)` on resolve failure. | The library shouldn't decide that a resolve miss (routine — locked #7 measured 9 of 38 provider domains as NXDOMAIN) is error-level. It returns Err(ProxyError::Resolve); the Broker counts it and tracing::debug!s it. |
| `proxy.rs` | ProxyConn borrows the Proxy mutably for the duration of a check. | Direct consequence of breaking the cycle. Python can hand the same Proxy to a negotiator, a checker and the output queue simultaneously; Rust cannot check a proxy and yield it at the same time. This is the desired constraint, but it does mean a future 'stream partial results while still checking' feature would need a redesign, not a tweak. |
| `judge.rs` | Judge.check catches only {asyncio.TimeoutError, ClientOSError, ClientResponseError, ServerDisconnectedError}; any other error (a generic aiohttp.ClientError, a decode failure inside `await resp.text()`, an invalid URL) escapes check() → escapes the bare `asyncio.gather` in check_judges → aborts EVERY other judge probe → Broker dies with "Not found judges". Rust maps ANY probe error to None (judge unavailable, logged at debug); one hostile judge cannot take down the run. | Bug fix. A judge probe is definitionally best-effort — the entire design already treats failure as "skip this judge". Sign-off needed because a previously-fatal misconfiguration (e.g. a malformed --judge URL) now degrades to a warning instead of an error; mitigated by JudgeSpec::parse rejecting bad URLs eagerly in JudgePool::new as a ConfigError. |
| `judge.rs` | Python stores `self.host = urlparse(url).netloc` — the authority INCLUDING any port — and then (a) DNS-resolves that string (judge.py:95 `self._resolver.resolve(self.host)`) and (b) hands it to the negotiator as the CONNECT target (checker.py:207/235 `negotiate(host=judge.host, ip=judge.ip)` → `_CONNECT_request(host, 25)` → authority `"example.com:8080:25"`). Any judge URL with an explicit port is therefore silently dropped at resolve time, or produces a malformed CONNECT if it survives. Rust splits `host` (DNS name / CONNECT target) from `port` from `authority` (the Host: header + fullpath string). | Bug fix. Invisible on the default judge list (no ports), live the moment a user passes `--judge http://myjudge.example:8080/azenv.php`. Sign-off needed because it changes what Checker passes to the negotiator: `judge.host` in Rust is the bare hostname, and checker.rs must use `judge.authority` for the Host header / fullpath URI. |
| `judge.rs` | Python computes the path as `url.split(self.host)[-1]` — split on the host substring, take the LAST piece. For a URL where the authority string reappears later (e.g. `http://example.com/r?u=example.com`) this yields `""` and the checker then requests `GET HTTP/1.1`. Rust uses `Url::path()` + `Url::query()`. | Bug fix, plus it drops a whole class of string-slicing surprises. Cannot fire on the default judges; fires on user-supplied ones. |
| `judge.rs` | Anything other than http/https/smtp in a judge URL is a ConfigError at parse time. Python uppercases whatever scheme it finds and only explodes later — with a KeyError on `self.available[self.scheme]` inside the gather, taking every other judge with it (see deviation 1). | Fail fast on config, and JudgeScheme being a closed enum is what makes JudgeSet's three fields (rather than a fallible dict lookup) sound. Sign-off: `ftp://…` is now rejected instead of accepted-then-fatal — strictly better, but it IS a new error path on the CLI. |
| `judge.rs` | Readiness is one gate for the whole judge set, not three per-scheme events. An HTTP-proxy check that starts during warm-up now waits for ALL judge probes to settle (bounded by JudgeConfig.timeout, default 8s) rather than for the first HTTP judge to verify (~200ms measured against azenv.net). | Removes three sync primitives, three conditional waits, the `_req_{http,https,smtp}_proto` triple, and the `Judge.ev[X].set()`-to-unblock-stranded-waiters hack. The cost is a one-time ≤8s window that JudgePool::warm overlaps with provider scraping, so in practice the first proxy has not arrived yet. If a benchmark shows this delays first-yield, the fix is three OnceCells, not a Notify — but do not pay for it speculatively. |
| `judge.rs` | Python's `Judge.available`/`Judge.ev` are class attributes, so two concurrent Brokers share one judge list and one set of events; `Checker.__init__` calls `Judge.clear()` unconditionally, which wipes (and un-sets the events of) a *live* first Broker mid-run — that Broker's already-waiting checks then proceed against an empty `available` and hit `secrets.choice([])` → IndexError. Rust: JudgePool is instance state on Checker (decision 10) and JudgeSet::get_random returns Option. | Bug fix, explicitly mandated by locked decision 10. Recorded here because it is a real behavior change: multi-Broker programs that today crash or cross-contaminate will now work, and each Broker pays its own judge-probe cost (N Brokers = N probe rounds — accepted; sharing a pool across Brokers is an explicit opt-in the caller can build by passing one Arc<JudgePool>, not an accident of module scope). |
| `judge.rs` | `JudgeSet::get_random` returns `Option<Arc<Judge>>`; Python's `secrets.choice(cls.available[scheme])` raises IndexError on an empty list. | The guard against that (check_judges disabling the protocol) lives 100 lines from the call site and is easy to bypass. Sign-off point: checker.rs must now handle `None` — treat it as "this protocol cannot be checked", the same outcome Python's disable_protocols path reaches, but locally and without a panic. |
| `checker.rs` | CONNECT:25 is actually removed from the protocol list when no SMTP judges are reachable. | BUG FIX. Python appends the string 'SMTP' to `disable_protocols`, then removes matching entries from `self._ngtrs` — but `_ngtrs` holds negotiator names, where the SMTP negotiator is called 'CONNECT:25'. The removal no-ops. A run with `--types CONNECT:25` and unreachable SMTP judges then hits `_check_conn_25` → `Judge.get_random('CONNECT:25')` → `secrets.choice([])` → IndexError propagating out of `check()`. Typing the list as `NegotiatorKind` fixes it and makes the class unrepresentable. |
| `checker.rs` | `proxy.is_working` is set true ONLY when the whole check succeeds, including the type/anonymity filter. Python sets `proxy.is_working = any(results)` (line 193) BEFORE consulting `_types_passed` (line 195) and never unsets it. | BUG FIX. A proxy rejected for anonymity level is left advertising `is_working == True` to anyone reading the object. `CheckOutcome` removes the side channel entirely. |
| `checker.rs` | Protocol iteration order in `check()` is the fixed NGTRS declaration order (HTTP, HTTPS, SOCKS4, SOCKS5, CONNECT:80, CONNECT:25), not hash order. | Locked requirement + determinism. Python iterates `self._ngtrs`, a `set` of `str`, whose order is PYTHONHASHSEED-randomized per process — the same proxy can be classified under a different protocol on different runs (the first protocol that works wins `check()`'s `any`, and the anonymity level attaches to whichever protocol was tried). Rust is reproducible. |
| `checker.rs` | DNSBL: a proxy is 'listed' only on a successful, non-empty A answer. Resolver errors of any kind mean 'not listed'. | BUG FIX. Python's `any(r for r in responses if not isinstance(r, ResolveError))` over `gather(return_exceptions=True)` treats every non-ResolveError exception as a positive listing — a DNS timeout or an unrelated bug silently blacklists a good proxy, and there is no log line to notice it. Note the fix makes the checker slightly more permissive: proxies that Python discarded on a flaky DNSBL query now pass. |
| `checker.rs` | DNSBL query names for IPv6 proxies use RFC 5782 reversed-nibble form. | BUG FIX. Python's `'.'.join(reversed(host.split('.')))` on an IPv6 literal returns the address unchanged (no dots), producing a nonsense query that always fails — so IPv6 proxies silently bypass DNSBL entirely. This fork ships IPv6 support elsewhere (bracketed parsing, SOCKS5 ATYP=0x04), so the hole is reachable. |
| `checker.rs` | Chunked-but-uncompressed judge responses are de-chunked before the response checks run. | BUG FIX / behavior change. Python only strips chunk framing on the compressed path; an uncompressed chunked response keeps its `278\r\n...\r\n0\r\n\r\n` framing in the string that `_check_test_response` and `_get_anonymity_lvl` then search. It mostly works by accident (substring search), but the chunk-size hex digits pollute `get_all_ip` and the `via`/`proxy` mark counts, which is exactly the anonymity classifier's input. Consequence: an anonymity level may differ from Python's on such judges. Rust is right. |
| `checker.rs` | gzip/deflate are selected by `Content-Encoding` (with a Gz→Zlib fallback), not by zlib's `MAX_WBITS\|32` auto-detect window. | flate2 has no single auto-detect decoder. The fallback preserves Python's tolerance for mislabeled encodings; a body that decompresses under neither yields an empty string, same as Python's `except zlib.error: content = b''`. |
| `checker.rs` | `Checker::check` cannot be called before judges are established — enforced by the type system, since `Checker` only exists as the output of `probe()`. | Locked #10 + the brief's ordering requirement. Python enforces it with three `asyncio.Event`s that `check()` must remember to await; forget one and you race the baseline. Trade-off: Broker must `await probe()` before spawning check workers, so judge probing no longer overlaps with proxy checking (it may still overlap with provider grabbing). Costs one judge-probe round-trip (~seconds) at startup, once. |
| `checker.rs` | `Error::NoJudges` is returned from `Broker::find`'s setup path, not raised from inside a spawned task. | Locked #11 (fatal vs per-proxy). Python raises `RuntimeError('Not found judges')` inside the `check_judges()` task; whether the user ever sees it depends on gather/task-exception plumbing in api.py. |
| `checker.rs` | `Proxy` does not own a socket; each attempt opens, negotiates, uses, and drops its own `TcpStream`. | Locked #8 — `Proxy` is yielded to users through `ProxyStream`, so it must be plain, Send, serializable data. Python's `Proxy` is simultaneously a record and a connection handle (`_reader`/`_writer`/`_ssl_context`/`_closed`/`ngtr`), which is why `close()` must be called from a `finally:` in two places. Behavior is equivalent — Python also opens a fresh connection per attempt and closes it in `finally`. `Proxy` still takes `&mut` so stats/runtimes/types are recorded. |
| `checker.rs` | Judge selection uses `rand` (non-crypto), not a CSPRNG. | Python uses `secrets.choice` and its own comment says why: 'clears SonarCloud S2245; the selection is not security-sensitive (just round-robins judges)'. No behavioral requirement. |
| `checker.rs` | `warnings.warn(UserWarning)` → `tracing::warn!` with the correct disabled-protocol list. | No warnings module in Rust; and Python's message is wrong anyway — the missing-SMTP case renders as 'Not found judges for the [] protocol. Checking proxy on protocols [\'SMTP\'] is disabled.' because `nojudges` is never appended for SMTP. |
| `checker.rs` | Anonymity classification ORs the `proxy` mark count with the `via` mark count. | NOT a deviation from the source — flagged because it IS a deviation from the brief, which describes via-count only. checker.py:369-371 is `via = (content.count('via') > judge.marks['via']) or (content.count('proxy') > judge.marks['proxy'])`. Source wins; recording it so the brief's author can confirm. |
| `broker.rs` | `find()` awaits `check_judges()` before returning, instead of racing it against grabbing. | Python spawns `check_judges()` and `_grab()` concurrently and gates individual checks on `Judge.ev[proto]` events (checker.py:173-177). Cost of serializing: judge checks take ~1-2s wall-clock at startup, once. Benefit: `Error::NoJudges` reaches the caller as an `Err` instead of being raised inside a detached task that nobody awaits (checker.py:137 `raise RuntimeError("Not found judges")` is currently swallowed as 'Task exception was never retrieved' — the run then hangs on `Judge.ev` forever). It also deletes three global Events and the entire wait-dance. If the 1-2s startup cost is judged unacceptable, the alternative is a `tokio::sync::watch` gate, which reintroduces the complexity for a one-time 2s. |
| `broker.rs` | Provider concurrency is `buffer_unordered(3)` (continuously refilled) instead of Python's disjoint batches of 3. | api.py:405-416 spawns a batch of 3, drains it via as_completed, and only then spawns the next 3 — so one slow provider idles two slots for the whole batch. `buffer_unordered` keeps exactly 3 in flight at all times. Same concurrency CAP (which is the thing MAX_CONCURRENT_PROVIDERS exists to enforce), strictly better utilization. Observable difference: providers finish in a different order and the grab cycle is faster. |
| `broker.rs` | serve() backpressure is bounded-channel + pool-driven pull, not `await self._proxies.join()`. | Python pauses checking when `self._server and not self._proxies.empty() and self._limit <= 0`, then resumes only when the result queue is FULLY drained (`join()` = every task_done called) — i.e. it refills only after the pool is empty, which is the pathological moment (all proxies just died, requests are failing now). Rust's feeder pulls from the ProxyStream while the pool is below `ServeConfig.limit`, so refill is continuous and the bounded mpsc throttles the checker. Same intent (don't check forever once you have enough), smoother behavior. Deviation is behavioral, not just internal. |
| `broker.rs` | `max_conn: NonZeroUsize`. | Python's `asyncio.Queue(maxsize=0)` means UNBOUNDED — so `Broker(max_conn=0)` silently disables the concurrency cap entirely and checks every proxy at once. `Semaphore::new(0)` would instead deadlock. Neither is what a user means. The type forbids it. |
| `broker.rs` | `ServeConfig.limit: NonZeroUsize` instead of a runtime `if limit <= 0: raise ValueError` (api.py:349). | Same reasoning as Python's — an unlimited serve() grabs forever — but enforced at construction. The error text moves to the CLI's arg parser. |
| `broker.rs` | Failed candidates are counted; Python drops them silently. | api.py:443 `except (ResolveError, ValueError): return`. `Stats.resolve_failed` now records them. `show_stats` currently reports 'Total found proxies: N' where N excludes everything that failed to resolve, with no indication any existed. |
| `broker.rs` | Ext-IP discovery failure is fatal (`Error::ExtIpUnknown`) only when the query requests anonymity levels; otherwise it warns and continues with an empty ext-IP set. | Python propagates any exception from `get_real_ext_ips()` out of find(), killing runs that did not care about anonymity. But silently continuing is worse when the user DID ask for `High`: with no real IP known, `_get_anonymity_lvl` (checker.py:373) can never return 'Transparent', so every transparent proxy is misclassified as High/Anonymous and silently passes a `--types HTTP:High` filter. Splitting on whether levels were requested is the only option that is neither too strict nor unsound. NEEDS SIGN-OFF — this is the one deviation with a security-ish flavor. |
| `broker.rs` | Per-run state is private to each find()/grab()/serve() call; a single Broker supports concurrent runs. | Python's find() writes `self._countries`, `self._limit`, `self._checker` on the Broker (api.py:264-265, 252), so two overlapping find() calls corrupt each other's limit countdown and country filter, and both push into the same queue. Same family of bug as the Judge class-attribute problem (locked decision 10). |
| `broker.rs` | `grab()` is not `async`. | api.py:185 `async def grab` awaits nothing — it sets two fields and calls create_task. Marking it async in Rust would force a pointless `.await` on every caller. |
| `broker.rs` | `Stats` counts `Connection success/timeout/failed` from typed check outcomes rather than log-string matching, and the buckets are counters not `list[Proxy]`. | Python's buckets hold Proxy objects so `pprint(stat)` can dump them; that requires retaining every proxy. Anyone who wants the objects themselves has the stream. Output shape changes: 'Wrong country: 12' instead of a printed list of 12 repr'd proxies. Flagging because it is a visible CLI output change. |
| `proxybroker.rs` | `-ssl` (the argparse single-dash multi-char alias for --verify-ssl) is not offered. Only --verify-ssl works. | clap short flags are exactly one char; `-ssl` would parse as `-s -s -l`, and `-s`/`-l` are already --strict and --limit. argparse's single-dash-long-option is a Python-only quirk. Scripts using `-ssl` break. |
| `proxybroker.rs` | Broker options (--max-conn/--max-tries/--timeout/--judge/--provider/--provider-dir/--verify-ssl/--log/--geo-db) are accepted BEFORE or AFTER the subcommand. Python only accepts them before (except --provider-dir, which has a bespoke dual-dest hack for both). | clap `global = true`. Strictly a superset of Python's accepted inputs, and it deletes _add_provider_dir_arg's workaround entirely. No existing command line changes meaning. |
| `proxybroker.rs` | serve's `--max-tries` is renamed `--srv-max-tries` and is now actually honored (it sets the server's per-incoming-request retry count, falling back to --max-tries when unset). | BUG FIX. In Python the flag parses into dest=srv_max_tries and is then never read — cli.py:506-524 builds broker.serve()'s kwargs by hand and omits it, so api.py:serve's `kwargs.pop("max_tries", self._max_tries)` always takes the fallback. The documented flag is a no-op today. The rename is forced by the collision with the now-global --max-tries; wiring it up is the point. |
| `proxybroker.rs` | `--format` rejects unknown values (and requires a value). | Python's nargs="?" + no choices means `--format bogus` and bare `--format` both silently degrade to default format. Silent misconfiguration on an output-shape flag is worth an error. Scripts passing a bogus value now fail loudly. |
| `proxybroker.rs` | `--log` requires a value; CRITICAL maps to tracing's ERROR (not OFF); RUST_LOG overrides it when set. | Python's nargs="?" makes bare `--log` produce None, which basicConfig(level=None) silently ignores — a footgun with no defensible semantics. tracing has no CRITICAL level; mapping to ERROR means genuine error! events surface at the default level where Python suppressed them. RUST_LOG is new and free with EnvFilter. |
| `proxybroker.rs` | Log line format differs from Python's `%(asctime)s - %(levelname)s - %(name)s - %(message)s` / `[%H:%M:%S]`. | tracing_subscriber's default fmt carries the same fields in a different layout. Reproducing the exact string needs a custom FormatEvent impl for zero benefit — logs go to stderr and are not a parsed interface. Flagging because it is technically observable. |
| `proxybroker.rs` | `--countries` values are uppercased and rejected unless 2 ASCII letters. | BUG FIX. api.py:_geo_passed does `proxy.geo.code in self._countries` against uppercase ISO codes, so `-c us` silently matches nothing and the run yields zero proxies with no diagnostic. |
| `proxybroker.rs` | `--judge` / `--provider` values are parsed as URLs at argument-parse time; `--host` as IpAddr; `--port` as u16; serve's `--limit` constrained to >= 1. | Python accepts any string and fails later (or, for serve limit, raises ValueError from api.py:serve deep inside the call). Parse-time rejection with clap's error message is strictly better UX. Anything previously accepted-then-crashing now fails earlier. |
| `proxybroker.rs` | `--lvl` supplied without HTTP in `--types` emits a tracing warning (still ignored, not an error). | Python's cli.py:453 gates the merge on `"HTTP" in ns.types`, so --lvl is discarded in total silence. Warn rather than error to keep every currently-working command line working. |
| `proxybroker.rs` | `--format json` output ends with a trailing newline after `]`. | Python writes `\n]` with no trailing newline, leaving a file without a final newline. One byte, POSIX-friendly, does not affect JSON parsing. |
| `proxybroker.rs` | Exit codes: 0 on success, 1 on fatal error, 2 on no-subcommand and on update-geo. Python exits 0 for no-subcommand (prints help) and 1-with-traceback for update-geo. | clap's arg_required_else_help convention. Note: still exits 0 when the run completes having found ZERO proxies (parity — see open questions). |
| `proxybroker.rs` | `update-geo` is hidden, prints a DB-IP/--geo-db migration message, and exits 2 instead of raising RuntimeError. | The command has been permanently broken since 2019-12-30 (MaxMind endpoint retirement, upstream issue #200) and this port ships DB-IP, not GeoLite2 (locked decision 3). Kept only as a signpost. |
| `proxybroker.rs` | New flag `--geo-db PATH`, and `--version`/`--help` carry `IP Geolocation by DB-IP (https://db-ip.com)` under the geo-bundled feature. | Locked decision 3 (user-supplied db override) and the CC BY 4.0 attribution requirement for redistributing DB-IP Country Lite. No Python equivalent. |
| `proxybroker.rs` | Ctrl-C is handled in the CLI via tokio::select! on tokio::signal::ctrl_c(), not by a signal handler registered inside the Broker. | Python's Broker(stop_broker_on_sigint=True) installs loop.add_signal_handler(SIGINT, self.stop) from library code and no-ops on Windows (NotImplementedError). Locked decision 8 makes drop = cancel, so the CLI owns the signal and the library never touches global process state. |
| `proxybroker.rs` | `--show-stats` no longer prints the per-negotiator event/runtime log dump. | api.py:show_stats(verbose=True) reconstructs it by substring-matching free-text messages out of proxy.get_log() ('Location of proxy' in msgs, 'Connection: success' in msgs). That log-scraping does not survive the port; typed counters on Stats replace it. The headline numbers (working count, per-proto counts, error histogram with wire-compatible keys) are preserved. |
| `resolver.py, 558 LOC)` | IPv6 zone IDs are rejected. `parse_ip_literal("fe80::1%eth0")` → `None`; Python's `host_is_ip` returns True and `canonicalize_ip` preserves the zone (utils.py:69-85 documents this as intentional, and the bracketed-`[v6]:port` provider regex accepts `%zone`). | Rust's `Ipv6Addr` parser has no zone-ID support (no `Ipv6Addr` scope_id field in std), so supporting it means carrying a parallel string type through every IP-shaped API to serve link-local addresses — which cannot be a usable public proxy anyway. The cost is the whole `IpAddr`-as-canonical-form simplification. Recommend accepting; the blast radius is provider feeds emitting link-local entries, which we'd discard on connect regardless. NOTE: also constrains util.rs's `canonicalize_ip`/`get_all_ip` port — needs a joint call. |
| `resolver.py, 558 LOC)` | The legacy leading-zero IPv4 path accepts ASCII digits only. Python builds `".".join(f"{int(n)}" ...)`, and CPython's `int()` accepts surrounding whitespace, a leading `+`, and Unicode decimal digits — so `host_is_ip("1.2.3. 4")` and `host_is_ip("１.２.３.４")` both return True today. | Over-acceptance bug. Python returns True and then `proxy.py:103` stores the WEIRD ORIGINAL string as `self.host`, which then fails `get_ip_info` (ValueError → geo Unknown) and gets emitted verbatim in output. Rust strips ASCII `0` prefixes and parses; anything else is `None`. Fixing it costs nothing and the only inputs it rejects were already broken downstream. |
| `resolver.py, 558 LOC)` | `parse_ip_literal` returns the NORMALIZED address, and callers store that; Python's `host_is_ip` returns a bool and the caller keeps the raw literal. | Consequence of the previous item: `Proxy(host="127.0.0.001")` currently keeps `"127.0.0.001"` forever — it survives `socket.connect` (inet_aton reads it as octal, coincidentally correct here) but breaks the mmdb lookup and pollutes stdout/JSON. Returning `IpAddr` makes the normalization unavoidable. Affects proxy.rs's field type (`host: IpAddr`, not `String`). |
| `resolver.py, 558 LOC)` | The DNS cache is per-`Resolver` (hickory `ResponseCache`), not process-global; entries expire on DNS TTL and the cache is bounded by `cache_size`. | Python's `_cached_hosts` is a CLASS attribute: unbounded, never-expiring, and shared across every Broker in the process — the same global-mutable-state defect as `Judge.available`/`Judge.ev` that locked decision 10 already fixes. Two Brokers with different resolv.conf-visible views, or a run spanning a DNS change, currently see each other's stale entries forever. Requires api.rs to share one `Arc<Resolver>` so we don't lose cache hits. |
| `resolver.py, 558 LOC)` | Fixes resolver.py:468 — `return self._cached_hosts.get(host)`. When a lookup returns an empty answer, Python falls through to re-read the cache and returns whatever is there, INCLUDING an entry that `_cache_compatible` just rejected two lines earlier (438) for being the wrong family. | Real bug: a caller pinning `family=AF_INET` can be handed the cached IPv6 it was explicitly guarded against, whenever the fresh A query comes back empty. Deleting the cache deletes the bug. Recorded rather than reproduced. (Unreachable today only because no caller passes `family` — see dropped items.) |
| `resolver.py, 558 LOC)` | `resolve` returns `Err(ProxyError::Resolve)` on an empty answer. Python returns `None` (or a stale cache value) and only raises `ResolveError` for a DNS-level error/timeout. | The `None` return is a trap every caller falls into differently: `Proxy.create` (proxy.py:87-97) catches `ResolveError` but not `None`, so it constructs `Proxy(host=None)` → `host_is_ip(None)` → False → a misleading `ValueError('The host of proxy should be the IP address')` that masks the actual DNS miss. 'Resolved to nothing' and 'resolution failed' are the same event to every caller; one `Result` says so. |
| `resolver.py, 558 LOC)` | Resolve failure logs at `debug`, not `warning` (resolver.py:467 `log.warning(f"{host}: Could not resolve host")`). | The `logging=False` parameter exists only so the DNSBL path (checker.py:160), which fires N-domains × M-proxies queries whose EXPECTED outcome is NXDOMAIN, doesn't flood the log with warnings. That's a parameter compensating for a wrong level. Log at debug, drop the parameter, and let the callers that care (judge, proxy) log at their own level with their own context. |
| `resolver.py, 558 LOC)` | GeoIP lookup no longer happens inside the Proxy constructor (proxy.py:133 `self._geo = Resolver.get_ip_info(self.host)`); the Broker/Checker pipeline populates it from its own `Option<Arc<GeoDb>>` at the construction site. | A constructor that reaches into a process-global mmdb handle is exactly the global state we're deleting, and it forces every `Proxy` — including ones built in tests with no geo feature — to pay a lookup nobody asked for. Makes `geo` a genuinely optional feature. Costs a small change to proxy.rs's shape (`geo: GeoData`, defaulted to `unknown()`), so it needs sign-off from that module's owner too. |
| `resolver.py, 558 LOC)` | `GeoDb::lookup` takes `IpAddr`, not a string, so Python's `except ... ValueError` arm (resolver.py:106, catching an unparseable IP string) becomes unrepresentable. | Type-driven: by the time we have a proxy we have an `IpAddr`. `InvalidDatabaseError` → Unknown behavior is preserved. |
| `resolver.py, 558 LOC)` | Endpoint trial order is shuffled with `rand::rng()` (non-crypto), not a CSPRNG. | Python uses `secrets.choice` and the code comment states the reason outright: 'Built via secrets.choice per pick to clear SonarCloud S2245.' It's load-balancing across public ext-IP services. Trivially reversible if someone wants `rand::rngs::OsRng`. |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | Pool ranks by (error_rate, avg_resp_time); Python ranks by avg_resp_time alone. | server.py:127 pushes `(proxy.avg_resp_time, proxy)` while `Proxy.priority` (proxy.py:207-208) returns `(error_rate, avg_resp_time)` and is called by nothing. The serve() docstring (api.py:280-282) and the brief both promise 'based on the percentage of errors and average response time'. Code and documentation disagree; the documentation and the dead `priority` property agree with each other. I read this as an unfinished refactor and implement the documented behavior. EFFECT: a fast-but-flaky proxy is now ranked below a slightly slower reliable one. Needs sign-off — it changes which proxy real traffic lands on. |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | Ranking key is a total order over (error_rate_x100, avg_resp_ms, host, port); ties never panic. | `heapq.heappush(self._pool, (avg_resp_time, proxy))` compares the second tuple element when the first ties, and `Proxy` defines no __lt__ -> TypeError. avg_resp_time is `round(..., 2)` (proxy.py:244), so ties are not exotic — two proxies at 0.12s collide. This is a live crash in the Python. Rust's key is integral and totally ordered, so there is no fallback comparison to reach. |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | get() filters newcomers by scheme. Python does a bare newcomers.pop(0). | server.py:63-64 returns a newcomer without checking `scheme in proxy.schemes`, even though every other path checks. _import (server.py:101) actively feeds wrong-scheme proxies into newcomers via put(). The returned proxy then reaches _choice_proto, which raises RuntimeError — a type _handle does not catch — escaping to the done-callback. This is a correctness bug with a crash attached, and it is the only known route to that RuntimeError. |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | A retry always uses a different proxy than the attempt that just failed. | Python's `finally` block put()s the failed proxy back BEFORE the next `get()`, so with exactly one eligible newcomer the loop hands the same broken proxy back up to max_tries times — burning all three attempts on one dead host. api.py:302-303 documents the intent: 'Attempts can be made with different proxies.' Rust holds tried proxies in a Vec and put()s them all after the loop ends. Small deviation, cheap, matches documented intent. |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | `history` is per-Server instance state, not a module global. | Same class of bug as locked decision 10 (Judge.available/ev). Two Brokers in one process share one TTLCache today, so Server A can answer /api/history with a proxy from Server B's pool. The key includes the peer IP but not the server identity. |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | The /api/history 200 response emits a correct Content-Length. | server.py:351 is `client_writer.write(f"Content-Length: {str(len(...) + 2).encode()}\r\n")` — the `.encode()` is INSIDE the f-string, so it interpolates the repr and would emit `Content-Length: b'25'`. Worse, the f-string produces a `str` and StreamWriter.write() requires bytes-like, so the line raises TypeError. The entire 200-with-a-hit branch of the history endpoint is dead code that has never executed successfully. Rust builds a typed Response and hyper computes the length. Flagging because 'we fixed an endpoint that never worked' is a behavior change even if nobody could have depended on it. |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | X-Proxy-Info is injected only into real HTTP responses and the synthesized CONNECT 200 — never into tunnel bytes. | server.py:407 passes `scheme=scheme, inject=...` to the proxy->client _stream unconditionally, so for HTTPS-over-SOCKS the first chunk is raw TLS and _inject_headers splits it on b'\r\n' and splices a header line in. Either it finds no \r\n and raises ValueError (uncaught by _stream's except list -> escapes _handle -> done-callback), or it finds one by chance inside a TLS record and silently corrupts the handshake. Header injection into an opaque byte tunnel is not a thing that can be made to work. |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | The CONNECT:80 path tunnels to the port the client actually asked for; Python hardcodes 80. | Connect80Ngtr does `_CONNECT_request(kwargs.get('host'), 80)` (negotiators.py:176), discarding the `port` kwarg that _handle carefully computed at server.py:375. A client requesting http://example.com:8080/ through a CONNECT:80-typed proxy gets port 80's content back with no error. Note the counter-argument for sign-off: the type name 'CONNECT:80' means 'CONNECT to :80 was verified working', so honoring an arbitrary port uses the proxy beyond what the checker proved. I still think returning the right resource beats returning the wrong one silently. |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | Requests sent through a SOCKS/CONNECT tunnel use origin-form request-targets; Python forwards the client's absolute-form bytes verbatim. | Python relays the raw request unchanged (server.py:386), so an origin server behind a SOCKS tunnel receives `GET http://host/path HTTP/1.1`. RFC 9112 §3.2.1 requires origin-form to an origin server (servers SHOULD accept absolute-form, so this mostly works today). With hyper I set the URI explicitly, and absolute-form is a deliberate choice for the HTTP-proto path only. Low risk; flagged because a strict origin server could respond differently. |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | avg_resp_time records time-to-first-response-byte, not total relay duration. | server.py:397 sets `stime` before the bidirectional relay and server.py:444 logs it after the relay completes, so proxy.py:334 appends the WHOLE session duration to _runtimes. A 5-minute download makes avg_resp_time 300s and the pool evicts a perfectly good proxy for exceeding max_resp_time=8. The recorded number also includes the client's own think time, which the proxy cannot control. TTFB is what 'response time' means everywhere else in this codebase (it is what the checker measures). THIS IS THE DEVIATION MOST WORTH ARGUING ABOUT: it changes eviction behavior for every user, and anyone who tuned --max-resp-time against the current semantics will see different proxies survive. |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | NoProxy shuts the server down via the cancellation token; it does not stop the runtime. | server.py:296-298 does `if isinstance(exc, NoProxyError): self.stop()` and stop() calls `self._loop.stop()`. The shutdown intent is preserved (no proxies left = nothing to serve); killing the caller's executor is not. In-flight connections drain instead of being severed mid-byte. |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | Exhausting max_tries returns 502 Bad Gateway; a DNS failure returns 502; an import timeout returns 504. | Python falls off the end of the retry loop and returns from _handle with no response written at all — the client sees a bare connection close and cannot distinguish 'proxy broker gave up' from 'network died'. The ResolveError path (server.py:378-379) does a bare `return` for the same silent close. hyper's service signature forces a Response, which is the right forcing function: a resolution failure is not the proxy's fault and the client deserves to know. |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | Malformed / unknown proxycontrol requests get 400 or 404 instead of falling through to the proxy path. | server.py:321 `_api, _operation, _params = headers['Path'].split('/', 5)[3:]` raises ValueError on any path with too few segments (uncaught -> done-callback). And an unrecognized _api, _operation, or query_type simply falls out of the if-chain into the normal relay loop, which then tries to proxy `http://proxycontrol/...` to a real upstream proxy and burns max_tries on it. Both become explicit status codes. |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | Checker backpressure is 'bounded channel is full', not 'the queue has been fully drained'. | The Python pause is api.py:480-483: once limit is exhausted, checking blocks on `await self._proxies.join()`, which returns only when EVERY queued proxy has been imported and task_done()'d — drain-to-zero hysteresis. A bounded mpsc (locked decision 8) resumes the checker as soon as ONE slot frees. Result: the checker wakes more often and in smaller bursts rather than in one batch after a full drain. Same steady-state throughput, different burst shape. The channel capacity that best approximates `serve(limit=N)` is an open question below. |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | Request bodies are not truncated at 64 KB. | Consequence of dropping _parse_request. Python reads one 65536-byte chunk (twice for POST) and forwards exactly that; a larger upload is silently cut. Listed separately because it is a user-visible behavior change (large POSTs through the local server start working) rather than a pure refactor. |
| `*.rs)` | proto for the proxyscrape SOCKS4 and SOCKS5 providers is [SOCKS4] / [SOCKS5]; in Python it is the STRING "SOCKS4" / "SOCKS5". | providers.py:706 and :710 write `proto=("SOCKS4")` and `proto=("SOCKS5")` — missing trailing commas, so these are strs, not 1-tuples. Consequences, both real: (1) Proxy.__init__ does `set(types) & {…}` -> set("SOCKS4") = {'S','O','C','K','4'}, intersection empty, so these proxies get NO expected types; (2) api.py:_grab filters on `pr.proto & types.keys()`, which iterates the string char-by-char and yields an empty intersection, so both providers are SILENTLY EXCLUDED from every `find(types=...)` call. That is 534 + 2084 = 2618 measured live proxies — the two highest-yield SOCKS sources in the whole registry — that the Python has never delivered to a filtered find. `proto: Vec<Proto>` makes the mistake unrepresentable. Needs sign-off because it materially changes SOCKS result volume. |
| `*.rs)` | Gatherproxy_com fetches both the 'anonymous' and the 'elite' page sets; Python fetches only 'elite' (plus one throwaway 'anonymous' probe). | providers.py:384 assigns `urls = [...]` inside the `for t in ['anonymous','elite']` loop instead of extending it, so iteration 2 discards iteration 1's URL list. The `urls = []` initializer at :377 is the tell that extend was intended. Rust extends. Roughly doubles this provider's yield — if gatherproxy.com is alive at all (see open_questions). |
| `*.rs)` | Parse::Regex patterns cannot use lookaround; the built-in ip:port pairing is a hand-written scanner, not a regex. | The `regex` crate has no lookahead by design (linear-time guarantee). utils.py's IPPortPatternGlobal and the Gatherproxy/Nntime/rosinstrument `_pattern`s all depend on `(?=.*?(…\|…))` with DOTALL. `parse::pair_hosts_with_ports` reproduces the semantics exactly (each host takes the first port token before the next host token) with two lookaround-free regexes. This is behavior-preserving for every bundled provider, but it is a USER-VISIBLE contract change: a user porting a Python `pattern:` that used lookaround gets a load-time regex error. Rejected fancy-regex — it would buy back lookaround at the cost of backtracking (ReDoS on a 5 MB scraped page) for zero bundled providers. Document the restriction in data/providers.yaml's header comment. |
| `*.rs)` | A provider config FILE contains a list of providers (`providers: [...]`); Python's ConfigurableProvider.from_config takes exactly one provider per file. | The bundled registry must be one file, and the bundled format and the user format must be the same format or they will drift. One-provider-per-file also makes `--provider-dir` a directory of 30 near-empty files. Migration is mechanical (wrap in a list) and the port has no installed base. Consequence: Registry::load_file returns a Registry, not a Provider. |
| `*.rs)` | Page-URL templates use `{page}`, not Python's bare `{}`. | PaginatedProvider._build_page_url uses `str.format` with `{}`. In YAML, `url: http://x/p?n={}` needs quoting to avoid the flow-mapping parse, and `{}` gives no error when someone writes two of them. `{page}` is self-documenting and quote-free. Same three substitution rules otherwise (placeholder / replace-existing-param / append-param). |
| `*.rs)` | fetch_page retries only on error; Python retries whenever the response body is falsy, including a successful 200 with an empty body. | providers.py:129-133 loops `if page: break`, so an empty-but-valid page costs 3 requests to 3 different sources of nothing. Rust: Err -> retry, Ok("") -> a successful empty page. Also fixes Python's UnboundLocalError when max_tries=0 (`page` is never bound before `return page`). |
| `*.rs)` | One shared reqwest::Client across all providers instead of a fresh aiohttp.ClientSession per provider per grab cycle. | providers.py:88 constructs a new session inside get_proxies, so serve mode (which re-grabs every GRAB_PAUSE seconds) discards the connection pool and re-does TLS for every provider every cycle. Purely an efficiency deviation with no observable semantic change now that the cookie jar is dropped. |
| `*.rs)` | Port is parsed to u16 at the provider boundary; unparseable or >65535 ports are dropped with a log. | Python carries port as a str all the way to Proxy.__init__'s `int(port)` / `> 65535` ValueError, i.e. a provider parsing bug surfaces as an exception in the checker, one proxy at a time, far from its cause. Typed at the boundary, attributed to the provider that emitted it. Net effect on results is nil (those entries could never become working proxies), but the counts and the logs move. |
| `*.rs)` | The JS char table (Xseo_in / Nntime_com charEqNum) is rebuilt per page instead of persisting on the instance/class. | Both classes declare `charEqNum = {}` at CLASS level and mutate it via `self.charEqNum = {...}` (Xseo/Nntime rebind, so they escape the shared-mutable-class-attr trap; Spys_ru does `self.charEqNum[char] = ...` and does NOT, so its table leaks across pages AND across every Spys_ru instance in the process). The table is a property of one page's JS. Same class of global-mutable-state bug as decision 10's Judge.available/Judge.ev. |
| `*.rs)` | APIProvider's proxy_path: a missing path segment yields zero seeds + a warning; Python silently keeps the parent object and keeps walking. | provider_utils.py:394 is `data = data.get(key, data)`. A typo'd `proxy_path: data.proxys` therefore falls back to scraping the entire JSON document with the generic extractor and looks like it worked. A path that doesn't resolve is a config bug and should say so. |

## Dropped — not carried over

| Module | What | Why |
|---|---|---|
| `error.rs` | errors.py:4 `class ProxyError(Exception): pass` — the base class itself | Never raised, never caught bare. Its only job was to make `issubclass(ProxyConnError, ProxyError)` true, which nothing in the library depends on (only tests/test_public_contracts.py:318 asserts it). One flat enum, no hierarchy. NOTE: the Rust type named `ProxyError` is NOT this class — see deviations. |
| `error.rs` | The reflective `err.errmsg` access pattern (proxy.py:333 reads the attribute off a class OBJECT, since call sites pass `err=BadStatusError` — the class, not an instance — at checker.py:297/301 and negotiators.py:80/150/180) | Rust has no class objects. `as_str(&self)` on a value. This also collapses Python's accidental two calling conventions (`err=SomeClass` at checker.py:297 vs `err=ProxyConnError(msg)` at proxy.py:391) into one — both worked in Python only because the attribute lives on the class. |
| `error.rs` | ProxyRecvError / ProxySendError as distinct types | Identical errmsg means they were already one bucket; no call site discriminates them. Merged into ProxyError::Reset (deviation recorded). |
| `error.rs` | BadStatusError's use in providers.py:150 (`raise BadStatusError(f"Status: {resp.status}")`) | Caught four lines later at providers.py:153 in the same function, converted to `page = ""`, never counted, never seen. It is a `goto` written as an exception. Provider scraping is reqwest-land (locked decision 4) and a provider is not a proxy — reusing the proxy taxonomy for it is a category error. Provider fetch returns `Option<String>` and logs; no error type crosses the boundary. |
| `error.rs` | `Error::NoProviders` and `Error::NoJudges` as sketched in research.md:909-910 | No Python grounding. checker.py:106-123 does NOT error when a judge pool is empty — it appends to `nojudges`, disables the affected protocols (`self._req_http_proto = False`, removes negotiators from `self._ngtrs`) and sets the event so waiters unblock. Graceful degradation, not a fatal. Inventing these variants would be exactly the speculative abstraction the brief forbids. Raised in open_questions instead. |
| `error.rs` | Wrapping/chaining a cause inside ProxyError (Python's `raise err from e`, `ErrorOnStream(e)`) | A `Copy + Hash` histogram key cannot own a `Box<dyn Error>`. Python's chained cause is only ever consumed by `log.debug(f"...{e!r}")` and by the `repr` string-match at server.py:433. Both are replaced: the former by `tracing::debug!` at the raise site (where the OS error is still in hand), the latter by a typed field on server::StreamFailure. |
| `error.rs` | User-extensible error classes (subclassing ProxyError with a new errmsg) | Closed set of 9 per-proxy failure modes. Locked decision 6 already establishes users extend PROVIDERS, never the check machinery. `#[non_exhaustive]` keeps additive room for us without offering an extension point nobody uses. |
| `negotiator.rs` | BaseNegotiator ABC, per-proxy negotiator instantiation, and the `self._proxy` back-reference (incl. `Proxy.ngtr` property/setter's `NGTRS[proto](self)`) | Locked decision 6. The class hierarchy exists only to attach a name + two bools + one method to a closed set of 6; the instance state is a single back-pointer used for I/O and logging. Enum + free fn + by-value Stream removes the object graph, the allocation, and the aliasing between Proxy and its negotiator. `Proxy._ngtr` becomes `Option<NegotiatorKind>` (Copy). |
| `negotiator.rs` | `**kwargs` extra-headers on `_CONNECT_request` (`kwargs.setdefault('User-Agent', ...)` + the `headers` join) | Dead. Verified both call sites project-wide: `_CONNECT_request(host, 80\|25\|443)` — no caller ever passes an extra header, so the loop always emits exactly one UA line. Hardcode the UA; if a header ever needs adding it is a one-line edit, not a parameter. |
| `negotiator.rs` | The `port` kwarg on Socks4Ngtr.negotiate / Socks5Ngtr.negotiate (`kwargs.get('port', 80)`) | Dead default. checker.py's only call is `negotiate(host=judge.host, ip=judge.ip)`, so SOCKS always targets port 80. Folded into `NegotiatorKind::target_port()` next to the CONNECT ports, which were already hardcoded at the call site. No behavior change; one source of truth instead of two. |
| `negotiator.rs` | `if not isinstance(resp, (bytes, str)): raise TypeError(...)` (Socks5Ngtr) and utils.get_status_code's identical guard | Dynamic-typing self-defense against a case the type system makes unrepresentable. `read_exact` yields `[u8]` or an io::Error, full stop. |
| `negotiator.rs` | `if isinstance(resp, asyncio.Future): resp = await resp` + `assert not isinstance(resp, asyncio.Future)` (Socks4Ngtr lines 158-160) | Cargo-cult dead code. `proxy.recv` is an `async def` that returns bytes; it cannot return a Future. Two lines and an assert defending against nothing. |
| `negotiator.rs` | Hand-rolled SOCKS5 wire code: greeting pack, 2-byte method reply, ipaddress-based ATYP dispatch, request pack, 4-byte reply header, rep_atyp length dispatch (0x01/0x03/0x04), BND.ADDR+BND.PORT drain | Locked decision 5: tokio-socks 0.5.3 does all of it and maps the 23 reply codes 1:1 to error variants (research.md, verified against docs.rs). Hand-rolling buys nothing but a place for an off-by-one to live — and Python already has one there (see deviations: IndexError on a short read). |
| `negotiator.rs` | Hand-rolled SOCKS4 wire code: `struct.pack('>2BH5B', 4, 1, port, *inet_aton(ip), 0)` + 8-byte reply check | Same reason. `Socks4Stream::connect_with_socket` + `into_inner()`. |
| `negotiator.rs` | The distinct log strings 'Failed (auth is required)' vs 'Failed (invalid data)' in Socks5Ngtr | Both raise the identical `BadResponseError` — the distinction never reaches the user's stats, only a debug line. tokio-socks' `NoAcceptableAuthMethods` variant carries the same information with more precision, retained as the error `#[source]`. |
| `negotiator.rs` | `_CONNECT_request`'s caller-supplied-bracket stripping (`if host_str.startswith('[') and host_str.endswith(']')`) | Defends against a caller passing an already-bracketed netloc from `urlparse(...).netloc`. In Rust the only caller is checker.rs with `Target.host` sourced from judge.rs, which parses the URL into an unbracketed host (locked: judge.rs owns URL parsing). Re-adding brackets at format time when the host parses as `Ipv6Addr` covers the real requirement. If judge.rs ever hands over a bracketed host that is a judge.rs bug, not something to paper over here. |
| `negotiator.rs` | `proxy.log(...)` calls and `stat['errors'][err.errmsg] += 1` side effects inside every negotiator | Negotiators become pure protocol. The caller has the error (typed) and the Proxy (owned) and does both — one place instead of six. Also removes the negotiator's need for a `&mut Proxy`, which is what forces the back-reference in the first place. |
| `negotiator.rs` | utils.get_status_code's 400 sentinel on unparseable input | An internal artifact: 400 is returned only so the caller's `!= 200` comparison fires. `Option<u16>` says the same thing honestly; both call sites already treat it as failure. |
| `negotiator.rs` | The `_reader`/`_writer` two-slot dicts + `reader`/`writer` 'ssl-or-conn' properties + `Proxy.close()`'s ordered writer teardown | Replaced by `enum Stream` + `Drop`. The dicts can represent states that cannot exist (both slots live, ssl-without-conn); the enum cannot. |
| `proxy.rs` | _format_host_port(host, port) | SocketAddr's Display already does RFC 3986 v6 bracketing. Storing SocketAddr instead of (str, int) deletes the helper and its three call sites, and makes every future format string correct without remembering the helper exists. |
| `proxy.rs` | Proxy.priority property (`(error_rate, avg_resp_time)`) | Dead. Grepped every call site: server.py:71/148's `priority, proxy = heapq.heappop(...)` is a tuple unpack of a locally-built `(avg_resp_time, proxy)` pair (server.py:127), not a read of this property. Nothing reads Proxy.priority. |
| `proxy.rs` | Proxy.avgRespTime property | Deprecated since 2.0, emits a DeprecationWarning, aliases avg_resp_time. A new crate has no back-compat surface to carry. Deletes the `warnings` import too. |
| `proxy.rs` | Proxy._schemes cache + the schemes property's tuple | Caches six enum comparisons behind an invalidation hook in the types setter. supports_scheme(Scheme) computes it and returns the boolean every caller actually wanted. |
| `proxy.rs` | types setter (whole-dict assignment + isinstance/TypeError check) | A runtime type check that the compiler now does. No production caller assigns the whole dict; the two real mutations are set_type/remove_type. |
| `proxy.rs` | Proxy.reader / Proxy.writer properties, Proxy._reader / Proxy._writer dicts, Proxy._closed | `self._writer.get('ssl') or self._writer.get('conn')` is a hand-rolled sum type made of two dicts. Replaced by one `Stream` enum field. `_closed` is replaced by ProxyConn's existence (Drop = closed). |
| `proxy.rs` | Proxy.ngtr property + setter (`self._ngtr = NGTRS[proto](self)`) | This IS the reference cycle (Proxy -> negotiator -> Proxy) that the brief calls out. The setter's only jobs are (a) picking a class from a dict — now `NegotiatorKind` (locked #6) — and (b) tagging log lines with `ngtr.name` — now a field on ProxyConn. Negotiators are zero-sized and take `&mut ProxyConn`. |
| `proxy.rs` | Proxy.close() | Drop. Removes `finally: proxy.close()` from both checker retry loops and makes the leak-on-early-return impossible rather than merely avoided. |
| `proxy.rs` | _make_unverified_ssl_context_for_proxy_testing() | Not proxy.rs's concern; the TLS config moves into ConnectOpts, built once in checker.rs/tls.rs. Per research.md, the rustls form is a custom ServerCertVerifier that always returns Ok but CAPTURES the presented chain — strictly better than Python's blanket CERT_NONE, since a MITM-ing proxy becomes a detectable quality signal instead of silently accepted. (No semgrep/NOSONAR/nosec/noqa suppression comment stack needed either — five suppressions on one 6-line function.) |
| `proxy.rs` | Proxy._recv's Content-Length / chunked / at_eof body loop | A hand-rolled HTTP/1.1 response parser that exists only because Python hand-rolls the whole stack. Locked #4 puts the judge request on hyper, which parses the response correctly (including chunked) for free. Negotiation needs only recv_exact(n) and recv_head — kept. This also drops proxy.rs's dependency on utils.parse_headers. |
| `proxy.rs` | Proxy.recv(length=0, head_only=False) unified signature | Three modes behind two flags where no caller passes both. Split into recv_exact(len) and recv_head(); the third mode (full body) is the dropped one above. |
| `proxy.rs` | Proxy.as_text() | `f'{host}:{port}\n'` — a Display plus a newline the caller supplies. `writeln!(out, "{}", p.addr())` at cli.rs's one call site (cli.py:400). |
| `proxy.rs` | the `order(tp_lvl) = (len(tp_lvl[0]), tp_lvl[0][-1])` sort closure (defined twice: __repr__ and as_json) | Sorting an enum by the length and last character of its stringified name. Derived Ord with the variants declared in that order + BTreeMap gives identical output, once, structurally. |
| `proxy.rs` | `loop` kwarg threading (create(loop=...), Resolver(loop=loop)) | tokio has no loop to pass. |
| `proxy.rs` | the `set(types) & {'HTTP', 'HTTPS', ...}` silent filter in __init__ | Defends against unknown protocol strings reaching the constructor. `ProxyType: FromStr` rejects them at the CLI/config boundary with a message, instead of silently dropping them here where nobody sees it. |
| `judge.rs` | The three per-scheme readiness Events (Judge.ev) and their fine-grained "first HTTP judge verified → unblock HTTP checks" semantics | One OnceCell gates the whole JudgeSet. The fine grain buys at most (judge_timeout − first_judge_latency) ≈ a few seconds, ONCE per run, and JudgePool::warm already overlaps that window with provider scraping. Cost of keeping it: 3 sync primitives, 3 conditional waits, the `_req_*_proto` bool triple, and the set-the-event-for-the-empty-scheme unblock hack. Listed as a deviation too — it is a (small) behavior change. |
| `judge.rs` | Dead default judges: http://www.proxyfire.net/fastenv, https://www.proxy-listen.de/azenv.php, http://www.proxy-listen.de/azenv.php, http://ip.spys.ru/ | MEASURED 2026-07-15: proxyfire.net/fastenv — connection fails outright (curl exit, no HTTP status). proxy-listen.de — https returns 503, http returns 301→https which 503s. ip.spys.ru — http returns 301→https, and https returns 403; since Judge.check sets allow_redirects=False, a 301 can never pass the `status == 200` gate, so both entries were already unusable as configured. Same rule as decision 7: do not port dead endpoints. |
| `judge.rs` | The `real_ext_ip` (singular) parameter, the `isinstance(real_ext_ips, str)` defensive coercion, and the `frozenset(real_ext_ips or ())` normalisation (judge.py:73-92) | Three layers of Python back-compat scaffolding for one upstream API migration. Rust takes `&HashSet<IpAddr>` — a single string is not a set of IpAddr, so the whole class of "iterated a str into individual characters" bugs is a type error. No external Python callers to keep compatible in a fresh crate. |
| `judge.rs` | `canonicalize_ip(ip) or ip` normalisation of the real-ext-IP set (judge.py:134) | Textual canonicalisation only exists because Python passes IPs as strings. `IpAddr` is already canonical and `Eq`, so the whole real_canonicals/page_ips canonicalisation step is `real_ext_ips.intersection(&get_all_ip(body))`. The `or ip` fallback (keep the raw string if it fails to parse) becomes unrepresentable. |
| `judge.rs` | get_judges accepting a heterogeneous list of `str` OR pre-built `Judge` objects (judge.py:167) | The Judge-object branch exists only so a caller can hand-tune a judge before passing it — and get_judges immediately overwrites the only two tunable fields (timeout, verify_ssl) anyway, so it was already a no-op path. JudgeConfig takes URLs. |
| `judge.rs` | Per-Judge `_loop` / `loop=` plumbing and the per-Judge `Resolver()` instance (judge.py:32-37) | No explicit loop in tokio; one shared Resolver in JudgePool. Python's per-judge Resolver was itself pointless — its cache (`Resolver._cached_hosts`) is a class attribute, so ten Resolver objects shared one cache anyway. |
| `judge.rs` | `aiohttp.TCPConnector(force_close=True)` | Each judge is probed once per process. Connection reuse is irrelevant, and forcing pool-less behavior in reqwest costs a builder knob for no observable effect. |
| `judge.rs` | The `# TODO: need refactoring` markers (judge.py:82, checker.py:91) | This map is the refactor. |
| `checker.rs` | checker.py:ProxyChecker (deprecated subclass emitting DeprecationWarning) | A pre-1.0 Python alias. A fresh Rust crate has no deprecated surface to keep. |
| `checker.rs` | checker.py:Checker.__init__ `real_ext_ip` (singular) param + `self._real_ext_ip` accessor + the `isinstance(real_ext_ips, str)` defense (lines 51-71), and the mirrored normalization in _get_anonymity_lvl (lines 361-367) | ~20 lines of runtime type-sniffing that exist only because Python cannot distinguish `str` from `Iterable[str]`. `HashSet<IpAddr>` makes every one of those states unrepresentable. The comment 'Backward-compat: legacy real_ext_ip is accepted' has no meaning for a new crate. |
| `checker.rs` | checker.py:Checker.__init__ `loop=None` param and the `asyncio.get_running_loop()`/RuntimeError dance | tokio has no explicit loop handle to thread through. |
| `checker.rs` | judge.py:Judge.clear() and the `Judge.available`/`Judge.ev` class attributes | Locked #10. `clear()` is pure damage control for global mutable state; instance ownership deletes both the state and the cleanup. |
| `checker.rs` | checker.py:Checker._req_http_proto / _req_https_proto / _req_smtp_proto and the three `await Judge.ev[...].wait()` calls in check() | They exist only to gate proxy checks behind a concurrently-running check_judges task. Folding judge probing into the async constructor makes 'judges before checks' a construction-order fact, so the flags and events have nothing left to synchronize. |
| `checker.rs` | checker.py:_decompress_content's chunked-body reassembly (`content.split(b'\r\n')[1::2]`) and the `Transfer-Encoding: chunked` sniff | hyper de-chunks the body before we see it. Python hand-rolls this because proxy.py:_recv is a hand-rolled HTTP reader. |
| `checker.rs` | utils.py:get_status_code / parse_headers / parse_status_line as used by the checker path | hyper parses the status line and headers. `int(resp[9:12])` with a magic offset and a 400 fallback is a reimplementation of an HTTP parser we now have. |
| `checker.rs` | proxy.py:Proxy.connect/close/send/recv/_recv, Proxy._reader/_writer/_closed/_ssl_context, and `proxy.ngtr` as mutable state | The socket moves out of Proxy into a checker-local value per attempt. `Proxy` crosses the ProxyStream boundary to users (locked #8) and must be plain data. `proxy.ngtr = proto` then `proxy.ngtr.negotiate(...)` is an implicit-argument trick for the logger; Rust passes NegotiatorKind explicitly. |
| `checker.rs` | checker.py:_request's unconditional `hdrs['Content-Length'] = len(data)` on GET | http-body-util sets it from the body. Python only sets it because the request is a hand-formatted string. |
| `checker.rs` | checker.py:_check_test_response's two `get_headers()` calls to read the constant Referer/Cookie | Each call draws a fresh CSPRNG rv it immediately discards. Two consts in utils.rs. |
| `checker.rs` | checker.py:Checker._types_passed's `if not self._types: return True` early return | CheckerBuilder::new requires types; api.py already errors on empty. Unreachable state. |
| `broker.rs` | The `queue=None` constructor param and all out-of-band delivery (api.py:82 `self._proxies = queue or asyncio.Queue()`; cli.py:473-475 passes its own) | Locked decision 8. `find()` returns the stream; the caller never supplies the channel. This also deletes the class of bug where two Brokers share one queue and each pushes its own None sentinel, terminating the other's consumer early. |
| `broker.rs` | The `None` poison pill (api.py:522 `self._push_to_result(None)`) and the consumer-side `if proxy is None: break` | Locked decision 8: termination is dropping the Sender. Also fixes a real Python bug — `_done()` pushes None AND decrements `_limit` through `_push_to_result`, so a `_done()` triggered by the limit re-enters `_update_limit`; two sentinels can hit the queue. Dropping a Sender is idempotent. |
| `broker.rs` | `Broker.stop()` (500-514), `_done()` (516-523), `self._all_tasks` (88), and the `task.cancel()` loop | `JoinSet` inside `ProxyStream` aborts every worker on Drop. Manual task bookkeeping is exactly what JoinSet is. `ServerHandle::shutdown()` covers the serve() half. |
| `broker.rs` | `stop_broker_on_sigint=True`, `loop.add_signal_handler(SIGINT, self.stop)`, `_signal_handler_registered`, `remove_signal_handler` (77, 119-126, 507-513) | A library must not install process-wide signal handlers. Ctrl-C is the binary's business: `tokio::select! { _ = signal::ctrl_c() => break, p = stream.next() => ... }` in main.rs, and dropping the stream cancels. The NotImplementedError-on-Windows workaround evaporates with it. |
| `broker.rs` | `loop=None` param and `_resolve_loop` (81, 128-135) | Tokio has no explicit loop object to thread through; tasks bind to the ambient runtime. ~8 lines and a class of 'no running event loop, will be set later' latent None-deref. |
| `broker.rs` | `_resolve_deprecated_limits` (137-166): the `max_concurrent_conn` and `attempts_conn` kwargs, including `max_concurrent_conn._value` reaching into a Semaphore's private field | Deprecated since 0.2.0 (~2018). A new crate at 0.1.0 has no back-compat surface to keep. `**kwargs` disappears entirely, so a misspelled option is a compile error instead of a silent no-op. |
