| `broker.rs` | `show_stats(verbose=True)`'s per-negotiator event dump (api.py:584-597) and its dependency on `Proxy.get_log()` | It reconstructs a timeline by grouping human-readable log strings by negotiator and printing runtimes. That is what `tracing` spans do, better and structured: `RUST_LOG=proxybroker=debug`. Keeping it would force `Proxy` to retain an unbounded `Vec<(ngtr, msg, runtime)>` per proxy purely for a debug printout. |
| `broker.rs` | `show_stats`'s log-string-matching classification (`"Location of proxy" in msgs`, `"Connection: success" in msgs`, `"Protocol or the level" in msgs`) | Replaced by typed counters in `Stats`, incremented at the decision site. The Python approach means an innocuous log-message edit silently zeroes a stats bucket, and it cannot classify a proxy that never got a log line. |
| `broker.rs` | `data` as `io.TextIOWrapper` or `list` (api.py:379-397) | `Query::data(String)`. Reading stdin/a file is the CLI's job (cli.py already does exactly this with ExitStack); a library taking a file handle to call `.read()` on it buys nothing and drags `Read` bounds through the API. |
| `broker.rs` | `unique_proxies: dict[(host,port) -> Proxy]` retaining every Proxy object | Kept only so show_stats can walk them post-run. It is an unbounded leak on `serve()`, which grabs forever every 180s. Dedup needs a `HashSet<(IpAddr, u16)>`; stats need counters. |
| `broker.rs` | `api.py`'s reliance on `Judge.ev["HTTP"].wait()` / `Judge.available` class state (checker.py:106-121, 173-177) to synchronize find() against check_judges() | Locked decision 10 makes judges Checker-instance state; find() awaits `check_judges()` before returning the stream, so there is nothing to wait for. Deletes three global asyncio.Events, the `Judge.clear()` call, and the multi-Broker cross-talk bug. |
| `broker.rs` | `ProxyChecker` (checker.py:383-390) — not broker.rs's symbol, but it is reachable through Broker's public surface | Deprecated alias emitting a DeprecationWarning since 0.2.0. Nothing to port. |
| `proxybroker.rs` | utils.py:update_geoip_db() — the MaxMind GeoLite2 downloader | Permanently broken since 2019-12-30; already just `raise RuntimeError` in Python. We ship DB-IP Country Lite bundled (geo-bundled feature) and expose --geo-db for refresh, so there is nothing to download. Not reimplemented against DB-IP's monthly URL either — see open questions. |
| `proxybroker.rs` | cli.py:11-12 `if sys.platform == "win32": asyncio.set_event_loop_policy(WindowsSelectorEventLoopPolicy())` | An asyncio-selector-vs-proactor Python bug workaround. Tokio has no analogue. |
| `proxybroker.rs` | cli.py:_add_provider_dir_arg + the _provider_dirs_top / provider_dirs dual-dest merge in _resolve_provider_dirs | Pure argparse workaround: a repeated option on both parent and subparser makes the subparser's action="append" clobber the parent's. clap `global = true` gives one Vec. The merge logic and its 14-line explanatory comment both vanish. |
| `proxybroker.rs` | cli.py:add_help_arg and every `add_help=False` on parser/subparsers | clap derives -h/--help. Python disabled the default help only so it could re-add it inside a named argument group; clap's next_help_heading does that without the dance. |
| `proxybroker.rs` | contextlib.ExitStack (cli.py:457) | Drop closes files. Nothing to stack. |
| `proxybroker.rs` | cli.py:handle's `proxy is None` sentinel loop and the `asyncio.Queue` passed into Broker(queue=...) | Locked decision 8: Broker::find returns a ProxyStream and termination is sender-drop. The CLI does not construct or own a channel. |
| `proxybroker.rs` | `asyncio.gather(*tasks)` / the tasks list / loop.run_until_complete / loop.run_forever | The CLI had to co-schedule the consumer coroutine with broker.find(). With a Stream, the consumer IS the caller's loop. |
| `proxybroker.rs` | The tuple-smuggling in cli.py:453-455 (`ns.types.append(("HTTP", ns.anon_lvl))`) and its counterpart api.py:_update_types | Existed only because `types` had to be one Python list carrying two different shapes. Query has two typed fields. |
| `proxybroker.rs` | show_stats' deprecated `full=` kwarg + DeprecationWarning path (api.py:525-541) | Deprecated since 0.2.0 and unreachable from the CLI, which only ever calls show_stats(verbose=True). A new crate carries no 8-year-old deprecation. |
| `proxybroker.rs` | Broker's `max_concurrent_conn` / `attempts_conn` deprecated aliases (api.py:_resolve_deprecated_limits) | Never exposed by the CLI; deprecated in 0.2.0. Nothing to surface. |
| `resolver.py, 558 LOC)` | `Resolver._cached_hosts` (class attribute) + `_cache_compatible` (resolver.py:37, 437-438, 459-468, 470-493) | hickory-resolver has a built-in `ResponseCache` driven by `ResolverOpts::cache_size` / `positive_min_ttl`, keyed on real DNS TTLs — strictly more correct than a dict that never expires. The Python hand-rolls it only because aiodns has none. `_cache_compatible` exists solely to police that hand-rolled cache's family-blindness; with no cache of ours, there is nothing to police. No moka layer either: nothing here needs a post-processed cache above hickory's (research §Caching). |
| `resolver.py, 558 LOC)` | `_QTYPE_DEFAULT` sentinel, `_fetch_records`, `_race_a_aaaa`, `_resolve` (resolver.py:31, 495-557) | 120 lines implementing Happy Eyeballs DNS (RFC 8305 §3) by hand — spawn A + AAAA, first non-empty wins, cancel the loser, re-raise the last error. That is `ResolverOpts::ip_strategy = LookupIpStrategy::Ipv4AndIpv6` on one line. The sentinel and the whole qtype/family dispatch only exist to let callers opt OUT of the race, and no caller does. |
| `resolver.py, 558 LOC)` | `resolve(port=, family=, qtype=, logging=)` parameters and the addrinfo `list[dict]` return shape (resolver.py:444-458) | The `{hostname, host, port, family, proto: IPPROTO_IP, flags: AI_NUMERICHOST}` dicts are an aiohttp `TCPConnector` custom-resolver hook shape. Nothing in the codebase installs this Resolver as an aiohttp resolver, and nothing passes `family`, so the branch is unreachable dead code: every live call gets the `family is None` path, which stores and returns a bare string. |
| `resolver.py, 558 LOC)` | `get_real_ext_ip` (singular) (resolver.py:393-407) | Self-documented as a backward-compatibility shim ('Prefer get_real_ext_ips in new code'). Zero callers — api.py:246 uses the plural. A new crate has no back-compat to keep. |
| `resolver.py, 558 LOC)` | `_wait_for_first_success` / `_drain_with_budget` as named functions (resolver.py:342-391) | Not the logic — the logic is preserved — but they stop being separate staticmethods. They were extracted to keep `get_real_ext_ips` under a Sonar cognitive-complexity threshold; with `JoinSet` absorbing the cancellation bookkeeping, the whole orchestration is ~15 readable lines inline. |
| `resolver.py, 558 LOC)` | Module-global `_mmdb_reader` opened at import time (resolver.py:23) | Import-time file I/O that every `import proxybroker` pays whether or not geo is used, and process-global mutable-ish state of exactly the kind locked decision 10 rejects for judges. Becomes `Option<Arc<GeoDb>>` owned by Broker. |
| `resolver.py, 558 LOC)` | The `_citydb if os.path.exists(_citydb) else _countrydb` selection (resolver.py:21) | A filesystem probe for a file the package never ships and the Rust crate never can. Superseded by `--geo-db <PATH>` (locked decision 3), which is explicit and doesn't depend on what happens to be sitting in the install directory. |
| `resolver.py, 558 LOC)` | The bundled `proxybroker/data/GeoLite2-Country.mmdb` | Locked decision 3. The GeoLite EULA §6.3 requires destroying stale copies within 30 days; a published crates.io version is immutable forever, so the obligation is unsatisfiable by construction. Replaced by DB-IP Country Lite (CC BY 4.0, no update clause, schema-compatible `country.iso_code`). Python's own bundle is 8.9 years stale and in breach on five independent grounds — do not copy the cautionary tale. |
| `resolver.py, 558 LOC)` | `canonicalize_ip` calls throughout this module (resolver.py:435, 451, 255) | Not the utils function (that's util.rs's problem) — its use HERE. Once resolve/probe/lookup all traffic in `IpAddr`, canonicalization is the parse, and `Display for IpAddr` is already RFC 5952. There is no textual form to normalize because there is no textual form. |
| `resolver.py, 558 LOC)` | The deferred-aiodns-construction guard and `loop=` parameter (resolver.py:53-63, 547-549) | Pure Python-runtime scar tissue: aiodns grabs `asyncio.get_event_loop()` at construction and Python 3.14 made that raise, so construction had to be lazy. Rust has no ambient event loop; `Resolver::new` just builds. |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | strategy="random" | Does not exist. server.py:56-57 raises ValueError for anything but 'best'. The brief mentions best/random and cli.py:273 takes a free-form string, but the source is the truth: `random` was never implemented. Do not invent it — a `--strategy random` user today gets a crash, and a Rust port that silently implements it is a new feature wearing a port's clothes. |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | heapq / the `_pool` binary heap | The heap is a liability, not an asset, at this size. heapq cannot pop a filtered minimum, so both `get()` and `remove()` drain the whole heap into a temp list and push it all back on any miss — O(N log N) with an in-source apology (server.py:140-142). A Vec + min_by_key scan over tens of proxies is faster, is 19 fewer lines, and removes the tuple-comparison TypeError. |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | Server._parse_request (incl. the 65536 cap and the aiohttp POST double-read hack) | hyper frames the request. The Python reads ONE 64 KB chunk and calls it the request, then re-reads once more if the method is POST and the chunk ends in \r\n\r\n — a comment-documented workaround ('For aiohttp. POST data returns on second reading') that is really a missing body-framing loop. Any request over 64 KB is truncated today. |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | Server._inject_headers | res.headers_mut().insert(). The function splices a header line in after the first \r\n of a raw byte chunk; with a typed Response there is nothing to splice. It is also the source of a corruption bug (see deviations). |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | utils.parse_headers / parse_status_line / get_status_code / errors.BadStatusLine — as used by this module | hyper's parser supersedes all of them. BadStatusLine exists only so _check_response can remap it to BadResponseError; hyper rejects the malformed status line before we see it. |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | CONNECTED = b"HTTP/1.1 200 Connection established\r\n\r\n" | hyper serializes a typed Response::builder().status(200). A hardcoded byte string is only needed when you are your own HTTP writer. |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | errors.ErrorOnStream | A wrapper whose only job is to tell `_handle` 'this failure happened during relay, not setup' so it can check `client_reader.at_eof()` and cancel the sibling stream task. In Rust that distinction is 'which function returned Err', and copy_bidirectional has no sibling to cancel. |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | Server.stop() and its `self._loop.stop()` | A library must never kill the caller's event loop. Merged into CancellationToken; there is no tokio equivalent and there should not be. |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | Server.aclose() / __aenter__ / __aexit__ | aclose() is stop() minus the loop kill; the context-manager pair exists to steer callers to the safe one. With one correct shutdown path there is nothing to steer around. Rust's Drop on the serve() future covers the RAII case. |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | Server._connections dict + _accept's _on_completion callback | The dict exists solely so stop() can iterate futures and cancel them, and the callback exists to pop from it and close the writer. CancellationToken + JoinSet + hyper's close-on-drop replace all of it. The callback's `raise exc` (server.py:299) inside a done-callback cannot even propagate — it goes to the loop exception handler. |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | asyncio.Queue.task_done() / join() backpressure plumbing | Locked decision 8/9: a bounded mpsc's capacity IS the backpressure. `_import`'s task_done() only exists to decrement the counter that api.py:482's `await self._proxies.join()` waits on. Note the semantics are not identical — see deviations. |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | Proxy.priority | Dead in Python — nothing calls it (the pool pushes avg_resp_time directly). Not dropped so much as finally used: it becomes `fn rank()`. |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | loop=None plumbing (Server._loop, the get_running_loop try/except, Resolver(loop=...)) | No tokio analogue. The try/except RuntimeError fallback at server.py:204-208 exists only because __init__ may run before a loop does. |
| `pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)` | client_reader._transport.get_extra_info('peername') | Private-attribute reach-through, used twice. The peer address is available from TcpListener::accept() and is passed down explicitly. |
| `*.rs)` | Provider subclasses for the 8 measured-dead registry entries: Freeproxylists_com, Proxylist_me, Foxtools_ru, Proxylist_download, and the bare Provider rows for ipaddress.com, hugeproxies.com, proxy.rufey.ru, geekelectronics.org | Decision 7 + measured: 4 domains do not resolve (freeproxylists.com, proxylist.me is DOMAIN-GONE, hugeproxies.com, proxy.rufey.ru, geekelectronics.org), foxtools.ru is ERR:URLError, ipaddress.com is 403, proxy-list.download is 502. Freeproxylists_com's two-stage uts-timestamp crawl and Proxylist_me's page-count discovery would each need real code for a domain that no longer exists. |
| `*.rs)` | The already-commented-out classes: Proxz_com (+ its Parse::UrlDecoded variant), Proxyb_net, Proxynova_com, _50kproxies_com, Free_proxy_cz, Maxiproxies-adjacent dead rows, and the commented bare providers (go4free.xyz, get-proxy.net, blackstarsecurity.com, ip-adress.com, cybersyndrome.net, proxylist.ro) | Commented out in the Python registry, i.e. already dead upstream, and independently confirmed dead by measurement (proxz.com/proxyb.net DOMAIN-GONE, ip-adress.com 403). Porting a class that nothing constructs is porting dead code. Note: Parse::UrlDecoded from research.md's sketch exists ONLY for Proxz_com and dies with it — do not add the variant. |
| `*.rs)` | ProxyProvider (the deprecated Provider alias emitting DeprecationWarning) | A deprecation shim for a 2018 rename. A new crate at 0.1 has no back-compat surface to preserve. |
| `*.rs)` | load_python_providers_from_directory() — importlib-based execution of arbitrary .py files from a directory, plus load_providers_from_directory(allow_python=True) | Both are in the public __all__ and both die. Rust has no equivalent that is not dlopen/libloading, which means an unsafe ABI-unstable plugin system for a proxy scraper — no. The replacement is strictly better on every axis: implement CustomProvider and call Registry::push_custom. The Python docstring itself calls it 'NOT safe for Docker bind-mounts'; the YAML path (which we keep) is the one it recommends anyway. load_providers_from_directory collapses into Registry::load_dir since the allow_python flag has nothing left to gate. |
| `*.rs)` | create_provider_config_template(filepath, provider_type) and its embedded `templates` dict | In __all__, but its whole job is emitting a commented example file. The bundled data/providers.yaml is 30 real, working, documented examples of all five Plan kinds — a strictly better template that cannot drift from the schema, because it IS the schema's only consumer. If the CLI wants `proxybroker providers template`, it prints the bundled file; that's a CLI concern, not a library API. |
| `*.rs)` | SimpleProvider._detect_format / _parse_csv / _parse_text / _parse_colon_proxy_line / _parse_text_proxy_line and the format: text\|csv\|html config values (~90 lines) | MEASURED against the actual algorithm: Parse::Default (the ip:port scanner) already subsumes all three. It pairs each IPv4 with the next 2-5 digit run before the next IPv4, so `1.2.3.4:8080`, `1.2.3.4\t8080`, `1.2.3.4,8080`, `"Server, Inc",1.2.3.4,8080` and `<td>1.2.3.4</td><td>8080</td>` all parse identically and correctly with zero format detection. The Python code path exists because Python reached for per-format parsers first and the scanner second. Only JSON genuinely needs structure (a `{"ip":..,"country_id":12,"port":8080}` body would pair the IP with `12`), so Parse::Auto = try-json-then-scan and Parse::Json stays. |
| `*.rs)` | APIProvider's api_key parameter and its three-header shotgun (setting X-API-Key AND Authorization: Bearer AND apikey simultaneously from one value) | Blasting a secret at three headers because you don't know which one the API wants is guessing, and it leaks the key to any endpoint that logs headers. `headers: {X-API-Key: ...}` in the config expresses the one true header exactly. Also removes the awkward Python template comment telling users not to paste a literal key into the YAML they are being handed. |
| `*.rs)` | Provider._cookies / the aiohttp cookies=self._cookies session param / Blogspot_com_base._cookies = {'NCR': 1} | Dead in Python and unused by anything else. Blogspot_com_base declares the class attribute, but Provider.__init__ unconditionally runs `self._cookies = {}`, which shadows it on every instance — the NCR cookie has never been sent. One provider family, one cookie, zero effect: do not port a cookie jar for it. (The static `Cookie: cookie=ok` in get_headers is a default header, not a jar, and survives.) |
| `*.rs)` | Provider.proxies property + setter (the `self._proxies` accumulating set) | Replaced by Provider::fetch returning owned Vec<Seed>. The setter's two jobs — attach self.proto and drop entries with a falsy port — move into Seed construction. The accumulation itself is the bug described in the fetch entry. |
| `*.rs)` | The `domain = 'blogspot.com^socks'` / `'tools.rosinstrument.com^socks'` caret suffix convention | A hack to give two providers on one domain distinct identities in logs. `name: blogspot-socks` in YAML is the identity; the domain is derivable from the URL when a log line wants it. |
| `*.rs)` | Provider._loop / the `try: loop or get_running_loop() except RuntimeError: self._loop = loop` constructor dance | Artifact of PROVIDERS being instantiated at import time, before any event loop exists. Registry entries are inert data; tokio needs no loop handle passed around. |

## Modules

### src/error.rs

errors.py's 10 classes are not one taxonomy, they are two wearing the same hat. Eight of them exist only to carry an `errmsg` class attribute that `proxy.py:333` reads reflectively (`self.stat["errors"][err.errmsg] += 1`) — they are histogram bucket keys, caught in bulk at every call site (checker.py:210-216, server.py:415-423) and never shown to a caller. Two of them (`NoProxyError`, `ResolveError`) actually reach the user. So: `ProxyError`, a flat `Copy + Eq + Hash` marker enum whose `Display` string IS the old `errmsg` (making it the literal key type of `HashMap<ProxyError, u32>`, a direct port of the `Counter()`); and `Error`, a `thiserror` enum of the things a caller can act on. `ProxyError` is deliberately dumb — no source chain, no payload — because a `Counter` key that allocates is a `Counter` key that is wrong. The errmsg strings are preserved byte-for-byte; the stats output stays wire-compatible.

**Crates:** `thiserror 2.0 — for `Error` only (`#[from]`, `#[source]`, `#[error(transparent)]`). NOT used for `ProxyError`.`, `serde 1 (derive not required here — the ProxyError impl is hand-written) — needed so `HashMap<ProxyError, u32>` is serializable for CLI stats output.`, `hickory-resolver 0.26 — `Error::Resolver` names `hickory_resolver::NetError` (research.md:486; the type is NOT called `ResolveError` in 0.26).`, `maxminddb 0.29 — `Error::GeoDb` names `maxminddb::MaxMindDbError` (lowercase `b`, research.md:571).`, `std::io, std::path::PathBuf — no crate.`

| Rust item | ← was | Action | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| `pub enum ProxyError` | errors.py:4 ProxyError (base) + ProxyConnError + ProxyRecvError + ProxySendError + ProxyTimeoutError + ProxyEmptyRecvError + BadStatusError + BadResponseError + BadStatusLine + ErrorOnStream | merge | One flat enum replaces nine exception classes because every call site already treats them as one set: checker.py:210-216 and checker.py:242-247 catch six of them in a single tuple; server.py:415-423 catches seven. Python's class hierarchy (ProxyError base) is load-bearing at exactly zero sites — nothing catches bare `ProxyError`. Copy+Eq+Hash is the whole point: this is the key type for the errors Counter (proxy.py:131 `Counter()`, proxy.py:333). No `#[source]`, no payload, no allocation — a bucket key that owns a String is a bucket key you cannot put in a HashMap cheaply. Causal detail (which syscall, which host) goes to `tracing` at debug, exactly where Python put it (the `msg` argument of `proxy.log`, which was always separate from `err`). |
| `ProxyError::ConnFailed` | errors.py:16 ProxyConnError (errmsg="connection_failed") | port | Raised at proxy.py:391 on ConnectionRefusedError/OSError/SSLError. errmsg string preserved verbatim. |
| `ProxyError::Timeout` | errors.py:28 ProxyTimeoutError (errmsg="connection_timeout") | port | Raised at proxy.py:387 (connect) and proxy.py:450 (recv). It is the ONE variant with distinct control flow: checker.py:208 and :239 `continue` (retry the same proxy) while all other variants `break`. That distinction must survive in checker.rs's match — it is not decorative. |
| `ProxyError::Reset` | errors.py:20 ProxyRecvError + errors.py:24 ProxySendError (BOTH errmsg="connection_is_reset") | merge | DEVIATION (see deviations). Two classes, one errmsg, therefore already one counter bucket in Python. No site discriminates them: checker catches both in the same tuple; server.py:507 catches ProxyRecvError only, but server._stream writes via `writer.write`/`drain` directly rather than `proxy.send`, so ProxySendError is unreachable there. Send-vs-recv direction lives in the tracing message ("Sending: failed" / "Received: failed"), which is where Python put it too (proxy.py:435, :453). |
| `ProxyError::EmptyRecv` | errors.py:32 ProxyEmptyRecvError (errmsg="empty_response") | port | Raised at proxy.py:459 when recv returns zero bytes without an OS error. Distinct from Reset because a clean zero-byte read is a different proxy pathology than RST. |
| `ProxyError::BadStatus` | errors.py:36 BadStatusError (errmsg="bad_status") | port | HTTP status != 200 from the judge (checker.py:297), CONNECT/SMTP negotiator status failure (negotiators.py:180/195/201/215), disallowed code in the local server (server.py:521). NOT ported for providers.py:150 — see dropped. Note Python's BadStatusError subclasses Exception, not ProxyError, despite being 100% a per-proxy failure; that split is an accident of the hierarchy, not a design. |
| `ProxyError::BadResponse` | errors.py:40 BadResponseError (errmsg="bad_response") | port | Malformed negotiator payload (negotiators.py:81/84/111/122/152/164), ValueError on response split (checker.py:301), and server.py:519's BadStatusLine->BadResponseError conversion. Carries no payload; negotiators.py:152's message ("SOCKS4 protocol does not support IPv6 destinations") becomes a tracing field, since the counter key was always just "bad_response". |
| `ProxyError::BadStatusLine` | errors.py:44 BadStatusLine (errmsg="bad_status_line") | port | Exists solely as the error return of `parse_status_line` (utils.py:159). Its errmsg is dead in Python — no `log(err=BadStatusLine)` call exists anywhere, and server.py:519 converts it to BadResponseError before it can be counted. Variant kept anyway because `parse_status_line` needs SOME error type and inventing a second one for a single unit variant is worse than one more arm. String preserved; it will simply never appear in the histogram, same as today. |
| `ProxyError::ErrorOnStream` | errors.py:48 ErrorOnStream (errmsg="error_on_stream") | port + redesign | This one IS counted, contrary to a first read: server.py:439 does `err = e` inside `except ErrorOnStream` and server.py:444's `finally` calls `proxy.log(request.decode(), stime, err=err)` -> `stat["errors"]["error_on_stream"] += 1`. So the key is live and must be preserved. Python's ErrorOnStream wraps its cause (`ErrorOnStream(e) from e`, server.py:511) purely so server.py:433 can do `"Timeout" in repr(e)` — a string-match on a repr. In Rust the variant is a bare marker and the cause travels typed, out of band, in a server-local newtype (next entry). |
| `ProxyError::Resolve` | errors.py:12 ResolveError (NO errmsg) | port + redesign | Return type of `Proxy::create` (proxy.py:83 `:raises ResolveError:`) and of resolver.rs's per-host lookup. Display string "resolve_failed" is NEW — Python's ResolveError has no errmsg, and passing it to `proxy.log(err=...)` would AttributeError. It is deliberately NOT incremented into any histogram: at api.py:443 the resolve fails BEFORE the Proxy exists, so there is no `stat` dict to count into. Variant exists to be a return type, not a bucket. Stats key set therefore unchanged from Python. |
| `ProxyError::as_str` | errors.py: the `errmsg` class attribute (consumed reflectively at proxy.py:333 via `err.errmsg` on a CLASS object, not an instance) | port + redesign | The single source of truth for every errmsg string. Python's version is a class attribute read off whatever object happens to be passed as `err=` — which is why it is a latent AttributeError for the three classes that lack it (see deviations). Here it is a total match over the enum: unrepresentable. `const fn` because it is a lookup table. Everything else (Display, Serialize) delegates to this, so the strings live in exactly one place. |
| `impl std::fmt::Display for ProxyError` | new | write fresh | Hand-written, NOT `#[derive(thiserror::Error)] #[error("connection_failed")]` as research.md sketches. Reason: per-variant `#[error("...")]` attributes would duplicate every literal that `as_str()` already owns, and the two would drift. Six lines of Display + a one-line `impl Error` is cheaper than the derive plus a duplicated table. thiserror is still used for `Error`, where it earns its keep (`#[from]`, `#[source]`). |
| `impl std::error::Error for ProxyError` | errors.py: `class ProxyError(Exception)` | write fresh | Empty body — no `source()`, because none of these have a cause worth chaining (the causes are `io::Error` kinds already collapsed into the variant). Needed only so `ProxyError` is a legal `E` in the `Result` returned by `Proxy::create` and the negotiators. |
| `impl serde::Serialize for ProxyError` | new | write fresh | Manual, not `#[derive(Serialize)]`, because the derive would emit variant NAMES ("ConnFailed") and the contract is the errmsg strings ("connection_failed"). Required for the CLI's stats output to be a JSON object keyed by errmsg — serde needs a string key for a HashMap key type. Python's equivalent is api.py:609 `print("Errors:", errors)` printing a Counter repr; JSON is the Rust-side upgrade. |
| `pub enum Error` | errors.py:8 NoProxyError + errors.py:12 ResolveError (the caller-facing half) | port + redesign | Everything a caller can actually do something about. Split from ProxyError by the only question that matters: can the caller act? A dead proxy -> no (count it, move on). A DB that will not open -> yes (fix the path). `#[non_exhaustive]` per the locked decision. Returned by `Broker::find`, `Broker::serve`, `GeoDb::open`. |
| `Error::NoProxy` | errors.py:8 NoProxyError (server.py:99, :107, :111) | port | Python raises it from three branches of ProxyPool.get (queue drained, timeout waiting for a scheme, max retries exhausted) and server.py:296 treats ALL of them as terminal: `if isinstance(exc, NoProxyError): self.stop()`. So it is fatal in practice regardless of which branch produced it; one variant, no branch discriminant. Also the one error in this module with a documented user-facing catch (examples/find_and_use.py:34). |
| `Error::Resolver` | resolver.py:547 `aiodns.DNSResolver()` deferred construction | port + redesign | Python constructs the resolver lazily inside the loop and lets a construction failure escape as a raw aiodns error. hickory 0.26's `Resolver::builder_tokio()` returns `Result<_, NetError>` (research.md:486-497 — NOT `ResolveError`, that name is gone in 0.26), so init failure is a typed fatal at Broker construction. Distinct from ProxyError::Resolve: this is "there is no DNS at all", that is "this one host did not resolve". |
| `Error::GeoDb` | resolver.py:106 `maxminddb.errors.InvalidDatabaseError` (swallowed) + the module-level `maxminddb.open_database(GEO_PATH)` | port + redesign | Python swallows InvalidDatabaseError at LOOKUP time (resolver.py:106 -> geo becomes "--"/"Unknown") but crashes hard at IMPORT time if the bundled db will not open. Rust keeps both halves but moves the hard failure to a returned error: a bad `--geo-db` path (locked decision 3 requires supporting one) must be fatal and named, not a panic at first use. Per-lookup misses stay non-fatal — maxminddb 0.29's `decode()` returns `Ok(None)` for a miss rather than erroring (research.md:568-569), so the swallow is now a match arm, not a catch. |
| `Error::Config` | provider_utils.py:565 `_load_provider_config` (yaml.YAMLError \| json.JSONDecodeError \| ValueError \| OSError, all logged and turned into None) | port + redesign | Locked decision 7 makes providers data-driven, which makes config the primary way a user breaks the build-free path — so a bad config the user NAMED must be fatal. Python's directory loader (`load_*_from_directory`) logs-and-skips a broken file so one typo does not kill 37 good providers; that behavior is preserved for directory scans. This variant is for an explicitly-pointed-at path only. `ConfigError` (serde_yaml/serde_json/io wrapper) lives in the provider config module, not here — it is a source, not a taxonomy. |
| `Error::Io` | server.py `asyncio.start_server` bind failures (uncaught in Python) | write fresh | `Broker::serve` binding a busy port is the concrete case. Python lets the OSError escape untyped; `#[from]` makes `?` work at the bind site. Transparent because wrapping "Address already in use" in prose adds nothing. |
| `pub type Result<T>` | new | write fresh | Standard alias for the fatal enum. Default type param so `Result<Proxy, ProxyError>` still spells out when the per-proxy enum is the error — the two must never be confusable at a glance. |
| `server::StreamFailure` | errors.py:48 ErrorOnStream(e) — the wrapping half | port + redesign | Not in error.rs — it is server-local control flow, not a taxonomy, and promoting it to a third public enum would violate locked decision 11. `_stream` returns `Result<(), StreamFailure>`; the handler counts `ProxyError::ErrorOnStream` (preserving the errmsg bucket) and reads `cause` to decide whether to break. Replaces server.py:433's `"Timeout" in repr(e)` with `failure.cause == ProxyError::Timeout` — this is the entire reason ProxyError is `PartialEq`. |

<details><summary><b>Proposed signatures</b></summary>

```rust
// pub enum ProxyError  ← errors.py:4 ProxyError (base) + ProxyConnError + ProxyRecvError + ProxySendError + ProxyTimeoutError + ProxyEmptyRecvError + BadStatusError + BadResponseError + BadStatusLine + ErrorOnStream
#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, Hash)] #[non_exhaustive] pub enum ProxyError { ConnFailed, Timeout, Reset, EmptyRecv, BadStatus, BadResponse, BadStatusLine, ErrorOnStream, Resolve }
// ProxyError::as_str  ← errors.py: the `errmsg` class attribute (consumed reflectively at proxy.py:333 via `err.errmsg` on a CLASS object, not an instance)
pub const fn as_str(&self) -> &'static str
// impl std::fmt::Display for ProxyError  ← new
fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result { f.write_str(self.as_str()) }
// impl std::error::Error for ProxyError  ← errors.py: `class ProxyError(Exception)`
impl std::error::Error for ProxyError {}
// impl serde::Serialize for ProxyError  ← new
fn serialize<S: Serializer>(&self, s: S) -> Result<S::Ok, S::Error> { s.serialize_str(self.as_str()) }
// pub enum Error  ← errors.py:8 NoProxyError + errors.py:12 ResolveError (the caller-facing half)
#[derive(Debug, thiserror::Error)] #[non_exhaustive] pub enum Error { ... }
// Error::NoProxy  ← errors.py:8 NoProxyError (server.py:99, :107, :111)
#[error("no available proxies")] NoProxy
// Error::Resolver  ← resolver.py:547 `aiodns.DNSResolver()` deferred construction
#[error("dns resolver init failed")] Resolver(#[source] hickory_resolver::NetError)
// Error::GeoDb  ← resolver.py:106 `maxminddb.errors.InvalidDatabaseError` (swallowed) + the module-level `maxminddb.open_database(GEO_PATH)`
#[error("cannot open geo database at {path}")] GeoDb { path: PathBuf, #[source] source: maxminddb::MaxMindDbError }
// Error::Config  ← provider_utils.py:565 `_load_provider_config` (yaml.YAMLError | json.JSONDecodeError | ValueError | OSError, all logged and turned into None)
#[error("invalid provider config at {path}")] Config { path: PathBuf, #[source] source: ConfigError }
// Error::Io  ← server.py `asyncio.start_server` bind failures (uncaught in Python)
#[error(transparent)] Io(#[from] std::io::Error)
// pub type Result<T>  ← new
pub type Result<T, E = Error> = std::result::Result<T, E>;
// server::StreamFailure  ← errors.py:48 ErrorOnStream(e) — the wrapping half
struct StreamFailure { cause: ProxyError }  // private to server.rs
```
</details>

**Open questions**

- Should an empty judge pool be fatal? checker.py:106-123 degrades silently — it disables HTTP/HTTPS/SMTP protocols and removes their negotiators, so a run with zero reachable judges yields zero proxies and reports nothing wrong. Preserving that is faithful; an `Error::NoJudges` when ALL protocols get disabled is arguably the right call but is a behavior change with no Python precedent. Dropped from the design pending sign-off.
- Is the errmsg key set a real public contract, or just human-printed? Python only ever renders it via `print("Errors:", errors)` (api.py:609) — a Counter repr. If nothing machine-reads it, preserving the exact strings (including the Recv/Send collapse and the omission of resolve_failed) buys nothing and we could pick better names. The whole design above assumes it IS a contract. Cheap to confirm; expensive to get wrong.
- `utils.py:179` (`parse_headers`) calls `parse_status_line` unguarded, so `BadStatusLine` can escape `parse_headers` into `server._parse_request` (server.py:449), where NOTHING catches it — it kills the client handler task. Latent Python bug. Rust forces the issue: `parse_headers` must return `Result<Headers, ProxyError>` and the server must decide. Suggest mapping it to `ProxyError::BadResponse` and dropping the client, mirroring server.py:518-519's handling of the same condition one layer down — but that is a new behavior, needs a call.
- `Error::NoProxy` is modeled as fatal because server.py:296 always calls `self.stop()` on it. But server.py:105-108 raises it on a per-request TIMEOUT waiting for a proxy of a given scheme, which reads transient. Is stopping the whole server on one slow request the intended behavior, or a Python bug we are about to faithfully port? If the latter, the timeout branch should be a retry, not an `Err`.
- Does `ProxyError` need `serde::Deserialize` as well as `Serialize`? Only matters if stats snapshots are ever read back in (resume, diffing runs). Nothing in the Python does this. Left out; trivial to add given `as_str()` is already the single table.

---

### src/utils.rs

| Rust item | ← was | Action | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| `test` | new | port | probe |

---

### src/negotiator.rs

Python's negotiators are a 6-class ABC hierarchy where each instance holds a back-reference to a Proxy and drives I/O through `proxy.send`/`proxy.recv`, logging and mutating the proxy's error counters as a side effect. In Rust this collapses to a closed `enum NegotiatorKind` + one free `async fn negotiate(kind, stream, target, tls) -> Result<Stream, ProxyFailure>` that is PURE protocol: it takes the transport by value, returns the negotiated transport, and never touches Proxy state — the caller (checker.rs) does the logging/stat accounting. SOCKS4/5 byte-banging is deleted entirely in favor of tokio-socks `connect_with_socket` + `into_inner`; only CONNECT (three variants sharing one tunnel helper) is hand-rolled. `Stream` is a two-variant enum (Plain/Boxed-Tls) so HttpsNgtr's asyncio `start_tls` in-place upgrade becomes a consuming `Stream::into_tls`.

**Crates:** `tokio (features: net, io-util, time)`, `tokio-socks 0.5.3`, `tokio-rustls 0.26`, `rustls 0.23`, `thiserror 2 (errors defined in errors.rs, used here)`, `tracing`

| Rust item | ← was | Action | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| `pub enum NegotiatorKind { Http, Https, Socks4, Socks5, Connect80, Connect25 }` | negotiators.py:BaseNegotiator + Socks5Ngtr/Socks4Ngtr/Connect80Ngtr/Connect25Ngtr/HttpsNgtr/HttpNgtr + NGTRS dict | port + redesign | Locked decision 6: closed set of 6, enum dispatch, no trait objects. The Python ABC exists only so `proxy.ngtr = 'SOCKS5'` can instantiate `NGTRS[proto](self)`; the instance carries exactly one field (`self._proxy`) and zero per-instance state. A Copy enum removes the allocation, the back-reference, and the dynamic dispatch. Derives Hash/Eq because checker.rs holds a `HashSet<NegotiatorKind>` (was `Checker._ngtrs`) and proxy.rs holds `HashMap<NegotiatorKind, Option<AnonLevel>>` (was `proxy.types`). |
| `NegotiatorKind::ALL` | negotiators.py:NGTRS / __all__ | port + redesign | `Checker.__init__` does `self._ngtrs = {proto for proto in types or NGTRS}` — the dict is used as an iterable of names, never as a factory map anywhere except `Proxy.ngtr` setter. A const array replaces both uses. No lazy_static, no registry. |
| `impl fmt::Display for NegotiatorKind` | negotiators.py: Socks5Ngtr.name='SOCKS5' … Connect25Ngtr.name='CONNECT:25' | port | Exact wire/CLI-visible strings preserved: HTTP, HTTPS, SOCKS4, SOCKS5, CONNECT:80, CONNECT:25. These strings are user-visible (CLI `--types`, `as_json()['types'][*]['type']`, log lines) so they are contract, not cosmetics. `proxy.log()` uses `self.ngtr.name if self.ngtr else 'INFO'` — the `INFO` fallback stays in proxy.rs as `Option<NegotiatorKind>`, not as a 7th variant. |
| `impl FromStr for NegotiatorKind` | proxy.py:Proxy.ngtr setter (`NGTRS[proto](self)`) + cli.py type parsing | port + redesign | Python's `NGTRS[proto]` raises KeyError on a bad name from CLI/API input; Rust returns a typed error so the CLI can print a real message listing the 6 valid names. Case-sensitive match on the exact Display strings (Python is too — `Proxy.__init__` intersects `set(types) & {'HTTP', ...}` and SILENTLY DROPS unknown names; that silent-drop stays in proxy.rs, unchanged, because it is the documented `expected_types` filter, not a parse). |
| `NegotiatorKind::check_anon_lvl` | negotiators.py:BaseNegotiator.check_anon_lvl=False / HttpNgtr.check_anon_lvl=True | port | True only for Http. Read by checker.rs `_check` to decide whether to compute the anonymity level. A const fn on the enum keeps the fact next to the variant, same as the Python class attribute. One-line match, no config. |
| `NegotiatorKind::use_full_path` | negotiators.py:BaseNegotiator.use_full_path=False / HttpNgtr.use_full_path=True | port | True only for Http. Read by checker.rs `_request` to send absolute-form request-target (`GET http://host/path`) instead of origin-form. Per research.md, hyper serializes the request Uri 'as-is' and does not validate origin-vs-absolute form, so this maps directly onto hyper 1.10 without a workaround. |
| `NegotiatorKind::target_port` | negotiators.py: `_CONNECT_request(host, 80)` / `(host, 25)` / `(host, 443)` and `kwargs.get('port', 80)` in Socks4Ngtr/Socks5Ngtr | port + redesign | Http/Socks4/Socks5/Connect80 => 80, Connect25 => 25, Https => 443. In Python the port lives in two unrelated places: hardcoded at the `_CONNECT_request` call sites, and as a never-supplied `port` kwarg defaulting to 80 in the SOCKS negotiators (verified: checker.py only ever calls `negotiate(host=..., ip=...)`, so SOCKS always targets 80). Folding both into one const fn keeps behavior identical and deletes the dead kwarg. This is why `Target` has no port field. |
| `NegotiatorKind::judge_scheme` | judge.py:Judge.get_random (the proto->scheme if/elif chain) | port + redesign | HTTPS=>Https, CONNECT:25=>Smtp, everything else=>Http. The mapping is a pure function of the negotiator, so it belongs next to the enum rather than as a stringly if/elif inside the judge picker. Locked decision 10 makes judge availability instance state on Checker; this fn is the key it indexes by. Borderline call — see open_questions if the lead prefers it in judge.rs. |
| `pub enum Stream { Plain(TcpStream), Tls(Box<TlsStream<TcpStream>>) }` | proxy.py:Proxy._reader/_writer = {'conn': ..., 'ssl': ...} + the `reader`/`writer` properties (`self._writer.get('ssl') or self._writer.get('conn')`) | port + redesign | Python models the TLS upgrade as two parallel dicts and picks 'ssl' first if present — an untyped state machine where 'both slots full' and 'plain closed but ssl live' are representable. The enum makes the state exact: exactly one transport, TLS-or-not. Tls is boxed because `TlsStream` is ~10KB (rustls buffers) and would otherwise bloat every `Stream` move and every future holding one. Python's `close()` closing the ssl writer then the conn writer becomes a plain `Drop`. |
| `impl AsyncRead for Stream / impl AsyncWrite for Stream` | proxy.py:Proxy.reader / Proxy.writer properties | write fresh | Mechanical delegation via match on the two variants (pin-project the inner). Exists so the CONNECT helpers and hyper's `TokioIo::new(stream)` accept the enum without caring which variant it is — same reason Python has the `reader`/`writer` properties. Note tokio-rustls docs (research.md) warn `poll_flush` is required after writing: the CONNECT writer MUST call `flush().await`, not just `write_all`, or the request can sit in the rustls buffer. |
| `Stream::into_tls` | proxy.py:Proxy.connect(ssl=True) — the asyncio `loop.start_tls(transport, protocol, ctx, server_hostname=self.host)` branch | port + redesign | This is the crux the brief flags. asyncio upgrades a transport IN PLACE; tokio-rustls `TlsConnector::connect(sni, stream)` CONSUMES the stream and hands back a new type. So the fn is consuming: `Plain(tcp)` => `Tls(Box::new(connector.connect(sni, tcp).await?))`. Already-`Tls` => `debug_assert!(false)` + return `ProxyFailure::BadResponse` (unreachable: HttpsNgtr negotiates exactly once per connection, and the checker drops the stream between attempts). No `Option::take`/`mem::replace` is needed at all once `negotiate` is consuming — see the `negotiate` entry. On TLS error the stream is consumed and dropped = closed, which matches Python's `finally: proxy.close()` on every failed attempt. |
| `pub struct Target<'a>` | negotiators.py: the `**kwargs` bag — `kwargs.get('host')`, `kwargs.get('ip')`, `kwargs.get('port', 80)`; supplied by checker.py as `negotiate(host=judge.host, ip=judge.ip)` | port + redesign | Replaces an untyped kwargs dict with the two fields that are actually passed. `host` is the judge's hostname (used for the CONNECT authority/Host header and now for SNI); `ip` is the judge's pre-resolved address (used as the SOCKS target so DNS stays LOCAL, never delegated to the proxy — i.e. socks5 semantics, not socks5h). Preserving that is important: resolving through the proxy would change what is being measured. `port` is dropped, see NegotiatorKind::target_port. Borrowed, not owned — it lives for one negotiate call. |
| `pub async fn negotiate` | negotiators.py:BaseNegotiator.negotiate (abstract) + proxy.py `proxy.ngtr = proto` instantiation + checker.py `await proxy.ngtr.negotiate(...)` | port + redesign | One free fn, `match kind` to six arms. THREE deliberate shape changes vs Python: (1) takes/returns `Stream` BY VALUE instead of the brief's `&mut Option<Stream>` — tokio-socks `connect_with_socket(socket, target)` and `TlsConnector::connect` both consume, so by-value is the natural fit and the Option dance buys nothing; the error path drops (=closes) the stream, exactly matching Python's per-attempt `finally: proxy.close()`. Flagged for sign-off since the brief specified Option::take. (2) takes no `&Proxy` — it does not log or bump `stat['errors']`; the caller does that from the returned error. (3) no internal timeout: the caller wraps the whole call in `tokio::time::timeout` (deviation, see deviations). `tls` is `&TlsConnector` (an `Arc<ClientConfig>` owned by Checker) — unused by 5 of 6 arms, which is cheaper than a second entry point. |
| `negotiate arm: NegotiatorKind::Http` | negotiators.py:HttpNgtr.negotiate (`pass`) | port | `Ok(stream)`. Literally a no-op, exactly as in Python — an HTTP proxy needs no handshake, the absolute-form request-target IS the negotiation (see use_full_path). Locked decision 5 explicitly keeps this a no-op. Do not invent a probe here. |
| `async fn negotiate_socks5` | negotiators.py:Socks5Ngtr.negotiate (lines 73-125) | replace-with-lib | All ~50 lines of hand-rolled RFC 1928 (greeting struct.pack('3B',5,1,0), 2-byte reply check, ATYP dispatch on ipaddress.ip_address, request pack, 4-byte reply header, rep_atyp length dispatch, BND.ADDR+BND.PORT drain) is DELETED. Body: `let Stream::Plain(tcp) = stream else { return Err(BadResponse) };` then `Socks5Stream::connect_with_socket(tcp, SocketAddr::new(target.ip, port)).await.map_err(map_socks_error)?.into_inner()` => `Stream::Plain`. tokio-socks handles v4/v6 ATYP, the domain-name reply case, and the BND drain; per research.md `into_inner()` returns the negotiated stream, so it composes straight on into TokioIo/hyper. No auth is offered (Python offers only method 0x00) — `connect_with_socket`, not `connect_with_password_and_socket`, matches that exactly. |
| `async fn negotiate_socks4` | negotiators.py:Socks4Ngtr.negotiate (lines 140-167) | replace-with-lib | `Socks4Stream::connect_with_socket(tcp, SocketAddrV4)` + `into_inner()`. The IPv6 guard is PRESERVED and moved up front: SOCKS4 has no ATYP byte and no v6 address type, so `IpAddr::V6 => return Err(ProxyFailure::BadResponse)` before touching the socket — same error class Python raises, and the type system now makes the `inet_aton` crash Python's comment mentions impossible. Empty user-id (Python packs a bare 0x00 terminator) => `connect_with_socket`, not `connect_with_userid_and_socket`. |
| `fn map_socks_error` | negotiators.py: `raise BadResponseError` on socks reply checks + proxy.py:recv's ProxyTimeoutError/ProxyRecvError/ProxyEmptyRecvError wrapping | write fresh | tokio-socks collapses I/O and protocol errors into one enum; Python split them across two layers (proxy.recv raised the I/O ones, the negotiator raised BadResponseError for protocol ones). Mapping that preserves the user-visible `stat['errors']` histogram keys: `Error::Io(e)` with `ErrorKind::UnexpectedEof` => `EmptyRecv` (Python's 'empty_response'), other `Io` => `Recv` ('connection_is_reset'), and ALL 22 protocol variants (`GeneralSocksServerFailure`, `NoAcceptableAuthMethods` — Python's 'auth is required' branch —, `ConnectionRefused`, `InvalidResponseVersion`, …) => `BadResponse` ('bad_response'). The 23 variants are NOT flattened away: the source error is retained via `#[source]` so the tracing line carries the reply code Python only ever logged as 'Failed (invalid data)'. |
| `async fn connect_tunnel` | negotiators.py: the identical CONNECT body shared by Connect80Ngtr.negotiate, Connect25Ngtr.negotiate and HttpsNgtr.negotiate (send _CONNECT_request; recv(head_only=True); get_status_code; != 200 => BadStatusError) | merge | Three byte-identical Python copies merged into one helper; the only difference between them was the port, now `kind.target_port()`. Takes `&mut Stream` (not by value) because the caller still owns it afterwards — Connect25 reads the SMTP banner from it, Https consumes it into TLS. Non-200 => `ProxyFailure::BadStatus` — preserving the exact variant matters (locked brief) because checker's per-proxy error counter feeds user-visible stats. |
| `fn connect_request` | negotiators.py:_CONNECT_request (lines 24-50) | port + redesign | Byte-for-byte identical output: `CONNECT {authority} HTTP/1.1\r\nHost: {host_header}\r\nUser-Agent: {ua}\r\nConnection: keep-alive\r\n\r\n`. The RFC 9112 §3.2.3 / RFC 9110 §7.2 IPv6 bracketing is PRESERVED: if `host.parse::<Ipv6Addr>().is_ok()` then authority=`[v6]:port` and Host=`[v6]`. Two Python quirks preserved deliberately for parity: the Host header carries NO port (while the authority does), and the trailing `Connection: keep-alive` is emitted after the UA. UA comes from utils.rs `get_headers()['User-Agent']` (= `PxBroker/{version}/`, empty rv suffix) — same source as Python. The `**kwargs` extra-headers parameter is dropped (see dropped). |
| `async fn read_head` | proxy.py:Proxy._recv(head_only=True) — the readline loop that stops at the first b'\r\n' | port + redesign | Only the `head_only=True` path is needed here — negotiators never read a body (checker.rs owns the full-response path, and that one moves to hyper entirely). So this is a small bounded loop over `AsyncBufRead::read_until(b'\n')` stopping at a bare CRLF, with a hard cap (e.g. 64 KiB / 100 lines) to bound a malicious proxy — Python's loop is unbounded except by the wall-clock timeout. Empty read => `ProxyFailure::EmptyRecv` (Python's ProxyEmptyRecvError); io error => `Recv`. |
| `fn parse_status_code` | utils.py:get_status_code(resp, start=9, stop=12) | port + redesign | Python slices fixed byte offsets [9:12] (works only for `HTTP/1.x NNN`) and swallows ValueError by returning 400 so the caller's `!= 200` check fires. Rust parses the status line properly (split on ASCII whitespace, take field 1) and returns None on garbage; the two CONNECT call sites treat `None` and `Some(n) if n != 200` identically => `BadStatusError`. Net observable behavior is the same; the fake 400 sentinel is dropped as an internal artifact. See deviations for the case where they differ. |
| `negotiate arm: NegotiatorKind::Connect80` | negotiators.py:Connect80Ngtr.negotiate | port | `connect_tunnel(&mut stream, target.host, 80)?; Ok(stream)`. Nothing else — Python does not validate the tunnel beyond the 200. |
| `async fn negotiate_connect25` | negotiators.py:Connect25Ngtr.negotiate (lines 189-201) | port | CONNECT to :25, then read EXACTLY 3 bytes (`read_exact`, was `proxy.recv(length=3)`) and compare to SMTP_READY. CRITICAL, per the brief: banner mismatch raises **BadStatus**, NOT BadResponse — Python uses `get_status_code(resp, start=0, stop=3)` + `err=BadStatusError`, and that key ('bad_status') lands in `proxy.stat['errors']` which is user-visible. Python's `readexactly` short-read returns the partial buffer, which then parses to some non-220 number => BadStatusError; Rust's `read_exact` UnexpectedEof maps to the same `BadStatus`, preserving the outcome. |
| `const SMTP_READY: u16 = 220` | negotiators.py:SMTP_READY = 220 | port | Compare the 3 banner bytes directly rather than int-parsing them — the only consumer is one equality check. Keeps the named constant (it documents 'SMTP service ready'). |
| `async fn negotiate_https` | negotiators.py:HttpsNgtr.negotiate (lines 209-216) + proxy.py:Proxy.connect(ssl=True) | port + redesign | The one with teeth. `connect_tunnel(&mut stream, target.host, 443)?` then `stream.into_tls(tls, ServerName::try_from(target.host.to_owned())?)`. Python's `await self._proxy.connect(ssl=True)` upgrades the SAME asyncio transport in place; Rust swaps the enum variant instead. SNI is the JUDGE host (`target.host`), NOT the proxy IP — Python passes `server_hostname=self.host`, which is the proxy's own IP. That is a bug; see deviations. Non-`Plain` input is unreachable (a fresh TCP stream per attempt). |
| `ProxyFailure (variants consumed here)` | errors.py:BadStatusError('bad_status'), BadResponseError('bad_response'), ProxyRecvError/ProxySendError('connection_is_reset'), ProxyEmptyRecvError('empty_response'), ProxyTimeoutError('connection_timeout') | port | Listed here because the map must record WHICH variant each path produces — checker.rs catches exactly this set (`except (ProxyConnError, ProxyRecvError, ProxySendError, ProxyEmptyRecvError, BadStatusError, BadResponseError): break`) versus ProxyTimeoutError (which `continue`s to the next try). If negotiate returns the wrong variant, retry behavior silently changes. `Timeout` is constructed by the caller's `tokio::time::timeout`, never by this module. Per locked decision 11 the enum is `#[non_exhaustive]` + thiserror, and each variant carries `errmsg()` (the stable histogram key) so proxy.rs stat counting is a straight port. |

<details><summary><b>Proposed signatures</b></summary>

```rust
// pub enum NegotiatorKind { Http, Https, Socks4, Socks5, Connect80, Connect25 }  ← negotiators.py:BaseNegotiator + Socks5Ngtr/Socks4Ngtr/Connect80Ngtr/Connect25Ngtr/HttpsNgtr/HttpNgtr + NGTRS dict
#[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug, PartialEq, Eq, Hash)] pub enum NegotiatorKind { Http, Https, Socks4, Socks5, Connect80, Connect25 }
// NegotiatorKind::ALL  ← negotiators.py:NGTRS / __all__
pub const ALL: [NegotiatorKind; 6]
// impl FromStr for NegotiatorKind  ← proxy.py:Proxy.ngtr setter (`NGTRS[proto](self)`) + cli.py type parsing
type Err = UnknownNegotiator; fn from_str(s: &str) -> Result<Self, Self::Err>
// NegotiatorKind::check_anon_lvl  ← negotiators.py:BaseNegotiator.check_anon_lvl=False / HttpNgtr.check_anon_lvl=True
pub const fn check_anon_lvl(self) -> bool
// NegotiatorKind::use_full_path  ← negotiators.py:BaseNegotiator.use_full_path=False / HttpNgtr.use_full_path=True
pub const fn use_full_path(self) -> bool
// NegotiatorKind::target_port  ← negotiators.py: `_CONNECT_request(host, 80)` / `(host, 25)` / `(host, 443)` and `kwargs.get('port', 80)` in Socks4Ngtr/Socks5Ngtr
pub const fn target_port(self) -> u16
// NegotiatorKind::judge_scheme  ← judge.py:Judge.get_random (the proto->scheme if/elif chain)
pub const fn judge_scheme(self) -> JudgeScheme  // JudgeScheme { Http, Https, Smtp } defined in judge.rs
// pub enum Stream { Plain(TcpStream), Tls(Box<TlsStream<TcpStream>>) }  ← proxy.py:Proxy._reader/_writer = {'conn': ..., 'ssl': ...} + the `reader`/`writer` properties (`self._writer.get('ssl') or self._writer.get('conn')`)
pub enum Stream { Plain(TcpStream), Tls(Box<tokio_rustls::client::TlsStream<TcpStream>>) }
// Stream::into_tls  ← proxy.py:Proxy.connect(ssl=True) — the asyncio `loop.start_tls(transport, protocol, ctx, server_hostname=self.host)` branch
async fn into_tls(self, tls: &TlsConnector, sni: ServerName<'static>) -> Result<Stream, ProxyFailure>
// pub struct Target<'a>  ← negotiators.py: the `**kwargs` bag — `kwargs.get('host')`, `kwargs.get('ip')`, `kwargs.get('port', 80)`; supplied by checker.py as `negotiate(host=judge.host, ip=judge.ip)`
pub struct Target<'a> { pub host: &'a str, pub ip: IpAddr }
// pub async fn negotiate  ← negotiators.py:BaseNegotiator.negotiate (abstract) + proxy.py `proxy.ngtr = proto` instantiation + checker.py `await proxy.ngtr.negotiate(...)`
pub async fn negotiate(kind: NegotiatorKind, stream: Stream, target: Target<'_>, tls: &TlsConnector) -> Result<Stream, ProxyFailure>
// async fn negotiate_socks5  ← negotiators.py:Socks5Ngtr.negotiate (lines 73-125)
async fn negotiate_socks5(stream: Stream, target: &Target<'_>, port: u16) -> Result<Stream, ProxyFailure>
// async fn negotiate_socks4  ← negotiators.py:Socks4Ngtr.negotiate (lines 140-167)
async fn negotiate_socks4(stream: Stream, target: &Target<'_>, port: u16) -> Result<Stream, ProxyFailure>
// fn map_socks_error  ← negotiators.py: `raise BadResponseError` on socks reply checks + proxy.py:recv's ProxyTimeoutError/ProxyRecvError/ProxyEmptyRecvError wrapping
fn map_socks_error(e: tokio_socks::Error) -> ProxyFailure
// async fn connect_tunnel  ← negotiators.py: the identical CONNECT body shared by Connect80Ngtr.negotiate, Connect25Ngtr.negotiate and HttpsNgtr.negotiate (send _CONNECT_request; recv(head_only=True); get_status_code; != 200 => BadStatusError)
async fn connect_tunnel(stream: &mut Stream, host: &str, port: u16) -> Result<(), ProxyFailure>
// fn connect_request  ← negotiators.py:_CONNECT_request (lines 24-50)
fn connect_request(host: &str, port: u16) -> Vec<u8>
// async fn read_head  ← proxy.py:Proxy._recv(head_only=True) — the readline loop that stops at the first b'\r\n'
async fn read_head(stream: &mut Stream, buf: &mut Vec<u8>) -> Result<(), ProxyFailure>
// fn parse_status_code  ← utils.py:get_status_code(resp, start=9, stop=12)
fn parse_status_code(head: &[u8]) -> Option<u16>
// async fn negotiate_connect25  ← negotiators.py:Connect25Ngtr.negotiate (lines 189-201)
async fn negotiate_connect25(stream: Stream, target: &Target<'_>) -> Result<Stream, ProxyFailure>
// const SMTP_READY: u16 = 220  ← negotiators.py:SMTP_READY = 220
const SMTP_READY: &[u8; 3] = b"220";
// async fn negotiate_https  ← negotiators.py:HttpsNgtr.negotiate (lines 209-216) + proxy.py:Proxy.connect(ssl=True)
async fn negotiate_https(stream: Stream, target: &Target<'_>, tls: &TlsConnector) -> Result<Stream, ProxyFailure>
// ProxyFailure (variants consumed here)  ← errors.py:BadStatusError('bad_status'), BadResponseError('bad_response'), ProxyRecvError/ProxySendError('connection_is_reset'), ProxyEmptyRecvError('empty_response'), ProxyTimeoutError('connection_timeout')
// defined in src/errors.rs; negotiator.rs only constructs BadStatus | BadResponse | Recv | Send | EmptyRecv
```
</details>

**Open questions**

- Strict 200 vs any 2xx for the CONNECT reply. Python requires exactly 200 (`if code != 200: raise BadStatusError`) in all three CONNECT paths; RFC 9110 §9.3.6 says any 2xx establishes the tunnel. I kept the strict 200 for parity, but it means a proxy replying `HTTP/1.1 201` is marked dead. Loosen to `(200..300)`? It would count as a deviation and change measured results.
- Does `enum Stream` belong in negotiator.rs or in a shared conn.rs? The brief puts it here, and the checker path is its only current consumer. But server.rs (the local proxy) also relays CONNECT and per research.md needs `serve_connection(..).with_upgrades()` on `TokioIo<TcpStream>` — if it ends up wanting the same Plain/Tls duality, `Stream` gets re-exported or moved. Lazy call: keep it in negotiator.rs, move it the day server.rs actually needs it.
- rustls crypto provider: aws-lc-rs (rustls 0.23 / reqwest 0.13 default) or `ring`? aws-lc-rs pulls cmake + a C toolchain (and NASM on Windows), which is a real friction tax on `cargo install proxybroker` for end users on stable 1.96.1. `ring` builds cleaner but diverges from reqwest 0.13's default, and having BOTH providers linked (reqwest for scraping, ours for checking) is a known footgun (`CryptoProvider::install_default` conflicts). Needs a crate-wide decision, not a per-module one.
- `NegotiatorKind::judge_scheme()` placement: it is a pure function of the negotiator kind so it reads naturally here, but locked decision 10 makes judge state Checker-owned and the mapping originates in judge.py:Judge.get_random. If the lead wants judge.rs to own the whole judge vocabulary, move it there and this module loses one entry.
- Python NEVER checks HTTPS-over-SOCKS: `Judge.get_random('SOCKS5')` falls into the `else: scheme='HTTP'` branch, so SOCKS is only ever validated against an HTTP judge on port 80 — yet `Proxy.schemes` advertises SOCKS4/SOCKS5 as supporting HTTPS (`_HTTPS_PROTOS`). So the HTTPS capability of every SOCKS proxy is asserted, never measured. Should the Rust checker substantiate it (SOCKS => judge:443 => TLS => HTTP/1.1)? The plumbing is already here — `target_port()` and `into_tls` compose — but it is a checker.rs policy decision and a new negotiation path, so I did not add it.
- Where is the `TlsConnector` built and what is its ALPN? research.md notes `alpn_protocols` is public, empty by default, and NOT offered unless set — it should almost certainly be `[b"http/1.1"]` since the checker speaks HTTP/1.1 via hyper's http1 handshake. Assumed Checker constructs one `Arc<ClientConfig>` at startup and passes `&TlsConnector` into `negotiate`; confirm that ownership.

---

### src/proxy.rs

Python's `Proxy` is two objects welded together: an immutable-ish *record* (host/port/types/geo/stats/log) that gets yielded to the user, and a *live connection* (reader/writer/_closed/_ngtr) that only exists during a check. The Rust split is `Proxy` (plain data, Clone + Send + 'static + Serialize, what `ProxyStream` yields) and `ProxyConn<'a> { proxy: &'a mut Proxy, stream: Stream }` (the transport, created by `Proxy::connect`, closed by `Drop`). That borrow inverts the Python ownership cycle in one move: negotiators become zero-sized enum variants that take `&mut ProxyConn`, the conn borrows the record, nothing owns the negotiator, no `Rc`/`Weak`/GC required. `SocketAddr` (not host+port strings) kills `_format_host_port`, the `port > 65535` check, and `host_is_ip`; `Ord`-derived `ProxyType` in a `BTreeMap` kills the `(len(tp), tp[-1])` sort-key hack; a structured `Event` enum kills api.py's substring-matching of log messages.

**Crates:** `serde (derive) — impl Serialize for Proxy / ProxyType / AnonLevel`, `thiserror — via crate::errors::ProxyError (defined in errors.rs, used as the Stats key here)`, `tokio (net, io-util, time) — TcpStream, AsyncReadExt/AsyncWriteExt, timeout`, `tokio-rustls 0.26 — TlsStream/TlsConnector for Stream::Tls + start_tls`, `rustls 0.23 — ClientConfig in ConnectOpts (type only)`, `hyper-util 0.1 (rt-tokio) — TokioIo in into_io()`, `tracing — the debug! that Proxy.record emits (facade only, ~free)`

| Rust item | ← was | Action | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| `pub struct Proxy` | proxy.py:Proxy | port + redesign | Record half only. The transport half (`_reader`, `_writer`, `_closed`, `_ngtr`) moves to `ProxyConn`; the policy half (`_timeout`, `_ssl_context`) moves to `ConnectOpts` owned by the Checker. Result: the thing `ProxyStream` yields is Clone + Send + 'static with no socket in it, which is what the streaming API (locked #8) requires. `types` is a BTreeMap so iteration order is the Python display order for free (see ProxyType). |
| `Proxy::new` | proxy.py:Proxy.__init__ | port + redesign | Infallible. All four Python `ValueError`s become unrepresentable: `host_is_ip` (host is `IpAddr` inside `SocketAddr`), `port is None`, `port > 65535` (u16), `int(port)` coercion. `types=()` filter `set(types) & {…}` disappears — an unknown protocol string can't reach here, it fails at `ProxyType::from_str` in the CLI/config layer. `timeout`/`verify_ssl` params dropped (see ConnectOpts). Geo is NOT computed here (Python calls the module-global `_mmdb_reader`); there is no global reader in Rust — the Broker sets it. |
| `Proxy::with_expected_types` | proxy.py:Proxy.__init__ (types= param) + Proxy.expected_types | port + redesign | Two-item mini-builder rather than a 5-arg constructor: `new(addr)` is the 90% case (providers construct with no expected types), `with_expected_types` is the CLI/Broker case. Read accessor is needed by checker.py:179-180 (`proxy.expected_types & self._ngtrs`), which becomes `BTreeSet::intersection`. |
| `Proxy::create` | proxy.py:Proxy.create (classmethod) | port | Async constructor, resolves domain->IP then builds. `resolver` is an explicit parameter, not a `kwargs.pop('resolver', Resolver(loop=loop))` default-construct — building a DNS resolver per proxy is a hidden cost the Python pays only because kwargs make it invisible. `loop` kwarg dropped (tokio). Returns `Err(ProxyError::Resolve)` instead of raising `ResolveError`; the `log.error(f'{host}:{port}: Error at creating')` line is dropped — it's the caller's decision whether a resolve miss is worth a log line (Broker already counts it). The whole `args[0] if args else kwargs.get('port','?')` defensive block evaporates with typed params. |
| `impl fmt::Display for Proxy` | proxy.py:Proxy.__repr__ | port | Byte-identical to Python's repr, which is genuinely user-facing (api.py:show_stats does `print(p)`). Reproducing it needs no sort-key closure: `BTreeMap<ProxyType, _>` already iterates in the Python order (see ProxyType). `{:.2}` on `avg_resp_time().as_secs_f64()` matches `f'{...:.2f}'`. Missing geo renders `--`, matching resolver.py's GeoData sentinel. |
| `impl fmt::Debug for Proxy` | new | write fresh | `#[derive(Debug)]`. Python overloads `__repr__` for both the human listing and debugging; Rust has two traits, so Display gets the pretty form and derived Debug gets the full struct dump (log, stats, runtimes) that the Python has no way to print. |
| `Proxy::addr / Proxy::host / Proxy::port` | proxy.py:Proxy.host, Proxy.port, _format_host_port | port + redesign | One stored field, three accessors. `SocketAddr`'s own Display already emits RFC 3986 bracketing (`[2001:db8::1]:8080`) for v6 and passes v4 through — `_format_host_port` and its three call sites are deleted outright, and every future `host:port` format string in the crate gets bracketing correct by construction rather than by remembering to call the helper. |
| `Proxy::types` | proxy.py:Proxy.types (getter) / Proxy._types | port | Read side only. Value is `Option<AnonLevel>` because Python's `None` level for non-HTTP types is a real absence, not a sentinel. |
| `Proxy::set_type / Proxy::remove_type` | proxy.py:checker.py:220,260 (`proxy.types[name] = lvl`) and checker.py:149 (`del proxy.types[proto]`) | port + redesign | Python exposes a mutable dict and lets callers poke it. Two named mutators instead: they are the only two operations anyone performs, and they keep `_schemes` invalidation from being a thing (the cache is gone). The whole-dict `types` SETTER — with its `isinstance(new_types, dict)` / `TypeError` runtime check — is dropped: it exists purely to guard against dynamic typing, and no production call site assigns it. |
| `Proxy::is_working / Proxy::set_working` | proxy.py:Proxy.is_working property + setter, Proxy._is_working | port | Straight port; the Python property pair is a no-op wrapper over the field. Written once by checker.py:193, read by api.py:544. |
| `Proxy::error_rate` | proxy.py:Proxy.error_rate | port + redesign | `sum(errors.values()) / requests`, 0.0 when `requests == 0`. Rounding to 2dp is NOT done here (see deviations) — it happens in the Serialize impl and in Display, so the number a caller compares against `max_error_rate` is the real one. |
| `Proxy::avg_resp_time` | proxy.py:Proxy.avg_resp_time | port + redesign | `Duration`, not bare f64 seconds — the unit is in the type, and `Duration::ZERO` for the empty case instead of Python's `int 0` (which is not even the same type as the float it returns otherwise). Sum/len over `runtimes: Vec<Duration>`; rounding moved to the render sites. |
| `Proxy::supports_scheme` | proxy.py:Proxy.schemes, _HTTP_PROTOS, _HTTPS_PROTOS, Proxy._schemes | port + redesign | Every real use is membership (`server.py:72,100`: `if scheme in proxy.schemes`). So return the answer, not a collection. Computed on the fly from `types` — the `_schemes` tuple cache (and the setter's cache-invalidation dance) is deleted: it caches at most six `match` arms. The two module-level frozensets become a `ProxyType::serves(Scheme) -> bool` match. |
| `pub enum Scheme` | proxy.py:_HTTP_PROTOS / _HTTPS_PROTOS keys ("HTTP"/"HTTPS" as scheme strings) | port + redesign | Python overloads the string "HTTP" as BOTH a proxy type and a URL scheme, which is why `_HTTP_PROTOS` has to list `SOCKS5` under `HTTP`. Two distinct concepts, two types. Consumed by server.rs's pool lookup. |
| `Proxy::geo / Proxy::set_geo` | proxy.py:Proxy.geo property, Proxy._geo, `Resolver.get_ip_info(self.host)` call in __init__ | port + redesign | `Option<Geo>` because the `geo` feature may be off, no db path supplied, or the IP simply isn't in the db. Populated by the Broker after construction (it owns the `GeoDb`); Python can do it in `__init__` only because it has a module-global mmdb reader opened at import time, which is exactly the global state we're deleting. `Geo` itself lives in geo.rs, not here. Read by api.py:462 country filtering and by as_json. |
| `Proxy::log` | proxy.py:Proxy.get_log | port + rename | Renamed getter->`log`, because Python's `log()` (the verb, appends) and `get_log()` (the noun, reads) collide on the good name. The verb becomes `record`. |
| `Proxy::record` | proxy.py:Proxy.log(msg, stime=0, err=None) | port + redesign | Python's `log()` does five jobs: tracing::debug, truncate msg to 60 chars, push a (ngtr, msg, runtime) tuple, bump `stat['errors'][err.errmsg]`, and append to `_runtimes` unless the *string* contains 'timeout'. Keeps four of five: emits `tracing::debug!`, pushes a structured `LogEntry`, bumps `stats.errors[err]`, and appends the runtime unless `event.is_timeout()`. Truncation is dropped (it's a formatting concern of api.rs's verbose printer, not of storage). Takes `stime` as an already-computed `Option<Duration>` rather than a unix-epoch float — callers use `Instant::elapsed()`. `pub(crate)` because only proxy.rs/negotiators.rs/checker.rs/api.rs call it. |
| `pub struct LogEntry` | proxy.py: the (ngtr, msg, runtime) tuple pushed to Proxy._log | port + redesign | Named struct over an anonymous 3-tuple. `ngtr: Option<_>` replaces the `'INFO'` magic string for entries recorded outside a negotiation (Display for the None case still prints `INFO`, so api.rs's grouped verbose output is unchanged). |
| `pub enum Event` | proxy.py / negotiators.py / checker.py / api.py: the ~18 distinct strings passed to proxy.log() | port + redesign | This is the one place I add structure rather than removing it, and it pays for itself twice. (1) api.py:572-590 CLASSIFIES proxies by substring-matching the joined log text — `'Location of proxy' in msgs`, `'Connection: success' in msgs`, `'Protocol or the level' in msgs`, `event.startswith('Initial connection')`. That is parsing your own debug output; with an enum it's a `matches!`. (2) proxy.py:334's `'timeout' not in msg` guard (which decides whether a measurement enters the response-time average) becomes `event.is_timeout()`. `impl Display for Event` emits the identical strings, so verbose CLI output stays byte-compatible. |
| `pub struct Stats` | proxy.py:Proxy.stat = {'requests': 0, 'errors': Counter()} | port + redesign | A dict-of-mixed-types becomes a struct. `HashMap<ProxyError, u32>` is the `Counter()` — keyed by the error enum itself, not by its `errmsg` string, which is only stringly-typed because Python lacks a cheap hashable enum (research.md is explicit: `ProxyError` is `Copy + Hash` precisely to be this key). api.py:552's `errors.update(p.stat['errors'])` becomes a merge over the map. |
| `pub enum ProxyType` | negotiators.py:NGTRS keys + the `set(types) & {...}` literal in Proxy.__init__ | port + redesign | DECLARATION ORDER IS LOAD-BEARING and is not alphabetical. Python sorts types for display with `key=lambda tp_lvl: (len(tp_lvl[0]), tp_lvl[0][-1])` — string length, then last character — duplicated verbatim in both `__repr__` and `as_json`. Evaluated over the six real values that key yields exactly: HTTP, HTTPS, SOCKS4, SOCKS5, CONNECT:80, CONNECT:25. Derive `Ord` with the variants in that order, store in a `BTreeMap`, and both sort closures are deleted while the output stays identical. Lives here rather than in negotiators.rs because Proxy is the type that carries it and negotiators.rs already depends on proxy.rs. |
| `pub enum AnonLevel` | checker.py:374-378 ('Transparent' / 'Anonymous' / 'High' string literals), cli.py:219 choices | port + redesign | The anonymity level is a closed 3-value set that Python passes around as bare strings, duplicated between checker.py and cli.py's `choices=[...]`. One enum makes clap's `value_parser` and the checker agree by construction. `Ord` is declared worst->best so `>= AnonLevel::Anonymous` is a legal filter (Python has to compare strings or hand-roll a rank table). |
| `impl Serialize for Proxy` | proxy.py:Proxy.as_json | port + redesign | Per brief: `impl Serialize`, not a method returning a map — so `serde_json::to_writer(out, &proxy)` works, and the CLI's `json.dumps(proxy.as_json())` becomes one call with no intermediate allocation. Hand-written `serialize` that builds the private `ProxyJson` view and forwards, because the wire shape (nested `geo.country.code` / `geo.region.name` / `geo.city`, `types` as a list of `{type, level}` objects with `level: ""` for None) does not match the struct layout. Wire-compatible with Python byte-for-byte, INCLUDING: the 2dp rounding of `avg_resp_time`/`error_rate` (applied here, at the boundary), the `--`/`Unknown` geo sentinels for a missing lookup, and the type ordering (free via BTreeMap). No `Deserialize` — nothing reads this format back. |
| `pub struct ProxyConn<'a>` | proxy.py:Proxy._reader, Proxy._writer, Proxy._closed, Proxy._ngtr, Proxy.reader, Proxy.writer | port + redesign | THE cycle-break. Python: Proxy owns `_ngtr`; `NGTRS[proto](self)` hands the negotiator a back-ref to Proxy; negotiator calls `self._proxy.send/recv/log`. Rust inverts it — the transport BORROWS the record (`&'a mut Proxy`), so stats/log writes still land on the proxy (`self.proxy.record(...)`) with no Rc, no Weak, no clone, and the borrow checker enforces the thing the Python comment can only ask for: you cannot yield a Proxy to the user while a check is still running against it. `_closed` is gone — a live `ProxyConn` IS an open connection, and Drop closes it. The `reader`/`writer` properties (`self._writer.get('ssl') or self._writer.get('conn')` — an ad-hoc union type built from two dicts) collapse into the single `stream` field holding `Stream::Plain \| Stream::Tls`. |
| `enum Stream` | proxy.py: the {'conn': ..., 'ssl': ...} reader/writer dict pair | port + redesign | Python models 'plain or TLS-upgraded' as two dicts with two keys each and an `or` in a property. Two variants. `Box` the TLS arm because `TlsStream` is large and the plain arm is the common case. |
| `Proxy::connect` | proxy.py:Proxy.connect(ssl=False) — the non-SSL branch | port + redesign | Splits Python's boolean-flag-overloaded `connect(ssl=)` (two unrelated code paths behind one param) into `connect` (TCP) and `ProxyConn::start_tls` (upgrade). Behavior preserved exactly: records `InitialConnection`, `tokio::time::timeout(opts.timeout, TcpStream::connect(addr))`, maps elapsed->`ProxyError::Timeout` and io error->`ProxyError::ConnFailed`, increments `stats.requests` and records the outcome event on EVERY path (Python's `finally:`). Takes `ngtr` because Python's `proxy.ngtr = proto` assignment-with-side-effects (a property setter that constructs an object) exists only to tag subsequent log lines — here it's just a value carried by the conn. `checker.py:205-206`'s `proxy.ngtr = proto; await proxy.connect()` becomes one call. |
| `ProxyConn::start_tls` | proxy.py:Proxy.connect(ssl=True) — the SSL branch | port + redesign | Consumes `self.stream`, wraps with `tokio_rustls::TlsConnector::from(opts.tls.clone()).connect(server_name, s)`, stores `Stream::Tls`. Replaces the asyncio internals-spelunking that Python needs here (`self._writer['conn'].transport`, a hand-built `StreamReaderProtocol`, `loop.start_tls`, reaching into `protocol._stream_reader` — a private attribute), which is ~20 lines of the file and the most fragile code in it. Same request counting + `SSL: Connection: {success,failed,timeout}` events. Called by the HTTPS negotiator after its CONNECT succeeds. Note per research.md: rustls needs `alpn_protocols = [b"http/1.1"]` set explicitly. |
| `ProxyConn::send` | proxy.py:Proxy.send | port | `write_all` + `flush` (Python's `write` + `drain`; tokio-rustls docs explicitly require the flush — poll_write alone does not reach the socket). `&[u8]` only — Python's `req.encode() if not isinstance(req, bytes)` str/bytes union disappears; callers pass `b"..."` or `s.as_bytes()`. Maps error to `ProxyError::Reset` (Python catches only `ConnectionResetError`; we catch any io::Error, see deviations) and records `Event::Request` on every path. |
| `ProxyConn::recv_exact` | proxy.py:Proxy.recv(length=N) + Proxy._recv's `readexactly` branch | port | The SOCKS path (negotiators call recv(2)/recv(4)/recv(1)/recv(8)) and Connect25's `recv(length=3)`. Wraps `read_exact` in `timeout(opts.timeout, ..)`. Python swallows `IncompleteReadError` and returns `e.partial`, then the caller indexes `resp[0]`/`resp[1]` — a short read becomes an IndexError instead of a proxy error; Rust returns `ProxyError::EmptyRecv` on a short read (see deviations). Empty response -> `ProxyError::EmptyRecv`, matching `ProxyEmptyRecvError`. Records `Received {bytes, head}` / `RecvFailed` / `RecvTimeout` with the first 12 bytes, as Python does. |
| `ProxyConn::recv_head` | proxy.py:Proxy.recv(head_only=True) + Proxy._recv's `line == b'\r\n'` head branch | port | Reads until CRLFCRLF (bounded — see deviations), for the CONNECT/HTTPS negotiators' reply status line. Same timeout/error/logging contract as recv_exact. This plus recv_exact is the entire negotiation surface; the judge request/response goes through hyper (locked #4), so Python's `_recv` body loop is dropped. |
| `impl Drop for ProxyConn<'_>` | proxy.py:Proxy.close | port + redesign | Drop takes the stream and drops it (closing the fd) and records `Event::ConnectionClosed` on the borrowed proxy — so `checker.py`'s `finally: proxy.close()` in both retry loops just disappears, along with the `_closed` re-entrancy guard (Drop runs once, by construction) and `self._ngtr = None` (the conn owns the ngtr and dies with it). Python's two `try/except Exception: self.log(f'Error closing ... writer')` blocks are dropped: closing a `TcpStream`/`TlsStream` in Rust is infallible and there is nothing to report. Non-async, so no TLS close_notify — acceptable, and matches Python, which also never awaits `wait_closed()`. |
| `ProxyConn::replace_stream_with` | new (enabling glue for tokio-socks / hyper composition) | write fresh | Python's negotiators only ever push bytes, so it never needs this. Rust's do: `tokio_socks::Socks5Stream::connect_with_socket(socket, target)` CONSUMES the socket and gives it back via `into_inner()` (research.md's key composition point), and `start_tls` likewise. This is the take-transform-put primitive both need, with the `Option<Stream>` niche kept private so `send`/`recv` never see a hole. Alternative considered and rejected: public `take_stream`/`put_stream`, which lets a caller lose the stream on an early `?`. |
| `ProxyConn::into_io` | new | write fresh | Hands the fully negotiated stream (post-SOCKS / post-CONNECT / post-TLS) to `hyper::client::conn::http1::handshake`. Required because hyper 1.x's `Read`/`Write` are `hyper::rt`'s, not tokio's (research.md flags this as the most common porting mistake) — one `TokioIo::new` at one boundary. This is the seam Python doesn't have: it hand-parses the judge's HTTP response in `_recv` instead. Consuming `self` means Drop no longer closes it — the hyper `Connection` task owns the socket from here. |
