| `pub struct ConnectOpts` | proxy.py:Proxy._timeout, Proxy._ssl_context, Proxy.__init__(timeout=8, verify_ssl=False) | port + redesign | Per-run policy, not per-proxy identity: every proxy in a Broker run gets the same timeout and the same SSL context, and Python re-stores both on each of the thousands of Proxy objects it creates. One `ConnectOpts` owned by the Checker, borrowed at connect time; `Arc<ClientConfig>` because rustls configs are meant to be shared (and building one per proxy would re-do cert-store setup thousands of times). Also gets `verify_ssl` off the yielded record, where it was never anyone's business. |

<details><summary><b>Proposed signatures</b></summary>

```rust
// pub struct Proxy  ← proxy.py:Proxy
#[derive(Debug, Clone)] pub struct Proxy { addr: SocketAddr, expected_types: BTreeSet<ProxyType>, types: BTreeMap<ProxyType, Option<AnonLevel>>, is_working: bool, geo: Option<Geo>, stats: Stats, log: Vec<LogEntry>, runtimes: Vec<Duration> }
// Proxy::new  ← proxy.py:Proxy.__init__
pub fn new(addr: SocketAddr) -> Self
// Proxy::with_expected_types  ← proxy.py:Proxy.__init__ (types= param) + Proxy.expected_types
pub fn with_expected_types(self, types: impl IntoIterator<Item = ProxyType>) -> Self  // + pub fn expected_types(&self) -> &BTreeSet<ProxyType>
// Proxy::create  ← proxy.py:Proxy.create (classmethod)
pub async fn create(host: &str, port: u16, resolver: &Resolver) -> Result<Proxy, ProxyError>
// impl fmt::Display for Proxy  ← proxy.py:Proxy.__repr__
// <Proxy US 1.12s [HTTP: Anonymous, HTTPS] 10.0.0.1:8080>
// Proxy::addr / Proxy::host / Proxy::port  ← proxy.py:Proxy.host, Proxy.port, _format_host_port
pub fn addr(&self) -> SocketAddr; pub fn host(&self) -> IpAddr; pub fn port(&self) -> u16
// Proxy::types  ← proxy.py:Proxy.types (getter) / Proxy._types
pub fn types(&self) -> &BTreeMap<ProxyType, Option<AnonLevel>>
// Proxy::set_type / Proxy::remove_type  ← proxy.py:checker.py:220,260 (`proxy.types[name] = lvl`) and checker.py:149 (`del proxy.types[proto]`)
pub fn set_type(&mut self, ty: ProxyType, lvl: Option<AnonLevel>); pub fn remove_type(&mut self, ty: ProxyType) -> Option<Option<AnonLevel>>
// Proxy::is_working / Proxy::set_working  ← proxy.py:Proxy.is_working property + setter, Proxy._is_working
pub fn is_working(&self) -> bool; pub fn set_working(&mut self, val: bool)
// Proxy::error_rate  ← proxy.py:Proxy.error_rate
pub fn error_rate(&self) -> f64
// Proxy::avg_resp_time  ← proxy.py:Proxy.avg_resp_time
pub fn avg_resp_time(&self) -> Duration
// Proxy::supports_scheme  ← proxy.py:Proxy.schemes, _HTTP_PROTOS, _HTTPS_PROTOS, Proxy._schemes
pub fn supports_scheme(&self, scheme: Scheme) -> bool
// pub enum Scheme  ← proxy.py:_HTTP_PROTOS / _HTTPS_PROTOS keys ("HTTP"/"HTTPS" as scheme strings)
#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq)] pub enum Scheme { Http, Https }
// Proxy::geo / Proxy::set_geo  ← proxy.py:Proxy.geo property, Proxy._geo, `Resolver.get_ip_info(self.host)` call in __init__
pub fn geo(&self) -> Option<&Geo>; pub fn set_geo(&mut self, geo: Geo)
// Proxy::log  ← proxy.py:Proxy.get_log
pub fn log(&self) -> &[LogEntry]
// Proxy::record  ← proxy.py:Proxy.log(msg, stime=0, err=None)
pub(crate) fn record(&mut self, ngtr: Option<NegotiatorKind>, event: Event, runtime: Option<Duration>, err: Option<ProxyError>)
// pub struct LogEntry  ← proxy.py: the (ngtr, msg, runtime) tuple pushed to Proxy._log
#[derive(Debug, Clone)] pub struct LogEntry { pub ngtr: Option<NegotiatorKind>, pub event: Event, pub runtime: Duration }
// pub enum Event  ← proxy.py / negotiators.py / checker.py / api.py: the ~18 distinct strings passed to proxy.log()
#[non_exhaustive] pub enum Event { InitialConnection { ssl: bool }, ConnectSuccess { ssl: bool }, ConnectFailed { ssl: bool }, ConnectTimeout { ssl: bool }, ConnectionClosed, Request { head: String }, Received { bytes: usize, head: Vec<u8> }, RecvFailed, RecvTimeout, JudgeSelected(String), NegotiationGranted, AuthRequired, InvalidData, Socks4Ipv6Unsupported, ConnectBadStatus(u16), GetResult { ok: bool }, ResponseCorrect, ResponseIncorrect, AnonymityVerdict { .. }, FoundInDnsbl, WrongTypeOrLevel, OutsideCountryList }  // impl Display reproduces the exact Python strings
// pub struct Stats  ← proxy.py:Proxy.stat = {'requests': 0, 'errors': Counter()}
#[derive(Debug, Clone, Default)] pub struct Stats { pub requests: u32, pub errors: HashMap<ProxyError, u32> }  // + pub fn stats(&self) -> &Stats
// pub enum ProxyType  ← negotiators.py:NGTRS keys + the `set(types) & {...}` literal in Proxy.__init__
#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, Hash, Serialize)] pub enum ProxyType { Http, Https, Socks4, Socks5, Connect80, Connect25 }  // + FromStr, Display ("HTTP", "HTTPS", "SOCKS4", "SOCKS5", "CONNECT:80", "CONNECT:25")
// pub enum AnonLevel  ← checker.py:374-378 ('Transparent' / 'Anonymous' / 'High' string literals), cli.py:219 choices
#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, Serialize)] pub enum AnonLevel { Transparent, Anonymous, High }  // + FromStr, Display
// impl Serialize for Proxy  ← proxy.py:Proxy.as_json
impl serde::Serialize for Proxy  // + private #[derive(Serialize)] struct ProxyJson<'a> { host, port, geo: GeoJson<'a>, types: Vec<TypeJson>, avg_resp_time: f64, error_rate: f64 }
// pub struct ProxyConn<'a>  ← proxy.py:Proxy._reader, Proxy._writer, Proxy._closed, Proxy._ngtr, Proxy.reader, Proxy.writer
pub struct ProxyConn<'a> { proxy: &'a mut Proxy, stream: Option<Stream>, ngtr: Option<NegotiatorKind>, opts: ConnectOpts }
// enum Stream  ← proxy.py: the {'conn': ..., 'ssl': ...} reader/writer dict pair
enum Stream { Plain(TcpStream), Tls(Box<TlsStream<TcpStream>>) }  // AsyncRead + AsyncWrite forwarded
// Proxy::connect  ← proxy.py:Proxy.connect(ssl=False) — the non-SSL branch
pub async fn connect(&mut self, ngtr: NegotiatorKind, opts: &ConnectOpts) -> Result<ProxyConn<'_>, ProxyError>
// ProxyConn::start_tls  ← proxy.py:Proxy.connect(ssl=True) — the SSL branch
pub async fn start_tls(&mut self) -> Result<(), ProxyError>
// ProxyConn::send  ← proxy.py:Proxy.send
pub async fn send(&mut self, req: &[u8]) -> Result<(), ProxyError>
// ProxyConn::recv_exact  ← proxy.py:Proxy.recv(length=N) + Proxy._recv's `readexactly` branch
pub async fn recv_exact(&mut self, len: usize) -> Result<Vec<u8>, ProxyError>
// ProxyConn::recv_head  ← proxy.py:Proxy.recv(head_only=True) + Proxy._recv's `line == b'\r\n'` head branch
pub async fn recv_head(&mut self) -> Result<Vec<u8>, ProxyError>
// ProxyConn::replace_stream_with  ← new (enabling glue for tokio-socks / hyper composition)
pub(crate) async fn replace_stream_with<F, Fut>(&mut self, f: F) -> Result<(), ProxyError> where F: FnOnce(Stream) -> Fut, Fut: Future<Output = Result<Stream, ProxyError>>
// ProxyConn::into_io  ← new
pub fn into_io(self) -> TokioIo<Stream>
// pub struct ConnectOpts  ← proxy.py:Proxy._timeout, Proxy._ssl_context, Proxy.__init__(timeout=8, verify_ssl=False)
#[derive(Clone)] pub struct ConnectOpts { pub timeout: Duration, pub tls: Arc<rustls::ClientConfig> }
```
</details>

**Open questions**

- Leading-zero IPv4 ("127.0.0.001"): port resolver.py's lenient normalization as `resolver::parse_ip_lenient` (applied ONLY to provider-scraped text, never to user input, given CVE-2021-29921's octal/decimal ambiguity), or accept dropping those proxies? Needs a measurement — how many proxies do the ~28 live providers actually emit in that form? If it's zero, this is free.
- Does anything need `Ord`/`PartialEq` on Proxy? server.py:127 does `heapq.heappush(self._pool, (proxy.avg_resp_time, proxy))` — on a tie in avg_resp_time (extremely common: two proxies with zero runtimes both give 0) Python's heapq falls through to comparing the Proxy objects themselves, which have no `__lt__` -> `TypeError: '<' not supported between instances of 'Proxy'`. That looks like a live crash in the local-server pool. It's server.rs's call (BinaryHeap<Reverse<(Duration, ProxyKey)>> avoids needing Ord on Proxy at all), but if server.rs wants `Ord` on Proxy it has to be declared here.
- Should `Stats::requests` also count the judge round-trip? Python increments `stat['requests']` only in `connect()` (and again in the SSL upgrade, so an HTTPS check counts 2 requests for 1 logical attempt) — meaning `error_rate` is really errors-per-connection-attempt, and an HTTPS proxy's denominator is inflated 2x relative to an HTTP one. Preserving this is bug-compatible; fixing it changes every error_rate number users have ever seen. Flagging rather than deciding.
- Exact numeric formatting of `avg_resp_time` in JSON: Python emits `round(x, 2)` (a float; `0.5` serializes as `0.5`, not `0.50`). `(x * 100.0).round() / 100.0` matches for every value that matters, but Python's `round()` is banker's rounding on ties while Rust's `f64::round` is half-away-from-zero. Differs only at exact .xx5 ties in a timing measurement. Confirm nobody diffs JSON output byte-for-byte before ignoring it.
- `Event`'s variant list is drawn from grepping every `proxy.log(...)` call across proxy.py/negotiators.py/checker.py/api.py. It is `#[non_exhaustive]`, but if checker.rs's redesign (hyper-based judge requests) changes which events exist, this enum moves with it — the checker's map should be written against this list and any mismatch reconciled there, not by widening the enum speculatively here.

---

### src/judge.rs

Judge becomes a plain immutable value (url/scheme/host/port/authority/path/ip/marks) with no globals, no `is_working` flag, and no per-judge timeout/verify_ssl/resolver/loop. Probing is `Judge::check(self, ...) -> Option<Judge>` — "working" is proven by *having* a Judge, so the mutable flag is unrepresentable. The class attributes `Judge.available`/`Judge.ev` collapse into two instance types owned by Checker: `JudgeSet` (the three per-scheme Vec<Arc<Judge>>) and `JudgePool` (an `Arc<tokio::sync::OnceCell<JudgeSet>>` + config). The readiness gate is the OnceCell itself — `pool.get().await` runs the probe if nobody has, otherwise waits — which replaces three asyncio.Events, the "set the event for the empty scheme to unblock waiters" hack, and `Judge.clear()` in one move.

**Crates:** `url (2.x) — Url parsing, replaces urlparse + the url.split(host)[-1] path hack`, `reqwest (0.13) — judge endpoint probe is a DIRECT (unproxied) GET; per decision 4 this is scraping-shaped, not checker-shaped`, `tokio (1.x, sync feature) — tokio::sync::OnceCell as the readiness gate; no Notify/watch needed`, `rand (0.9) — IndexedRandom::choose for get_random (ThreadRng is ChaCha12, a CSPRNG, so the Python secrets.choice intent is preserved for free)`, `tracing — log.debug equivalents`, `futures (or tokio::task::JoinSet) — concurrent probe of all judges, replaces asyncio.gather`, `internal: crate::resolver::Resolver, crate::utils::{get_all_ip, get_headers}, crate::errors::ConfigError, crate::negotiators::NegotiatorKind`

| Rust item | ← was | Action | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| `pub struct Judge` | judge.py:12 class Judge | port + redesign | Immutable value after construction+probe. Six Python fields die: `_is_working` (see JudgeSet — existence replaces the flag), `timeout`/`verify_ssl` (moved to JudgeConfig; get_judges set them AFTER __init__ anyway, so the __init__ defaults were dead), `_loop`, `_resolver` (one shared Resolver in JudgePool, not one per judge). `ip` is `IpAddr` not `Option<IpAddr>`: an unresolved judge never becomes a Judge, so the None state is unrepresentable. Python's single `self.host` (= urlparse().netloc, i.e. authority WITH port) is SPLIT into `host` (DNS name / CONNECT target), `port`, and `authority` (the exact netloc string the checker must emit as `Host:` and in the fullpath URI). See deviations — conflating them is a live bug for any judge URL with an explicit port. |
| `pub fn Judge::parse(url: &str) -> Result<Judge, ConfigError>` | judge.py:22 Judge.__init__ | port + redesign | Fallible constructor — Python's __init__ could not fail and deferred every parse defect to a crash at check time. Uses `url::Url` for scheme/host/port/path+query instead of `urlparse` plus `url.split(self.host)[-1]`. Returns `Judge` with `ip` unset — so it actually returns an intermediate; see `JudgeSpec` note in open_questions if the lead wants a separate pre-probe type. Simplest shape that holds: `parse` yields `Judge { ip: PLACEHOLDER }`… rejected. Concrete design: `Judge::parse` returns `JudgeSpec` (url/scheme/host/port/authority/path) and `JudgeSpec::check` yields `Judge` (spec + ip + marks). Two small structs, zero Option fields, no flags. |
| `pub struct JudgeSpec` | new (splits judge.py:22 Judge.__init__ from judge.py:73 Judge.check) | split | The parsed-but-unproven judge. Exists so `Judge` can hold `ip: IpAddr` and `marks: Marks` unconditionally. Python needed `ip=None` + `marks={0,0}` + `_is_working=False` on one object because it had one class for both states. |
| `pub enum JudgeScheme { Http, Https, Smtp }` | judge.py:24 self.scheme = urlparse(url).scheme.upper() (stringly typed) + the "HTTP"/"HTTPS"/"SMTP" dict keys of Judge.available/Judge.ev | write fresh | Closed set of 3, same reasoning as decision 6. Parsed in `Judge::parse`; any other scheme is a ConfigError instead of Python's silent acceptance (`ftp://x` → scheme "FTP" → KeyError deep inside check(), inside an asyncio.gather, killing every other judge probe). Makes the three-key dicts into an array/three fields with no key that can miss. |
| `fn JudgeScheme::for_negotiator(kind: NegotiatorKind) -> JudgeScheme` | judge.py:52-58 the if/elif chain inside Judge.get_random | split | HTTPS→Https, CONNECT:25→Smtp, everything else (HTTP, CONNECT:80, SOCKS4, SOCKS5)→Http. Extracted out of get_random so the mapping is testable and reusable by Checker's "which schemes do I require?" logic (checker.py:82-86 recomputes the same mapping by hand and can drift from it). |
| `pub struct Marks { pub via: usize, pub proxy: usize }` | judge.py:29 self.marks = {"via": 0, "proxy": 0} | port + rename | The anonymity BASELINE: count of the substrings "via"/"proxy" in the lowercased judge body fetched directly. Read by checker.py:369 `_get_anonymity_lvl`. Fields not a HashMap<String, usize>. Substring (not word) counting is preserved deliberately: `str::matches("via").count()` is non-overlapping exactly like Python's `str.count`, and both sides of the comparison count the same way, so "trivial" inflating the count is symmetric and harmless. Not a bug to fix. |
| `impl std::fmt::Display for Judge` | judge.py:39 Judge.__repr__ | port | Display, not Debug — it is used as user-facing text (checker.py:201/229 `proxy.log(f"Selected judge: {judge}")`). Keep the exact `<Judge [SCHEME] host>` format; log-scraping tests and the proxy log lines depend on it. Derive Debug separately. |
| `pub async fn JudgeSpec::check(self, probe: &JudgeProbe) -> Option<Judge>` | judge.py:73 Judge.check | port + redesign | Returns Some(Judge) with ip+marks filled, or None. Replaces Python's mutate-self-and-append-to-a-class-global: no `self.is_working = True`, no `self.available[scheme].append(self)`, no `self.ev[scheme].set()` — the caller (`JudgePool::probe_all`) collects the Somes and builds the JudgeSet. Flow: resolve host (None on ResolveError, as Python); if scheme == Smtp return Some early WITHOUT probing (Python parity — SMTP judges are never HTTP-probed, they only supply host+ip to Connect25Ngtr); else GET url with `get_headers(rv=true)` headers, redirects disabled, and accept iff `status == 200 && real_ext_ips ∩ get_all_ip(body) != ∅ && body.contains(rv)`. Body is lowercased before both the IP scan and the rv/marks scan, as in Python. ALL transport errors → None (see deviations). |
| `pub struct JudgeProbe<'a>` | new (bundles judge.py:95 self._resolver, judge.py:107-113 the per-check TCPConnector/ClientSession, and the real_ext_ips argument) | write fresh | Python built a fresh TCPConnector + ClientSession per judge per check — one TLS/conn stack per judge. One shared reqwest::Client instead (built once in JudgePool with `timeout(cfg.timeout)`, `redirect(Policy::none())`, and `danger_accept_invalid_certs(!cfg.verify_ssl)`). Passed by ref so `check` takes no owned deps and stays trivially concurrent. |
| `pub struct JudgeSet` | judge.py:15 Judge.available (class attribute) | port + redesign | Decision 10: instance state, owned by Checker via JudgePool. Three fields, not a HashMap — JudgeScheme is closed, so a missing key is unrepresentable and `available[scheme]` can never KeyError. `Arc<Judge>` because a judge is shared read-only across every concurrent proxy check; `Vec<Arc<_>>` (not `Arc<Vec<_>>`) so `get_random` hands out a cheap clone that outlives the borrow. Built once, never mutated afterwards → no Mutex/RwLock anywhere. `Judge.clear()` has nothing to clear. |
| `pub fn JudgeSet::get_random(&self, kind: NegotiatorKind) -> Option<Arc<Judge>>` | judge.py:51 Judge.get_random (classmethod) | port + redesign | &self, not a classmethod. `rand::seq::IndexedRandom::choose(&mut rand::rng())` — returns Option, so the empty set yields None instead of Python's `secrets.choice([])` → IndexError. Python only avoids that IndexError because check_judges pre-removes the protocol from `_ngtrs`; the guard lives far from the call site and any future caller re-introduces the panic. Keeping the CSPRNG is free (ThreadRng = ChaCha12), so the SonarCloud-S2245 note at judge.py:59 needs no counterpart. |
| `pub fn JudgeSet::is_empty_for(&self, scheme: JudgeScheme) -> bool` | checker.py:106/112/118 `len(Judge.available["HTTP"]) == 0` | split | The accessor Checker needs to decide which protocols to disable + which warning to emit. The DECISION stays in checker.rs (nojudges warning, disable_protocols, `RuntimeError("Not found judges")`); judge.rs only reports. Python entangled the two inside check_judges, which is why check_judges also had to poke Judge.ev. |
| `pub fn JudgeSet::len(&self) -> usize` | checker.py:99/135 `len(self._judges)` / `len(set(self._judges))` debug logs | port | Total across the three schemes. Note checker.py:135 logs `len(set(self._judges))` while :99 logs `len(self._judges)` — the two differ if the user passes duplicate judge URLs. Rust reports one number from one source of truth. |
| `pub struct JudgePool` | judge.py:16 Judge.ev (class attribute) + checker.py:90 Checker.check_judges + checker.py:172-177 the three `await Judge.ev[...].wait()` calls | port + redesign | This is the answer to the brief's readiness question: NO Notify, NO watch, NO per-scheme events. `tokio::sync::OnceCell::get_or_init` IS the event — the first caller runs `probe_all`, every other caller awaits the same init, and after that `get()` is a non-async-ish cheap hit. The whole JudgeSet lands atomically, which also removes Python's ugly `Judge.ev[X].set()`-for-the-empty-scheme unblock hack (checker.py:111/117/121) — with a OnceCell there is no waiter left stranded when a scheme comes up empty. Arc<JudgePool> is cloned into every concurrent check. |
| `pub async fn JudgePool::get(&self) -> &JudgeSet` | checker.py:172-177 `if self._req_http_proto: await Judge.ev["HTTP"].wait()` (x3) | port + redesign | One await replaces three conditional event waits. The `_req_http_proto`/`_req_https_proto`/`_req_smtp_proto` triple in Checker.__init__ existed ONLY to pick which events to wait on; with one gate they collapse (checker.rs still needs the requested-types set for `_ngtrs`, but not as three bools). `get_or_init(\|\| self.probe_all())`, so a Checker used without an explicit warm-up still works — lazy by construction. |
| `pub async fn JudgePool::warm(self: &Arc<Self>)` | api.py:267 `tasks = [asyncio.create_task(self._checker.check_judges())]` | port + redesign | Just `let _ = self.get().await;`. Preserves Python's overlap of judge probing with provider scraping (the reason the events existed at all) without a second readiness mechanism — the spawned warm-up and any early proxy check converge on the same OnceCell init. |
| `async fn JudgePool::probe_all(&self) -> JudgeSet` | checker.py:94-98 `await asyncio.gather(*[j.check(...) for j in self._judges])` + the `[j for j in self._judges if j.is_working]` filter | port + redesign | Parses JudgeConfig.urls → JudgeSpec (bad URLs are a ConfigError surfaced by JudgePool::new, not here), probes all concurrently (JoinSet / futures::future::join_all), keeps the Somes, partitions by scheme into JudgeSet. Emits the `N judges added. Runtime: …` debug line. Unlike gather-without-return_exceptions, one bad judge cannot abort the others. |
| `pub struct JudgeConfig` | judge.py:152 get_judges(judges=None, timeout=8, verify_ssl=False) parameters | port + redesign | Timeout/verify_ssl live once here instead of being stamped onto every Judge instance (get_judges:168-169 overwrote each judge's __init__ defaults — a constructor parameter that was always ignored). `timeout: Duration` not `timeout: u64` seconds. Wired to CLI --judge (cli.py:167) and Broker(judges=…) (api.py:73/104/253). |
| `pub fn default_judge_urls() -> Vec<&'static str>` | judge.py:153-164 the get_judges default list | port + redesign | MEASURED 2026-07-15, keep only the live ones: http://httpbin.org/get?show_env (200), https://httpbin.org/get?show_env (200), http://azenv.net/ (200, verified echoing REMOTE_ADDR + the rv-bearing User-Agent), http://proxyjudge.us/azenv.php (200), smtp://smtp.gmail.com, smtp://aspmx.l.google.com. DROP three dead entries (see dropped). Judge default list stays a compiled-in constant rather than config data — unlike providers (decision 7) this is 6 URLs with a probe that already fails-soft, and --judge already overrides it. No config file for a constant. |
| `fn build_probe_client(cfg: &JudgeConfig) -> Result<reqwest::Client, ConfigError>` | judge.py:107-116 aiohttp.TCPConnector(ssl=verify_ssl, force_close=True) + ClientTimeout(total=timeout) + session.get(allow_redirects=False) | port + redesign | One Client for all judges, built in JudgePool::new. `.timeout(cfg.timeout)` = aiohttp total timeout; `.redirect(reqwest::redirect::Policy::none())` = allow_redirects=False; `.danger_accept_invalid_certs(!cfg.verify_ssl)` = aiohttp `ssl=False`. `force_close=True` dropped — each judge is probed once per process, connection pooling is irrelevant, and reqwest has no per-request equivalent worth the `pool_max_idle_per_host(0)` cost. Deliberately NOT the research.md recording-ServerCertVerifier: that buys signal for the CHECKER path, and a judge with a bad cert is simply a judge we don't use. |
| `Judge.clear` | judge.py:64 Judge.clear (classmethod), called at checker.py:47 | drop | Nothing to clear. It existed solely to un-poison the class-level `available`/`ev` between Broker instances (decision 10). With JudgeSet/JudgePool owned by Checker, a second Broker gets a fresh pool by construction — and `Judge.ev[...].clear()` at checker.py:69-71 racing an in-flight check from a previous Broker was a real bug (see deviations). |
| `Judge::is_working / is_working setter` | judge.py:28/43-49 self._is_working + @property + @is_working.setter | drop | A getter/setter pair over a plain bool with no invariant. Replaced by the type: `check` returns `Option<Judge>`, JudgeSet only ever contains working judges. Removes checker.py:98's `[j for j in self._judges if j.is_working]` filter pass entirely. |

<details><summary><b>Proposed signatures</b></summary>

```rust
// pub struct Judge  ← judge.py:12 class Judge
pub struct Judge { pub url: Url, pub scheme: JudgeScheme, pub host: String, pub port: u16, pub authority: String, pub path: String, pub ip: IpAddr, pub marks: Marks }
// pub fn Judge::parse(url: &str) -> Result<Judge, ConfigError>  ← judge.py:22 Judge.__init__
pub fn parse(url: &str) -> Result<Judge, ConfigError>
// pub struct JudgeSpec  ← new (splits judge.py:22 Judge.__init__ from judge.py:73 Judge.check)
pub struct JudgeSpec { url: Url, scheme: JudgeScheme, host: String, port: u16, authority: String, path: String }
// pub enum JudgeScheme { Http, Https, Smtp }  ← judge.py:24 self.scheme = urlparse(url).scheme.upper() (stringly typed) + the "HTTP"/"HTTPS"/"SMTP" dict keys of Judge.available/Judge.ev
#[derive(Copy, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Hash, Debug)] pub enum JudgeScheme { Http, Https, Smtp }
// fn JudgeScheme::for_negotiator(kind: NegotiatorKind) -> JudgeScheme  ← judge.py:52-58 the if/elif chain inside Judge.get_random
fn for_negotiator(kind: NegotiatorKind) -> JudgeScheme
// impl std::fmt::Display for Judge  ← judge.py:39 Judge.__repr__
fn fmt(&self, f: &mut Formatter) -> fmt::Result  // "<Judge [HTTP] azenv.net>"
// pub async fn JudgeSpec::check(self, probe: &JudgeProbe) -> Option<Judge>  ← judge.py:73 Judge.check
pub async fn check(self, probe: &JudgeProbe) -> Option<Judge>
// pub struct JudgeProbe<'a>  ← new (bundles judge.py:95 self._resolver, judge.py:107-113 the per-check TCPConnector/ClientSession, and the real_ext_ips argument)
pub struct JudgeProbe<'a> { client: &'a reqwest::Client, resolver: &'a Resolver, real_ext_ips: &'a HashSet<IpAddr> }
// pub struct JudgeSet  ← judge.py:15 Judge.available (class attribute)
pub struct JudgeSet { http: Vec<Arc<Judge>>, https: Vec<Arc<Judge>>, smtp: Vec<Arc<Judge>> }
// pub fn JudgeSet::get_random(&self, kind: NegotiatorKind) -> Option<Arc<Judge>>  ← judge.py:51 Judge.get_random (classmethod)
pub fn get_random(&self, kind: NegotiatorKind) -> Option<Arc<Judge>>
// pub fn JudgeSet::is_empty_for(&self, scheme: JudgeScheme) -> bool  ← checker.py:106/112/118 `len(Judge.available["HTTP"]) == 0`
pub fn is_empty_for(&self, scheme: JudgeScheme) -> bool
// pub struct JudgePool  ← judge.py:16 Judge.ev (class attribute) + checker.py:90 Checker.check_judges + checker.py:172-177 the three `await Judge.ev[...].wait()` calls
pub struct JudgePool { cell: tokio::sync::OnceCell<JudgeSet>, cfg: JudgeConfig, client: reqwest::Client, resolver: Arc<Resolver>, real_ext_ips: HashSet<IpAddr> }  // held as Arc<JudgePool> by Checker
// pub async fn JudgePool::get(&self) -> &JudgeSet  ← checker.py:172-177 `if self._req_http_proto: await Judge.ev["HTTP"].wait()` (x3)
pub async fn get(&self) -> &JudgeSet
// pub async fn JudgePool::warm(self: &Arc<Self>)  ← api.py:267 `tasks = [asyncio.create_task(self._checker.check_judges())]`
pub async fn warm(self: &Arc<Self>)  // callers: tokio::spawn({ let p = pool.clone(); async move { p.warm().await } })
// async fn JudgePool::probe_all(&self) -> JudgeSet  ← checker.py:94-98 `await asyncio.gather(*[j.check(...) for j in self._judges])` + the `[j for j in self._judges if j.is_working]` filter
async fn probe_all(&self) -> JudgeSet
// pub struct JudgeConfig  ← judge.py:152 get_judges(judges=None, timeout=8, verify_ssl=False) parameters
pub struct JudgeConfig { pub urls: Vec<String>, pub timeout: Duration, pub verify_ssl: bool }  // Default: urls = default_judge_urls(), timeout = 8s, verify_ssl = false
// fn build_probe_client(cfg: &JudgeConfig) -> Result<reqwest::Client, ConfigError>  ← judge.py:107-116 aiohttp.TCPConnector(ssl=verify_ssl, force_close=True) + ClientTimeout(total=timeout) + session.get(allow_redirects=False)
fn build_probe_client(cfg: &JudgeConfig) -> Result<reqwest::Client, ConfigError>
```
</details>

**Open questions**

- HTTPS judging currently rests on ONE endpoint. MEASURED 2026-07-15: of the default list, only httpbin.org serves the `https://` scheme — azenv.net:443 and proxyjudge.us:443 refuse connections, proxy-listen.de returns 503. If httpbin.org is down or rate-limits us, `JudgeSet::is_empty_for(Https)` is true and HTTPS proxy checking silently disables itself (with a warning) for the whole run. Do we want to research and add a second HTTPS judge before shipping, or accept the single point of failure with a louder warning?
- Where does the `check_judges` failure policy live? Python's check_judges both (a) warns `Not found judges for the [X] protocol` and disables protocols, and (b) raises `RuntimeError("Not found judges")` when nothing at all verified. I have judge.rs expose `is_empty_for`/`len` and put the policy in checker.rs. Confirm — alternative is a `JudgePool::get()` that returns `Result<&JudgeSet, FatalError>` and refuses to hand back a fully-empty set (per decision 11 that is a fatal error: no network / bad config, not a per-proxy failure).
- `danger_accept_invalid_certs(!verify_ssl)` for the judge probe vs. research.md's recommended custom recording `ServerCertVerifier`. I chose the blunt flag: a judge with a bad cert is a judge we skip, there is no anonymity signal to salvage, and it keeps judge.rs on reqwest instead of dragging rustls internals into it. Confirm that the recording verifier is checker-only.
- Should JudgeConfig.urls stay a compiled-in default (`default_judge_urls()`) or join the data-driven providers config from decision 7? I argue compiled-in: 6 URLs, fail-soft probe, already overridable via --judge / Broker(judges=…), whereas a dead provider is a silent yield-zero. Flagging because the same 'dead endpoint requires a recompile' argument technically applies.
- Judge marks (the anonymity baseline) are captured from a GET, but Checker can be configured with `post=True` (checker.py:_method) and will then compare against a POST response body. Judge probing has no POST mode in Python either, so this is pre-existing; I preserved it. Worth fixing (probe with the configured method) or leave the asymmetry alone?

---

### src/checker.rs

The Rust checker collapses Python's `Checker.__init__` + `check_judges()` + three `asyncio.Event` gates into a single fallible async constructor (`Checker::probe`) that returns a `Checker` only once a judge baseline exists — the event dance and the `Judge` class-level globals disappear entirely, which is what locked decision #10 buys. `check(&self, proxy: &mut Proxy) -> CheckOutcome` stays sequential per protocol, but iterates a fixed `[NegotiatorKind; 6]` in declaration order instead of a hash-ordered Python set, and returns an outcome enum instead of `bool` + a side-effect on `proxy.is_working`. The socket no longer lives on `Proxy`: each attempt opens its own `TcpStream`, hands it to a negotiator, wraps it in `TokioIo` for a hyper 1.x handshake, and drops it — `Proxy` stays pure data (types, stats, runtimes) so it can be yielded across the `ProxyStream` boundary.

**Crates:** `tokio (net, time, sync, macros)`, `hyper 1.10 (client, http1)`, `hyper-util 0.1 (rt::TokioIo)`, `http 1`, `http-body-util (Full, BodyExt::collect)`, `bytes`, `tokio-socks 0.5.3 (SOCKS4/5 negotiation, 23 reply-code error variants)`, `tokio-rustls 0.26 + rustls 0.23 (HTTPS negotiator TLS upgrade, custom ServerCertVerifier)`, `flate2 (gzip/deflate response bodies; replaces Python zlib)`, `rand 0.9 (judge selection; IndexedRandom::choose)`, `futures (join_all over concurrent judge probes / DNSBL queries)`, `thiserror`, `tracing`, `hickory-resolver 0.26 (DNSBL A-record lookups, via crate Resolver)`, `reqwest 0.13 (transitively: judge baseline probe in judge.rs is a direct, non-proxied GET)`, `url`

| Rust item | ← was | Action | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| `pub struct Checker` | checker.py:Checker | port + redesign | Judges are owned INSTANCE state (locked #10), not `Judge.available` class attrs. `protocols` is an ordered Vec, not a set — this is where Python's nondeterministic dict/set iteration is killed. `types` is a BTreeMap so the requested-type filter is order-stable too. All methods take `&self` (Python only mutates `self._judges` inside `check_judges`, which is now folded into the constructor), so a single `Arc<Checker>` is shared by all worker tasks behind the `tokio::sync::Semaphore` of locked #9. |
| `pub struct CheckerBuilder` | checker.py:Checker.__init__ (13 params, 2 of them legacy) | port + redesign | Builder per the many-optional-fields rule; Python's __init__ is 9 optionals plus a keyword-only backward-compat arg. `types` is required at `new()` — api.py already raises ValueError('`types` is required'), so make it non-optional in the type system rather than a runtime check. Note `types` empty is NOT a legal state in Rust; Python's `not types` fallback (`self._ngtrs = {proto for proto in types or NGTRS}`) is unreachable from api.py. |
| `Checker::probe` | checker.py:Checker.__init__ + checker.py:Checker.check_judges | merge | MERGE of the constructor and `check_judges()`. Python spawns `check_judges()` as a task concurrent with `_grab`, and every `check()` blocks on `Judge.ev[...]` until it lands — three asyncio.Events, a `Judge.clear()` call, and a `# TODO: need refactoring` comment exist solely to synchronize that. Making judge probing the async constructor means `Checker::check` is UNCONSTRUCTIBLE before the baseline exists: the ordering constraint in the brief becomes a type-system fact and all three Events + `Judge.clear()` + the `_req_*_proto` flags evaporate. Broker can still overlap provider grabbing with `probe()` — it just awaits `probe()` before spawning check workers. Returns `Err(Error::NoJudges)` where Python raises `RuntimeError('Not found judges')`. |
| `Checker::check` | checker.py:Checker.check | port + redesign | Returns `CheckOutcome` instead of `bool` + mutating `proxy.is_working` as a side channel. Order preserved: DNSBL gate → protocol loop (SEQUENTIAL, reusing nothing but the Proxy stats handle) → `any(results)` → `types_passed`. The three `await Judge.ev[...].wait()` calls are gone (see `Checker::probe`). Protocol set = `proxy.expected_types ∩ self.protocols` (Python: `proxy.expected_types & self._ngtrs`), computed as a filtered iterator over the ordered Vec so intersection does not reintroduce hash order. |
| `pub enum CheckOutcome` | new (replaces checker.py:Checker.check's bool return + `proxy.is_working = working`) | write fresh | Python conflates three distinct rejections into `return False`, and leaves `proxy.is_working = True` set even when `_types_passed` rejects the proxy (checker.py:193 runs before checker.py:195) — a caller reading `proxy.is_working` sees a lie. The enum makes the reason legible to Broker's per-outcome counters (which is what api.py's `_on_check` loop and `show_stats` actually want) and lets `is_working` be set exactly once, only on `Working`. Not an `Err`: per locked #8 a failed proxy is a non-result, not an error. |
| `Checker::check_proto` | checker.py:Checker._check + checker.py:Checker._check_conn_25 | merge | MERGE: `_check` and `_check_conn_25` are the same function modulo the test request. Both pick ONE judge before the loop (same judge for all retries — preserved), then run the identical retry policy: retry on timeout, `break` on every other ProxyError, `break` on success. Body: select judge → `for _ in 0..max_tries { match self.attempt(..).await { Err(ProxyError::Timeout) => continue, Err(_) => break, Ok(lvl) => { proxy.set_type(ngtr, lvl); return true } } }`. The CONNECT:25 divergence (no test request, level always None) becomes one `if ngtr == Connect25` inside `attempt`. Python's `finally: proxy.close()` has no analogue — the connection is a local that drops. |
| `Checker::attempt` | checker.py:Checker._check body (lines 233-238) + Checker._check_conn_25 body (lines 205-207) | port + redesign | ONE attempt: `TcpStream::connect((proxy.host, proxy.port))` under `timeout` → `negotiators::negotiate(ngtr, stream, judge)` → for CONNECT:25 return `Ok(None)` right there → otherwise `TokioIo::new(stream)` + `hyper::client::conn::http1::handshake` + `send_request` under `timeout` → collect body → decompress → `response_is_correct` → if `ngtr.check_anon_lvl()` compute `anonymity_level`, else `None`. Replaces Python's `proxy.connect()/send()/recv()/close()` handle protocol wholesale — see the Proxy-owns-no-socket deviation. `conn` future is spawned per hyper's documented shape and dropped with the attempt. Records phase timings into `proxy` (Python got these from `proxy.log(msg, stime)`). |
| `Checker::types_passed` | checker.py:Checker._types_passed | port | Semantics preserved verbatim, including the asymmetry that reads like a bug but isn't: NON-strict returns true on the FIRST proto whose level matches (or whose proto has no level constraint) and leaves unrequested protos in `proxy.types`; STRICT removes every non-matching proto and returns true iff anything survives. `self.types.is_empty()` short-circuit dropped — the builder makes it unrepresentable. Python's `proxy.types.copy()` guard against mutation-during-iteration is unnecessary in Rust (retain/drain); use `BTreeMap::retain` in the strict path. |
| `Checker::in_dnsbl` | checker.py:Checker._in_DNSBL | port + redesign | Fires all zone queries concurrently (`futures::future::join_all`, as Python's `asyncio.gather`) and returns true iff at least one query returns a successful A answer. Python's predicate is `any(r for r in responses if not isinstance(r, ResolveError))` over `gather(return_exceptions=True)` — so ANY non-ResolveError exception (timeout, servfail wrapped differently, a bug in Resolver) is counted as 'listed' and silently discards the proxy. Rust: `matches!(r, Ok(answer)) && !answer.is_empty()`. Non-resolve errors are logged at debug and treated as not-listed. See deviations. |
| `fn dnsbl_query_name` | checker.py:Checker._in_DNSBL line 156 (`'.'.join(reversed(host.split('.')))`) | port + redesign | Extracted as a free fn so it is unit-testable without a resolver. IPv4: reversed octets + zone (identical to Python). IPv6: RFC 5782 §2.4 reversed-nibble form (`x.x.x…ip6-style` + zone) — Python's naive dot-split on an IPv6 literal produces the address back unchanged (no dots to reverse), yielding a garbage query that always ResolveErrors, i.e. IPv6 proxies silently skip DNSBL. This fork already supports IPv6 proxies (utils.py `IPv6BracketedPortPattern`, negotiators.py ATYP=0x04), so the gap is real. |
| `fn test_request` | checker.py:_request (+ utils.py:get_headers(rv=True)) | port + redesign | Builds a typed `http::Request` instead of formatting raw bytes with `'{method} {path} HTTP/1.1\r\n...'.format()`. Returns the rv marker alongside. `use_full_path` (only HttpNgtr) selects absolute-form URI `http://host/path` vs origin-form `/path` — hyper serializes the Uri as-is and explicitly does not validate the form (research §HTTP stack), which is exactly what the HTTP-proxy case needs. `Connection: close` preserved. `Content-Length` is set by http-body-util from `Full<Bytes>`, so Python's unconditional `hdrs['Content-Length'] = len(data)` on GET is dropped. `Content-Type: application/octet-stream` on POST preserved. Empty body both ways (Python's `data` is always ''). |
| `Checker::send_test_request` | checker.py:_send_test_request | port + redesign | hyper gives a parsed `Response<Incoming>`; `status != 200 -> ProxyError::BadStatus` preserved. Python's `resp.split(b'\r\n\r\n', maxsplit=1)` → ValueError → BadResponseError becomes hyper's own parse error → `ProxyError::BadResponse`. `utils.get_status_code(resp, 9, 12)` (byte-slice `int(resp[9:12])`, returning 400 on garbage) is dropped — hyper parses the status line. The `finally:` debug log of the full raw response is preserved as `tracing::debug!`. |
| `fn decompress_body` | checker.py:_decompress_content | port + redesign | Dispatch on `Content-Encoding`: gzip → `flate2::read::GzDecoder`, deflate → `flate2::read::ZlibDecoder` (Python used `zlib.MAX_WBITS\|32`, auto-detect gzip-or-zlib, so it never actually distinguished; keep the auto behavior by falling back Gz→Zlib on error to stay bug-for-bug on servers that mislabel). Decompression failure → empty String (matches Python's `except zlib.error: content = b''`). Python's manual chunk-frame strip (`b''.join(content.split(b'\r\n')[1::2])`) is DELETED — hyper de-chunks before we see the body. `String::from_utf8_lossy` == Python's `.decode('utf-8','ignore')`. |
| `fn response_is_correct` | checker.py:_check_test_response | port | All four conjuncts preserved: rv marker echoed, at least one IP literal found (`utils::get_all_ip`), the constant Referer echoed, the constant Cookie echoed. Python re-calls `get_headers()` twice here purely to read those two CONSTANTS out of the dict (each call burns a fresh CSPRNG draw for an rv it discards) — replaced by `const REFERER` / `const COOKIE` in utils.rs. Takes `&str` + `&str` and does not touch `proxy`; the two `proxy.log` calls become `tracing::debug!` at the call site so this is a pure, unit-testable predicate. |
| `fn anonymity_level` | checker.py:_get_anonymity_lvl | port + redesign | Pure free fn, the single most test-worthy thing in the module. Order preserved exactly: lowercase body → `get_all_ip` → if `real_ext_ips ∩ found_ips` non-empty → Transparent; elif `body.matches("via").count() > judge.marks.via \|\| body.matches("proxy").count() > judge.marks.proxy` → Anonymous; else High. NOTE the brief says via-count only — the SOURCE also ORs the `proxy` mark count (checker.py:369-371); source wins. `real_ext_ips` is `HashSet<IpAddr>` so `canonicalize_ip` is structural (parse once at the Broker boundary) rather than a per-call normalize pass; the legacy `isinstance(real_ext_ips, str)` branch and the `canonicalize_ip(ip) or ip` fallback are unrepresentable and dropped. |
| `pub enum Anonymity` | checker.py:_get_anonymity_lvl string literals 'Transparent'/'Anonymous'/'High' | port + redesign | Stringly-typed levels become an enum; `Ord` gives the requested-level `BTreeSet` and the `--types HTTP:Anonymous,High` CLI filter a total order for free. `Display` reproduces the exact Python strings (proxy repr / as_json are wire-visible). Python's `lvl[:4]` truncation in the debug log ('Tran'/'Anon'/'High') is cosmetic — reproduce or not, no caller depends on it. `Option<Anonymity>` carries Python's `proxy.types[name] = None` for non-HTTP protocols. |
| `struct JudgePool` | judge.py:Judge.available (class attr) + judge.py:Judge.ev (class attr) + checker.py:Checker.check_judges lines 98-137 | port + redesign | Locked #10 made concrete: the three-list registry that Python hangs off the `Judge` CLASS becomes a plain struct owned by `Checker`. `Judge.clear()` exists ONLY because that state is global — it is dropped, and with it the real bug that two concurrent `Broker`s stomp each other's judge lists. Three `Vec`s, not a `HashMap<Scheme, Vec<Judge>>`: the key set is closed and three fields cost nothing. |
| `JudgePool::probe` | checker.py:Checker.check_judges lines 92-101 | port | `futures::future::join_all` over `Judge::check` (judge.py:Judge.check lives in src/judge.rs), then bucket the working ones by scheme. The `stime`/elapsed debug log is preserved as `tracing::debug!`. `set(self._judges)` in Python's final log is a dedupe-for-counting artifact over a list that contains a literal duplicate URL in the default set — see open questions. |
| `JudgePool::prune_protocols` | checker.py:Checker.check_judges lines 103-133 | port + redesign | Returns the disabled kinds for the warning. No HTTP judges → disable Http, Connect80, Socks4, Socks5. No HTTPS judges → disable Https. No SMTP judges → disable **Connect25**. THAT LAST ONE IS THE BUG FIX: Python appends the literal `'SMTP'` to `disable_protocols` and then does `if proto in self._ngtrs: self._ngtrs.remove(proto)` — but `_ngtrs` holds NEGOTIATOR names, and there is no negotiator called `'SMTP'` (it's `'CONNECT:25'`). So the removal silently no-ops and a `--types CONNECT:25` run with unreachable SMTP judges reaches `_check_conn_25` → `Judge.get_random('CONNECT:25')` → `secrets.choice([])` → **IndexError out of `check()`**. Typing the disable list as `NegotiatorKind` makes the class of bug unrepresentable. The three `_req_*_proto` flags and the three `Judge.ev[...].set()` calls that guard 'coroutines already waiting' are dropped with the events. |
| `JudgePool::random` | judge.py:Judge.get_random (classmethod) | port + redesign | Instance method, returns `Option` instead of raising IndexError on an empty list. Callers can only reach it for a kind that survived `prune_protocols`, so `Option` is belt-and-braces — log and return false rather than panic. `secrets.choice` → `rand::seq::IndexedRandom::choose(&mut rand::rng())`; the Python comment says outright that secrets was chosen to silence SonarCloud S2245 and the selection is not security-sensitive. |
| `enum JudgeScheme` | judge.py:Judge.get_random's proto→scheme mapping (lines 53-58) + judge.py:Judge.scheme string | port + redesign | The scheme mapping moves onto the negotiator as `NegotiatorKind::judge_scheme(self) -> JudgeScheme` — `Https => Https`, `Connect25 => Smtp`, everything else => `Http` (verbatim Python). Putting it on the enum makes it exhaustive-checked; Python's `else: scheme = 'HTTP'` silently absorbs typos. |
| `NegotiatorKind::ALL` | negotiators.py:NGTRS dict (insertion order HTTP, HTTPS, SOCKS4, SOCKS5, CONNECT:80, CONNECT:25) | port + redesign | Lives in negotiators.rs (locked #6) but named here because it is the source of the checker's protocol ORDER. Python's `self._ngtrs = {proto for proto in types or NGTRS}` builds a **set** of strings, so iteration order in `check()` is Python's hash order over str — PYTHONHASHSEED-randomized, i.e. a different protocol order every process. `Checker.protocols` is built by filtering `ALL` in this fixed order, so the order is the NGTRS declaration order, always. Locked-decision requirement; also makes the sequential check reproducible for tests. |
| `Checker::protocols_for` | checker.py:Checker.check lines 179-182 | port | `self.protocols.iter().copied().filter(\|k\| proxy.expected_types.is_empty() \|\| proxy.expected_types.contains(k))`. Preserves Python's `proxy.expected_types & self._ngtrs` with the empty-expected fallback, but the ordering comes from `self.protocols` (ordered) rather than from set intersection. |
| `NegotiatorKind::check_anon_lvl / NegotiatorKind::use_full_path` | negotiators.py:BaseNegotiator.check_anon_lvl / .use_full_path class attrs (True only on HttpNgtr) | port + redesign | Declared in negotiators.rs; named here because `Checker::attempt` and `test_request` are the only consumers. Two `matches!(self, Http)` one-liners — no trait, no per-kind struct (locked #6). Consequence preserved: anonymity is classified for HTTP only; every other protocol stores `None`. |
| `Error::NoJudges` | checker.py:Checker.check_judges line 137 (`raise RuntimeError('Not found judges')`) | port + redesign | Fatal-error enum (locked #11, research §Errors). Surfaces from `Checker::probe`, i.e. out of `Broker::find` before any proxy work starts, instead of from inside a spawned task where Python's `asyncio.gather` may report it late or not at all. |
| `ProxyError (consumed, not defined here)` | errors.py:ProxyConnError/ProxyRecvError/ProxySendError/ProxyTimeoutError/ProxyEmptyRecvError/BadStatusError/BadResponseError | port + redesign | Retry policy maps 1:1 onto the enum: `ProxyError::Timeout` → `continue` (Python's `except ProxyTimeoutError: continue`); every other variant → `break` (Python's 6-exception bulk catch, checker.py:210-218). The `#[error("...")]` strings ARE the old `errmsg` values, keeping `proxy.stat['errors']` histogram keys wire-compatible. |
| `tracing::warn! in Checker::probe` | checker.py:Checker.check_judges lines 127-133 (`warnings.warn(..., UserWarning)`) | port + redesign | Python's message is also broken: `nojudges` never gets 'SMTP' appended (line 118-121 skips it) while `disable_protocols` does, so the missing-SMTP case prints 'Not found judges for the [] protocol. Checking proxy on protocols [\'SMTP\'] is disabled.' Rust logs the actual disabled `NegotiatorKind` list and the actual missing schemes. |

<details><summary><b>Proposed signatures</b></summary>

```rust
// pub struct Checker  ← checker.py:Checker
pub struct Checker { judges: JudgePool, method: http::Method, max_tries: u8, timeout: Duration, verify_ssl: bool, strict: bool, dnsbl: Vec<String>, real_ext_ips: HashSet<IpAddr>, types: BTreeMap<NegotiatorKind, BTreeSet<Anonymity>>, protocols: Vec<NegotiatorKind>, resolver: Arc<Resolver> }
// pub struct CheckerBuilder  ← checker.py:Checker.__init__ (13 params, 2 of them legacy)
impl CheckerBuilder { pub fn new(types: impl IntoIterator<Item=(NegotiatorKind, BTreeSet<Anonymity>)>) -> Self; pub fn judges(self, urls: Vec<Url>) -> Self; pub fn max_tries(self, n: u8) -> Self; pub fn timeout(self, d: Duration) -> Self; pub fn verify_ssl(self, b: bool) -> Self; pub fn strict(self, b: bool) -> Self; pub fn post(self, b: bool) -> Self; pub fn dnsbl(self, zones: Vec<String>) -> Self; pub fn real_ext_ips(self, ips: HashSet<IpAddr>) -> Self; pub async fn probe(self, resolver: Arc<Resolver>) -> Result<Checker, Error> }
// Checker::probe  ← checker.py:Checker.__init__ + checker.py:Checker.check_judges
async fn probe(self, resolver: Arc<Resolver>) -> Result<Checker, Error>
// Checker::check  ← checker.py:Checker.check
pub async fn check(&self, proxy: &mut Proxy) -> CheckOutcome
// pub enum CheckOutcome  ← new (replaces checker.py:Checker.check's bool return + `proxy.is_working = working`)
#[non_exhaustive] pub enum CheckOutcome { Working, DnsblListed, NoProtocolWorked, TypesMismatch }
// Checker::check_proto  ← checker.py:Checker._check + checker.py:Checker._check_conn_25
async fn check_proto(&self, proxy: &mut Proxy, ngtr: NegotiatorKind) -> bool
// Checker::attempt  ← checker.py:Checker._check body (lines 233-238) + Checker._check_conn_25 body (lines 205-207)
async fn attempt(&self, proxy: &mut Proxy, ngtr: NegotiatorKind, judge: &Judge) -> Result<Option<Anonymity>, ProxyError>
// Checker::types_passed  ← checker.py:Checker._types_passed
fn types_passed(&self, proxy: &mut Proxy) -> bool
// Checker::in_dnsbl  ← checker.py:Checker._in_DNSBL
async fn in_dnsbl(&self, host: IpAddr) -> bool
// fn dnsbl_query_name  ← checker.py:Checker._in_DNSBL line 156 (`'.'.join(reversed(host.split('.')))`)
fn dnsbl_query_name(ip: IpAddr, zone: &str) -> String
// fn test_request  ← checker.py:_request (+ utils.py:get_headers(rv=True))
fn test_request(method: &http::Method, judge: &Judge, use_full_path: bool) -> (http::Request<Full<Bytes>>, String)
// Checker::send_test_request  ← checker.py:_send_test_request
async fn send_test_request(&self, sender: &mut SendRequest<Full<Bytes>>, judge: &Judge, ngtr: NegotiatorKind) -> Result<(http::HeaderMap, Bytes, String), ProxyError>
// fn decompress_body  ← checker.py:_decompress_content
fn decompress_body(headers: &http::HeaderMap, body: Bytes) -> String
// fn response_is_correct  ← checker.py:_check_test_response
fn response_is_correct(body: &str, rv: &str) -> bool
// fn anonymity_level  ← checker.py:_get_anonymity_lvl
fn anonymity_level(real_ext_ips: &HashSet<IpAddr>, judge: &Judge, body: &str) -> Anonymity
// pub enum Anonymity  ← checker.py:_get_anonymity_lvl string literals 'Transparent'/'Anonymous'/'High'
#[derive(Copy, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, Hash)] pub enum Anonymity { Transparent, Anonymous, High }
// struct JudgePool  ← judge.py:Judge.available (class attr) + judge.py:Judge.ev (class attr) + checker.py:Checker.check_judges lines 98-137
struct JudgePool { http: Vec<Judge>, https: Vec<Judge>, smtp: Vec<Judge> }
// JudgePool::probe  ← checker.py:Checker.check_judges lines 92-101

// JudgePool::prune_protocols  ← checker.py:Checker.check_judges lines 103-133

fn random(&self, scheme: JudgeScheme) -> Option<&Judge>
// enum JudgeScheme  ← judge.py:Judge.get_random's proto→scheme mapping (lines 53-58) + judge.py:Judge.scheme string
#[derive(Copy, Clone, PartialEq, Eq)] enum JudgeScheme { Http, Https, Smtp }

impl NegotiatorKind { pub const ALL: [NegotiatorKind; 6] = [Http, Https, Socks4, Socks5, Connect80, Connect25]; }
// Checker::protocols_for  ← checker.py:Checker.check lines 179-182
fn protocols_for<'a>(&'a self, proxy: &'a Proxy) -> impl Iterator<Item = NegotiatorKind> + 'a

impl NegotiatorKind { fn check_anon_lvl(self) -> bool; fn use_full_path(self) -> bool }
```
