```rust
#[error("no judges reachable; cannot verify anonymity")] NoJudges
// ProxyError (consumed, not defined here)  ← errors.py:ProxyConnError/ProxyRecvError/ProxySendError/ProxyTimeoutError/ProxyEmptyRecvError/BadStatusError/BadResponseError
Result<_, ProxyError> from errors.rs; ProxyError: Copy + Eq + Hash
// tracing::warn! in Checker::probe  ← checker.py:Checker.check_judges lines 127-133 (`warnings.warn(..., UserWarning)`)
tracing::warn!(?disabled, "no judges for {missing:?}; disabling these protocols")
```
</details>

**Open questions**

- Timeout granularity. Python applies `self._timeout` independently to `connect()` and to EVERY `recv()`, so one attempt's worst case is roughly 3-4x timeout (connect + negotiate recv + response recv), unbounded in the number of recvs for a slow drip. Rust proposal: one `tokio::time::timeout` per phase (connect / negotiate / request+body), which is close but not identical, OR one budget for the whole attempt (cleaner, stricter, changes which proxies pass at the margin). Need a call.
- Where do per-attempt runtimes and the `proxy.get_log()` transcript get recorded now that `Proxy` holds no socket? Python's `proxy.log(msg, stime)` is the single place `_runtimes` (→ `avg_resp_time`) and `stat['errors']` (→ `error_rate`) are populated, and it is called from inside connect/send/recv. If those move into the checker, the checker owns the instrumentation and `Proxy` exposes `record_runtime`/`record_error`. Is `get_log()` (the human-readable per-proxy transcript) worth porting at all, or is `tracing` with a `host:port` span enough? Leaning: drop `get_log`, keep the numeric stats. This is really a proxy.rs decision the checker forces.
- Is `post=True` worth porting? It flips the judge request to POST with an EMPTY body and `Content-Type: application/octet-stream`. Nothing in the repo tests it, most azenv-style judges are GET-only, and a POST with no body tests nothing a GET doesn't. Candidate for the dropped list if the lead agrees.
- The default judge list (judge.py:get_judges) contains a literal duplicate (`http://www.proxy-listen.de/azenv.php` at both index 5 and 9, differing only in `www.`) plus almost certainly dead entries (`proxyfire.net/fastenv`, `proxyjudge.us`). Same problem as the dead-providers finding (locked #7) but unmeasured for judges. Probe the default judge list before porting it — a dead judge is a slow startup and a skewed `marks` baseline. Belongs to src/judge.rs but blocks `JudgePool::probe`'s default.
- Ordering of `proxy.types` for display. Python sorts by `(len(tp), tp[-1])` in `__repr__`/`as_json`, an arbitrary key that happens to produce HTTP, HTTPS, SOCKS4, SOCKS5, CONNECT:25, CONNECT:80. If `Proxy.types` is a `BTreeMap<NegotiatorKind, Option<Anonymity>>` keyed by the enum's declaration order, output order changes (CONNECT:80 before CONNECT:25). Wire-visible in `as_json`. Match the Python sort key, or accept the enum order?
- SMTP judges are never actually probed — `Judge.check` returns early after a successful DNS resolve and marks itself working (judge.py:99-103), so `marks` stays {via:0, proxy:0} and no baseline exists. `_check_conn_25` correspondingly sends no test request; a CONNECT:25 'success' means only that the proxy returned HTTP 200 to `CONNECT host:25` and then a 220 banner. Port as-is (honest parity) or actually verify the SMTP judge? Port as-is is my recommendation; recording it because 'CONNECT:25 is checked' means much less than it sounds.

---

### src/broker.rs

In Python, `Broker` is a stateful god-object: it holds per-run state (`_limit`, `_countries`, `_checker`, `_all_tasks`, `unique_proxies`), spawns fire-and-forget tasks, and delivers results out-of-band into a user-supplied `asyncio.Queue` terminated by a `None` poison pill. In Rust it splits in two: `Broker` becomes immutable, cheaply-cloneable *configuration* (`Arc<BrokerInner>`: resolver, HTTP client, providers, judge config, limits), and every call to `find()`/`grab()`/`serve()` allocates a private `Run` that owns all per-run mutable state (dedup set, semaphore, limit counter, stats, sender). `find(query) -> Result<ProxyStream, Error>` yields a named `Stream<Item = Proxy>` backed by a bounded mpsc and a `JoinSet` that aborts on drop — which deletes `stop()`, `_done()`, `_all_tasks`, the SIGINT plumbing, and the `None` sentinel in one move. Fatal conditions (no providers, no types, no judges) surface once, up front, in the `Err`; per-proxy failures only ever move counters in `Stats`.

**Crates:** `tokio (features: rt, sync, time, macros, net)`, `futures-core (Stream trait for the impl)`, `futures-util (stream::iter / buffer_unordered / StreamExt in grab_loop)`, `tracing`, `thiserror (via crate::errors)`, `reqwest 0.13 (the shared Client built in BrokerBuilder::build and handed to providers)`, `hickory-resolver 0.26 (transitively, via crate::resolver::Resolver — build() is fallible, error type NetError)`, `maxminddb 0.29 (transitively, via crate::geo::GeoDb, feature-gated)`, `crate-internal: crate::proxy::{Proxy, Proto}, crate::checker::{Checker, CheckOutcome}, crate::providers::{Provider, PROVIDERS}, crate::judge::JudgeSpec, crate::resolver::Resolver, crate::parse::find_addrs, crate::errors::{Error, ProxyError}, crate::server::{ServeConfig, ServerHandle} (feature = "server"), crate::geo::{GeoDb, Country} (feature = "geo")`

| Rust item | ← was | Action | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| `pub struct Broker` | api.py:Broker (the __init__ state block, lines 81-126) | port + redesign | Newtype over Arc so spawned tasks can hold 'static config without cloning the provider list or re-building the resolver/HTTP client. Python's Broker carries BOTH config and per-run state; every mutable field (`_limit`, `_countries`, `_checker`, `_all_tasks`, `unique_proxies`, `_server`) moves out to `Run`. Consequence: two concurrent `find()` calls on one Broker no longer stomp each other's limit/countries (they do in Python — see deviations). |
| `struct BrokerInner` | new (extracted from api.py:Broker.__init__) | write fresh | All immutable after `build()`. `reqwest::Client` is built once here and shared with every provider fetch (Python builds an aiohttp session per provider). `verify_ssl` maps to the custom rustls `ServerCertVerifier` decision in research.md §HTTP stack, not to a bool passed down per-connection. |
| `pub struct BrokerBuilder` | api.py:Broker.__init__(queue, timeout, max_conn, max_tries, judges, providers, verify_ssl, loop, stop_broker_on_sigint, provider_dirs, **kwargs) | port + redesign | The brief's requested builder. 11 Python kwargs collapse to 8 real ones; `queue`, `loop`, `stop_broker_on_sigint`, and the two deprecated `**kwargs` are dropped (see dropped). Defaults ported exactly: timeout=8s, max_conn=200, max_tries=3, verify_ssl=false. |
| `BrokerBuilder::timeout / max_conn / max_tries / verify_ssl` | api.py:84-86, 102-103 (self._timeout, self._on_check maxsize, self._max_tries, self._verify_ssl) | port | `timeout: Duration` instead of bare int seconds. `max_conn: NonZeroUsize` because `Semaphore::new(0)` deadlocks forever — Python's `asyncio.Queue(maxsize=0)` silently means UNBOUNDED, the opposite meaning. Type-level fix, see deviations. |
| `BrokerBuilder::judges` | api.py:104 (self._judges = judges) | port | Passed straight through to `Checker` at find() time. Python accepts str-or-Judge union; Rust takes a typed `JudgeSpec` (judge.rs owns `FromStr`). Per locked decision 10, judges become instance state owned by `Checker`, so Broker only carries the spec list. |
| `BrokerBuilder::providers / provider_dir` | api.py:_resolve_providers (168-183) + api.py:116-118 (str -> Provider coercion) | port + redesign | Preserves the documented contract exactly: unset => bundled PROVIDERS defaults; `providers(vec![])` => empty base; every `provider_dir` appends to whichever base was chosen, so `providers(vec![]) + provider_dir(d)` yields ONLY dir-loaded providers. `provider_dir` is additive/repeatable (Python takes a list). The `p if isinstance(p, Provider) else Provider(p)` coercion becomes `impl From<Url> for Provider` in providers.rs, not broker code. |
| `BrokerBuilder::geo_db` | new (implicit in api.py:461 _geo_passed via Resolver.get_ip_info) | write fresh | Python reaches a process-global mmdb through `Resolver.get_ip_info`. Per locked decision 3 the DB is an owned `Arc<GeoDb>` (bundled DB-IP by default, `--geo-db` override). Broker holds it because the country filter (`_geo_passed`) is Broker's job, and it hands it to `Proxy` construction. |
| `BrokerBuilder::build` | api.py:81-126 (the fallible half of __init__) | port + redesign | Fallible where Python's __init__ is not: `Resolver::builder_tokio()?.build()?` returns `Result` (research.md: hickory 0.26 `build()` is a Result, error type `NetError`), provider-dir YAML/JSON parse can fail (-> Error::Config{path,source}), reqwest Client build can fail, GeoDb open can fail. Python defers all of these to first use or panics at import. Does NOT validate non-empty providers — that is a find()-time check, because a Broker built for `serve()` with data= needs no providers. |
| `pub struct Query` | api.py:Broker.find(types, data, countries, post, strict, dnsbl, limit, **kwargs) | port + redesign | find()'s 7 kwargs become one struct so `serve()` can take `(Query, ServeConfig)` instead of Python's `**kwargs` bag that gets forwarded to BOTH Server and find() (api.py:356-368 — `min_queue`/`strategy` are passed to find(), which swallows them in **kwargs; a typo there is silently ignored today). `limit: Option<usize>` per the brief: None = unlimited, replacing Python's `limit=0` + underflow trick. `data: Option<String>` — caller reads the file/stdin. |
| `Query::new + fluent setters` | api.py:199-250 (find signature + `if not types: raise ValueError`) | port + redesign | `types` is the sole positional arg because Python documents it as required and raises ValueError otherwise. `countries()` is `#[cfg(feature = "geo")]` — without the geo feature there is no country code to filter on, so the option should not exist rather than silently no-op. `limit(n)` takes a plain usize (Some(n)); omit the call for unlimited — the `0 means unlimited` sentinel dies here. |
| `Broker::find` | api.py:Broker.find (199-273) | port + redesign | Per locked decision 8, the single biggest shape change. Python's find() is a SPAWNER: it creates the Checker, fires `check_judges()` and `_grab()`/`_load()` as detached tasks, returns immediately, and delivers on `self._proxies`. Rust: (1) validate query.types non-empty -> Error::NoTypes; (2) validate providers non-empty when data is None -> Error::NoProviders; (3) await `resolver.external_ips()`; (4) build `Checker` and await `checker.check_judges()` EAGERLY so Error::NoJudges surfaces in the Err rather than as a RuntimeError inside a detached task (Python: api.py:267 spawns it, checker.py:137 raises inside the task, nobody awaits it — the RuntimeError is swallowed into 'Task exception was never retrieved'); (5) create bounded `mpsc::channel(max_conn)`, build `Run`, spawn the source task into a JoinSet, return `ProxyStream`. Still async because of ext-IP + judge checks. |
| `Broker::grab` | api.py:Broker.grab (185-197) | port + redesign | Same ProxyStream return as find() for a uniform API. NOT async: Python marks it `async def` but awaits nothing (it only sets two fields and calls create_task) — the `async` is noise. Two args, so no builder: a `GrabQuery` struct would be speculative. Errors only with Error::NoProviders. Internally: `Run` with `checker: None` and `Mode::OneShot`, so `handle_candidate` takes the `_push_to_result` branch (`check=False`). |
| `Broker::serve` | api.py:Broker.serve (275-370) | port + redesign | Python's serve() is sync-but-blocking: it calls `self._loop.run_until_complete(run_server())`, meaning the Broker owns the event loop and the caller cannot compose. Rust: async, binds the TcpListener (so EADDRINUSE lands in the Err, not a panic inside a callback), spawns a feeder task that pumps a `Mode::Continuous` ProxyStream into `ProxyPool`, and returns a `ServerHandle` (defined in server.rs) with `local_addr()` and `shutdown()`. `ServeConfig.limit: NonZeroUsize` replaces the runtime `if limit <= 0: raise ValueError` at api.py:349. `kwargs.pop("max_tries", self._max_tries)` becomes `ServeConfig.max_tries: Option<u32>` defaulting to the Broker's. |
| `pub struct ProxyStream` | api.py:Broker.__init__ `self._proxies = queue or asyncio.Queue()` + the None poison pill at api.py:522 | port + redesign | Per locked decision 8. Bounded receiver => backpressure (Python gets this free from `asyncio.Queue(maxsize=...)` only on the CHECK queue, never on the result queue — the result queue is unbounded unless the user passes one). `JoinSet` aborts every worker on Drop, which IS `Broker.stop()` — `find().take(10)` cancels the whole grab/check fleet with no user action. Not Box<dyn Stream>: a named inherent type carries `stats()` and is nameable in user structs (research.md §Streaming). No pin-project needed — every field is Unpin. |
| `impl Stream for ProxyStream` | api.py: the `while True: proxy = await queue.get(); if proxy is None: break` consumer idiom (cli.py:handle) | port + redesign | Termination = all senders dropped => `poll_recv` yields None. The `None` poison pill is deleted. `Item = Proxy`, never `Result<Proxy, _>` — a proxy that fails its check is a non-result, not an error (research.md §Errors). |
| `ProxyStream::stats` | api.py:Broker.unique_proxies (read by show_stats) | port + redesign | Snapshot clone under a short Mutex. Live-readable mid-stream, unlike Python where you must wait for the run to finish and then re-derive everything by grepping every Proxy's log. |
| `pub struct Stats` | api.py:Broker.show_stats (525-609) — its Counter/`stat` dicts | port + redesign | Counters incremented at the decision site. Python DERIVES these by string-matching each proxy's human log text — `if "Location of proxy" in msgs` (576), `elif "Connection: success" in msgs` (578), `"Protocol or the level" in msgs` (579). That coupling means changing a log message silently breaks stats. `errors: HashMap<ProxyError, u32>` ports `Counter(p.stat["errors"])` and is why ProxyError is Copy+Hash (research.md §Errors); the `#[error("...")]` strings keep the histogram keys wire-compatible. `resolve_failed` is new — Python drops those on the floor (api.py:443). |
| `impl fmt::Display for Stats` | api.py:Broker.show_stats print block (602-609) | port + redesign | The library formats a report; it does not print one. `broker.show_stats(verbose=True)` becomes `println!("{}", stream.stats())` in main.rs. Keeps the output lines: working count, per-type breakdown, error histogram. The `verbose` per-negotiator event dump is dropped (see dropped). |
| `struct Run` | api.py: the mutable half of Broker (self._limit, self._countries, self._checker, self._on_check, self.unique_proxies, self._server, self._all_tasks) | write fresh | The load-bearing refactor: everything Python mutates on `self` during a run lives here, one per find()/grab()/serve() call, `Arc<Run>` shared by the spawned tasks. `checker: None` == Python's `check=False` grab path, which removes the `if check:` branch from the hot path AND makes 'grab with no checker' unrepresentable (Python's `_handle(check=True)` would AttributeError on `self._checker` = None if find() had not run). |
| `enum Mode` | api.py: the `if self._server:` tests at 425 and 480 and 497 | port + redesign | Python overloads the `self._server` field as a three-way behavior switch: re-grab forever after GRAB_PAUSE (425), pause-on-full (480), and don't-stop-at-limit (497). Rust names it. `find()`/`grab()` => OneShot; `serve()` => Continuous. Two variants, no config knob. |
| `Run::grab_loop` | api.py:Broker._grab (404-432) incl. the nested _get_tasks generator | port + redesign | Provider filter ports verbatim: `!types \|\| !pr.proto \|\| pr.proto & types.keys()` -> `types.is_none() \|\| p.proto.is_empty() \|\| p.proto.iter().any(\|t\| types.contains(t))` (note: a provider with an EMPTY proto list means 'all protocols', not 'none' — easy to invert). Concurrency: `stream::iter(providers).map(\|p\| p.fetch(&http)).buffer_unordered(MAX_CONCURRENT_PROVIDERS)` replaces Python's chunk-of-3 + `as_completed` (see deviations). Outer loop: OneShot => break after one cycle; Continuous => `tokio::time::sleep(GRAB_PAUSE)` then re-grab. Ends by returning, which drops the Sender. |
| `Run::load_data` | api.py:Broker._load (372-402) | port + redesign | The IPv6-masking parse (extract `[v6]:port` first, blank out those spans, THEN run the v4 line regex so `[::ffff:1.2.3.4]:8080` does not also emit a phantom `1.2.3.4:8080`) is real logic and must be preserved — but it belongs in `crate::parse::find_addrs(&str) -> Vec<(String, u16)>` alongside the provider parsers, not in broker.rs. broker.rs just calls it, dedups (`set(data)`), and feeds handle_candidate. `io.TextIOWrapper`/list inputs are gone: `data: &str` only. |
| `Run::handle_candidate` | api.py:Broker._handle (434-452) | port + redesign | Order preserved exactly: resolve -> unique -> geo -> check-or-emit. `except (ResolveError, ValueError): return` becomes `Err(_) => { stats.resolve_failed += 1; return; }` — counted rather than silently dropped. Note Python constructs the Proxy (and thus does the DNS resolve + geo lookup) BEFORE the dedup check, so a duplicate still costs a resolve; keep that order because dedup keys on the RESOLVED IP, not the raw host — two provider entries `foo.example` and `1.2.3.4` for the same box must collide. |
| `Run::mark_unique` | api.py:Broker._is_unique (454-459) | port + redesign | `HashSet` insert, not a `HashMap<key, Proxy>`. Python retains every Proxy object forever purely so show_stats can walk them at the end — that is an unbounded leak on a long serve() run (millions of scraped candidates). Stats are counted incrementally instead. `stats.found` replaces `len(self.unique_proxies)`. |
| `Run::geo_passed` | api.py:Broker._geo_passed (461-466) | port | `self._countries and proxy.geo.code not in self._countries`. HashSet lookup instead of Python's O(n) list `in`. On reject: `stats.wrong_country += 1` + `tracing::debug!` instead of `proxy.log("Location of proxy is outside...")` — the log line existed to be string-matched by show_stats. Whole fn is `#[cfg(feature = "geo")]`-gated; without geo, `countries` is unconstructible so the call site compiles to nothing. |
| `Run::check_and_emit` | api.py:Broker._push_to_check (468-488) incl. the _task_done closure | port + redesign | Per locked decision 9: `let permit = self.sem.clone().acquire_owned().await` replaces the `asyncio.Queue(maxsize=max_conn)`-as-semaphore plus its `task_done()` / `if not empty: get_nowait()` dance (Python's `_task_done` does task_done() AND get_nowait() on the same callback — a hand-rolled release that leaks a slot if the queue is momentarily empty). The permit is held by the task and released on drop, so cancellation cannot leak a slot; Python's `except asyncio.CancelledError: pass` in the callback is the manual version. Body: `match checker.check(&mut proxy).await { CheckOutcome::Working => self.emit(proxy), _ => {} }`. The `if self._server and not self._proxies.empty() and self._limit <= 0: await self._proxies.join()` pause (480-483) is deleted — bounded mpsc + the serve() feeder do it (see deviations). |
| `Run::emit` | api.py:Broker._push_to_result (490-493) | port + redesign | `self.tx.send(proxy).await` (awaits on a full channel = backpressure; Python uses `put_nowait` into an unbounded queue). Returns false when the receiver is gone (user dropped the ProxyStream) so callers can bail early. Records `stats.working += 1` and `by_type` before sending. Then calls `take_limit_slot`. |
| `Run::take_limit_slot` | api.py:Broker._update_limit (495-498) | port + redesign | The brief's headline case. Python: `self._limit -= 1; if self._limit == 0 and not self._server: self._done()` — `limit=0` means unlimited ONLY because the counter underflows to -1, -2, ... and never re-equals 0. Rust: `remaining: Option<AtomicUsize>`; None => unlimited, always false; Some => `fetch_update(\|n\| n.checked_sub(1))`, returns true on hitting 0. `Mode::Continuous` (serve) never stops on limit, matching `and not self._server`. Stopping = the caller returns, dropping its Sender clone — no `_done()` call. |
| `const MAX_CONCURRENT_PROVIDERS: usize = 3` | api.py:26 | port | Private const, feeds `buffer_unordered`. Not a builder knob — no config for a constant. |
| `const GRAB_PAUSE: Duration` | api.py:23 (GRAB_PAUSE = 180) | port | Private const, only read on the Mode::Continuous path. Typed as Duration, not a bare int. |
| `Error::NoTypes / Error::NoProviders` | api.py:250 `raise ValueError("`types` is required")`; no Python equivalent for NoProviders | port + redesign | Additions to the fatal `Error` enum in errors.rs (which is `#[non_exhaustive]`, so this is free). NoProviders has no Python analogue: `Broker(providers=[])` in Python grabs nothing and the run just completes empty, indistinguishable from '38 providers all returned zero'. |
| `Error::ExtIpUnknown` | api.py:246 `ips = await self._resolver.get_real_ext_ips()` (exception propagates out of find()) | port + redesign | Returned from find() ONLY when the query actually asks for anonymity levels (any TypeSpec with a non-empty level list). Otherwise ext-IP failure is a `tracing::warn!` and the Checker runs with an empty ext-IP set — which checker.py:_get_anonymity_lvl already supports and documents ('Empty/None means no real IP known — Transparent classification disabled'). See deviations; this one needs sign-off. |
| `TypeSpec / Proto / AnonLevel` | api.py:_update_types (612-625) | port + redesign | `_update_types` exists solely to normalize a Python union type (`dict` \| `list[str]` \| `list[(str, str)]` \| `list[(str, list)]`, with `lvl.split()` on a space-joined string) into `{proto: levels}`. In Rust the union is unrepresentable: `Query::new` takes `TypeSpec` directly, so the function has no body left. The string parsing survives only as `impl FromStr for TypeSpec` for the CLI (`--types HTTP:High,Anonymous`), and the type itself belongs in proxy.rs/types.rs next to `Proto`, not in broker.rs. broker.rs consumes `Vec<TypeSpec>` and hands the Checker a `TypeSet`. |

<details><summary><b>Proposed signatures</b></summary>

```rust
// pub struct Broker  ← api.py:Broker (the __init__ state block, lines 81-126)
#[derive(Clone)] pub struct Broker { inner: Arc<BrokerInner> }
// struct BrokerInner  ← new (extracted from api.py:Broker.__init__)
struct BrokerInner { resolver: Resolver, http: reqwest::Client, providers: Vec<Provider>, judges: Option<Vec<JudgeSpec>>, timeout: Duration, verify_ssl: bool, max_conn: usize, max_tries: u32, #[cfg(feature = "geo")] geo: Option<Arc<GeoDb>> }
// pub struct BrokerBuilder  ← api.py:Broker.__init__(queue, timeout, max_conn, max_tries, judges, providers, verify_ssl, loop, stop_broker_on_sigint, provider_dirs, **kwargs)
pub struct BrokerBuilder { /* all Option<_> */ } ; impl Broker { pub fn builder() -> BrokerBuilder }
// BrokerBuilder::timeout / max_conn / max_tries / verify_ssl  ← api.py:84-86, 102-103 (self._timeout, self._on_check maxsize, self._max_tries, self._verify_ssl)
pub fn timeout(self, d: Duration) -> Self; pub fn max_conn(self, n: NonZeroUsize) -> Self; pub fn max_tries(self, n: u32) -> Self; pub fn verify_ssl(self, yes: bool) -> Self
// BrokerBuilder::judges  ← api.py:104 (self._judges = judges)
pub fn judges(self, judges: Vec<JudgeSpec>) -> Self
// BrokerBuilder::providers / provider_dir  ← api.py:_resolve_providers (168-183) + api.py:116-118 (str -> Provider coercion)
pub fn providers(self, p: Vec<Provider>) -> Self; pub fn provider_dir(self, dir: impl Into<PathBuf>) -> Self
// BrokerBuilder::geo_db  ← new (implicit in api.py:461 _geo_passed via Resolver.get_ip_info)
#[cfg(feature = "geo")] pub fn geo_db(self, path: impl AsRef<Path>) -> Self
// BrokerBuilder::build  ← api.py:81-126 (the fallible half of __init__)
pub fn build(self) -> Result<Broker, Error>
// pub struct Query  ← api.py:Broker.find(types, data, countries, post, strict, dnsbl, limit, **kwargs)
pub struct Query { types: Vec<TypeSpec>, data: Option<String>, countries: Option<HashSet<Country>>, post: bool, strict: bool, dnsbl: Vec<String>, limit: Option<usize> }
// Query::new + fluent setters  ← api.py:199-250 (find signature + `if not types: raise ValueError`)
pub fn new(types: impl IntoIterator<Item = TypeSpec>) -> Self; pub fn data(self, s: String) -> Self; #[cfg(feature = "geo")] pub fn countries(self, c: impl IntoIterator<Item = Country>) -> Self; pub fn post(self, b: bool) -> Self; pub fn strict(self, b: bool) -> Self; pub fn dnsbl(self, d: Vec<String>) -> Self; pub fn limit(self, n: usize) -> Self
// Broker::find  ← api.py:Broker.find (199-273)
pub async fn find(&self, query: Query) -> Result<ProxyStream, Error>
// Broker::grab  ← api.py:Broker.grab (185-197)
pub fn grab(&self, countries: Option<HashSet<Country>>, limit: Option<usize>) -> Result<ProxyStream, Error>
// Broker::serve  ← api.py:Broker.serve (275-370)
#[cfg(feature = "server")] pub async fn serve(&self, query: Query, cfg: ServeConfig) -> Result<ServerHandle, Error>
// pub struct ProxyStream  ← api.py:Broker.__init__ `self._proxies = queue or asyncio.Queue()` + the None poison pill at api.py:522
pub struct ProxyStream { rx: mpsc::Receiver<Proxy>, _tasks: JoinSet<()>, stats: Arc<Mutex<Stats>> }
// impl Stream for ProxyStream  ← api.py: the `while True: proxy = await queue.get(); if proxy is None: break` consumer idiom (cli.py:handle)
impl futures_core::Stream for ProxyStream { type Item = Proxy; fn poll_next(...) -> Poll<Option<Proxy>> { self.rx.poll_recv(cx) } }
// ProxyStream::stats  ← api.py:Broker.unique_proxies (read by show_stats)
pub fn stats(&self) -> Stats
// pub struct Stats  ← api.py:Broker.show_stats (525-609) — its Counter/`stat` dicts
#[derive(Clone, Default, Debug)] pub struct Stats { pub found: usize, pub working: usize, pub by_type: BTreeMap<Proto, usize>, pub errors: HashMap<ProxyError, u32>, pub wrong_country: usize, pub wrong_protocol_or_anon: usize, pub conn_success: usize, pub conn_timeout: usize, pub conn_failed: usize, pub resolve_failed: usize }
// impl fmt::Display for Stats  ← api.py:Broker.show_stats print block (602-609)
impl std::fmt::Display for Stats
// struct Run  ← api.py: the mutable half of Broker (self._limit, self._countries, self._checker, self._on_check, self.unique_proxies, self._server, self._all_tasks)
struct Run { broker: Arc<BrokerInner>, checker: Option<Arc<Checker>>, tx: mpsc::Sender<Proxy>, sem: Arc<Semaphore>, seen: Mutex<HashSet<(IpAddr, u16)>>, remaining: Option<AtomicUsize>, countries: Option<HashSet<Country>>, stats: Arc<Mutex<Stats>>, mode: Mode }
// enum Mode  ← api.py: the `if self._server:` tests at 425 and 480 and 497
enum Mode { OneShot, Continuous }
// Run::grab_loop  ← api.py:Broker._grab (404-432) incl. the nested _get_tasks generator
async fn grab_loop(self: Arc<Self>, types: Option<&TypeSet>)
// Run::load_data  ← api.py:Broker._load (372-402)
async fn load_data(self: Arc<Self>, data: &str)
// Run::handle_candidate  ← api.py:Broker._handle (434-452)
async fn handle_candidate(self: Arc<Self>, host: &str, port: u16)
// Run::mark_unique  ← api.py:Broker._is_unique (454-459)
fn mark_unique(&self, addr: (IpAddr, u16)) -> bool
// Run::geo_passed  ← api.py:Broker._geo_passed (461-466)
fn geo_passed(&self, proxy: &Proxy) -> bool
// Run::check_and_emit  ← api.py:Broker._push_to_check (468-488) incl. the _task_done closure
async fn check_and_emit(self: Arc<Self>, proxy: Proxy)
// Run::emit  ← api.py:Broker._push_to_result (490-493)
async fn emit(&self, proxy: Proxy) -> bool
// Run::take_limit_slot  ← api.py:Broker._update_limit (495-498)
fn take_limit_slot(&self) -> bool  // true = quota exhausted, stop
// const MAX_CONCURRENT_PROVIDERS: usize = 3  ← api.py:26
const MAX_CONCURRENT_PROVIDERS: usize = 3;
// const GRAB_PAUSE: Duration  ← api.py:23 (GRAB_PAUSE = 180)
const GRAB_PAUSE: Duration = Duration::from_secs(180);
// Error::NoTypes / Error::NoProviders  ← api.py:250 `raise ValueError("`types` is required")`; no Python equivalent for NoProviders
#[error("query specifies no proxy types")] NoTypes,  #[error("no providers configured")] NoProviders
// Error::ExtIpUnknown  ← api.py:246 `ips = await self._resolver.get_real_ext_ips()` (exception propagates out of find())
#[error("could not determine this host's external IP; anonymity levels cannot be classified")] ExtIpUnknown
// TypeSpec / Proto / AnonLevel  ← api.py:_update_types (612-625)
pub struct TypeSpec { pub proto: Proto, pub levels: Option<Vec<AnonLevel>> } ; impl FromStr for TypeSpec
```
</details>

**Open questions**

- Does `ProxyStream` live in broker.rs or its own stream.rs? It is ~80 lines (struct, Stream impl, stats, Drop semantics) and is the crate's headline public type. I have it in broker.rs since Broker is its only constructor, but it is a fine candidate for splitting if broker.rs crosses ~500 lines.
- `Stats` ownership: `Arc<Mutex<Stats>>` shared between Run and ProxyStream is the lazy choice and contention is trivial (one lock per proxy decision vs. a network round-trip). If a lock-free `Stats` with atomics is wanted for aesthetics, say so now — the `HashMap<ProxyError, u32>` bucket makes it non-trivial (would need a fixed-size array indexed by discriminant).
- serve() + `Query::data`: cli.py:518 passes `data=ns.data` through to serve()'s find(). With data (a fixed list) and Mode::Continuous, the re-grab loop has nothing to re-grab — Python would loop `_load` forever, re-parsing the same string every 180s and finding zero unique proxies each pass. Should `serve(query.with_data(..), _)` be rejected at compile/runtime, or silently run the data once and then idle? Python's behavior here is accidental; I do not want to port an accident without a call.
- Country filter without the `geo` feature: I gate `Query::countries()` on `#[cfg(feature = "geo")]` so the option does not exist. Alternative is a runtime `Error::GeoUnavailable`. The cfg is cleaner but means a `--countries` CLI flag must also be cfg'd (the `cli` feature implies `geo` per the locked Cargo layout, so this is consistent — confirm that implication holds).
- `ServeConfig.limit` vs `Query.limit` are two different limits with the same name: Python collapses them (serve's limit is forwarded as find's limit at api.py:368, then reinterpreted by the `not self._server` branch as a pool target rather than a stop condition). I keep them separate — ServeConfig.limit = pool target, Query.limit ignored in serve mode. Should passing `Query::limit` to serve() be an error rather than ignored?
- Should `Broker::find` take `&self` or `self`? `&self` (my choice) lets one Broker serve many queries, which is the point of splitting config from Run. But it means `Run` holds `Arc<BrokerInner>` and the ProxyStream can outlive the Broker binding — which is correct, just worth confirming as intended.

---

### src/bin/proxybroker.rs

The CLI collapses cli.py's 400 lines of argparse builder functions (create_parser + 8 add_*_args helpers + the _provider_dirs_top dual-dest hack) into ~5 clap 4.6 derive structs: one `Cli` with `global = true` Broker options, one `Command` enum (find/grab/serve/+hidden update-geo stub), and three flattened `Args` structs mirroring Python's argument groups. Everything downstream of parsing is thin: build a `Query`, call `Broker::find`/`grab`/`serve`, and drain the `ProxyStream` through one `OutputSink` that reproduces Python's three formats byte-for-byte (default repr / txt / streamed JSON array). `update-geo` dies (MaxMind endpoint gone; we ship DB-IP instead) and is replaced by `--geo-db PATH`; CC BY 4.0 attribution for the bundled DB-IP database is compiled into both `--version` and `--help`.

**Crates:** `clap (4.6, features = ["derive", "env"])`, `tokio (1, features = ["rt-multi-thread", "macros", "signal", "io-std"])`, `anyhow (1) — main() only; lib stays thiserror`, `serde_json (1) — --format json`, `tracing (facade, always on)`, `tracing-subscriber (0.3, features = ["fmt", "env-filter"]) — gated by the `cli` feature per research.md`, `futures-util (0.3, default-features = false) — StreamExt::{next, take} over ProxyStream`, `url (2) — value_parser for --judge/--provider`, `proxybroker (the lib half of this same crate)`

| Rust item | ← was | Action | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| `fn main() -> std::process::ExitCode` | cli.py:cli() + __main__.py | port + redesign | Parses Cli, inits tracing, dispatches to cmd_find/cmd_grab/cmd_serve. Returns ExitCode instead of falling off the end: 0 on success, 1 on fatal proxybroker::Error (printed via anyhow chain to stderr), 2 for the update-geo stub. Python's `loop = asyncio.new_event_loop(); asyncio.set_event_loop(loop)` and the whole ExitStack/run_until_complete/run_forever dance collapse into #[tokio::main] + await. anyhow only lives here; the lib uses thiserror (research.md: ripgrep's split). |
| `#[derive(Parser)] pub struct Cli` | cli.py:create_parser + cli.py:add_broker_args | port + redesign | Keeps Python's prog/description/epilog (issue-tracker URL) verbatim. `add_help=False` + explicit add_help_arg vanish — clap generates -h/--help. Argument *groups* (Python's add_argument_group(title="Options")) become clap `#[command(next_help_heading = ...)]` on the flattened structs, preserving the grouped --help layout. |
| `#[derive(Args)] struct BrokerOpts` | cli.py:add_broker_args (lines 142-202) | port + redesign | `global = true` is the whole point: it makes `proxybroker find --timeout 5` AND `proxybroker --timeout 5 find` both work, which deletes _add_provider_dir_arg's entire dual-dest (_provider_dirs_top vs provider_dirs) workaround and its 14-line comment. action=Append is implicit for Vec. `-v` is spelled explicitly because clap's derived version flag is `-V`; Python uses `-v`. --geo-db is new (locked decision 3). Values feed Broker's builder. |
| `#[derive(Subcommand)] enum Command` | cli.py:create_parser subparsers (find/grab/serve/update-geo) | port | Same four names, same help/description strings. Python's `if not ns.command: parser.print_help(); return` becomes #[command(subcommand_required = true, arg_required_else_help = true)] on Cli. |
| `#[derive(Args)] struct FindCmd` | cli.py:create_parser fparser (lines 70-84) | port | Mirrors Python's composition exactly: add_find_args + add_grab_args + add_limit_arg + add_outfile_arg + add_format_arg + add_show_stats_arg. The composition helpers become #[command(flatten)] structs — this is the direct clap analogue and needs no other machinery. |
| `#[derive(Args)] struct GrabCmd` | cli.py:create_parser gparser (lines 86-99) | port | grab deliberately has NO --types/--data/--dnsbl/--post/--strict, same as Python (it never checks, so those are meaningless). Preserved. |
| `#[derive(Args)] struct ServeCmd` | cli.py:create_parser sparser (lines 101-122) + add_serve_args | port + redesign | serve carries its OWN --limit (default 100, Python's add_limit_arg(_def=100) with the 'lazily paused' help text) instead of OutputOpts' default 0 — serve has no --outfile/--format/--show-stats in Python and must not gain them. `range(1..)` moves api.py:serve's runtime `ValueError: limit cannot be <= 0` to parse time. |
| `#[derive(Args)] struct FindOpts` | cli.py:add_find_args (lines 205-242) | port | nargs="+" -> num_args=1.. . `type=str.upper`/`str.title` -> ignore_case=true on the ValueEnum. --data stays a String because "-" (stdin) is a legal value, resolved by read_data(). Note --strict keeps `-s` (single char, clap-legal), unlike `-ssl`. |
| `#[derive(Args)] struct GeoOpts` | cli.py:add_grab_args (lines 245-251) | port + redesign | Python passes the raw strings straight to api.py:_geo_passed, which does `proxy.geo.code in self._countries` against an UPPERCASE ISO code — so `-c us` silently matches zero proxies forever. parse_country_code uppercases and rejects anything that isn't 2 ASCII letters. Misnamed helper in Python (it's on grab AND find AND serve, not grab-specific); renamed GeoOpts. |
| `#[derive(Args)] struct ServeOpts` | cli.py:add_serve_args (lines 254-332) | port + redesign | Three changes. (1) --host is IpAddr not String — server.py binds it; garbage should fail at parse. (2) --port is u16 (Python accepts 99999 and blows up in bind). (3) Python's serve `--max-tries` (dest srv_max_tries) is NEVER READ — cli.py:506 builds the broker.serve() kwargs by hand and omits it, so the documented flag is a silent no-op. Renamed --srv-max-tries (a plain --max-tries would collide with the now-global broker --max-tries) and actually threaded into ServerConfig. See deviations. --strategy is a ValueEnum, not a free string (server.py has a closed set of strategies). |
| `#[derive(Args)] struct OutputOpts` | cli.py:add_limit_arg + add_outfile_arg + add_format_arg + add_show_stats_arg | merge | Four one-argument builder functions merged into one Args struct — they are always used together (find, grab) and never used at all (serve). --outfile stays String because "-" means stdout. limit=0 means unlimited, as in Python. |
| `#[cfg_attr(feature = "cli", derive(clap::ValueEnum))] pub enum Proto` | cli.py:add_find_args choices [HTTP, HTTPS, SOCKS4, SOCKS5, CONNECT:80, CONNECT:25] | port + redesign | The CLI does NOT define its own copy of the type list plus a From impl. Single crate lib+bin (locked decision 1) means the lib type can carry a cfg_attr'd ValueEnum derive under the `cli` feature and the bin uses it directly — zero conversion code, one source of truth, no drift when a proto is added. Same trick for AnonLevel and Strategy. |
| `#[cfg_attr(feature = "cli", derive(clap::ValueEnum))] pub enum AnonLevel` | cli.py:add_find_args --lvl choices [Transparent, Anonymous, High] | port + redesign | Same cfg_attr rationale as Proto. `type=str.title` becomes ignore_case=true at the arg site. |
| `#[derive(ValueEnum)] enum OutFormat { Default, Txt, Json }` | cli.py:add_format_arg (--format, nargs="?", type=str.lower, NO choices) | port + redesign | Python validates nothing: `--format bogus` silently produces default-format output, and bare `--format` (nargs="?") yields None which also means default. A closed ValueEnum rejects both. This is the format contract for OutputSink. |
| `#[derive(ValueEnum)] enum LogLevel + fn init_tracing(level: LogLevel)` | cli.py:add_broker_args --log + cli.py:447-451 logging.basicConfig | port + redesign | Same six choice names for compat. Maps to tracing: NOTSET->TRACE, WARNING->WARN, CRITICAL->ERROR (tracing has no CRITICAL). tracing_subscriber::fmt().with_writer(io::stderr) — MUST be stderr, since --outfile defaults to stdout and log lines would corrupt --format json. EnvFilter honors RUST_LOG when set, otherwise --log wins (new; free with EnvFilter, and the idiomatic Rust escape hatch for per-module filtering that Python's single global level can't express). Python's exact format string (%(asctime)s - %(levelname)s - %(name)s - %(message)s, datefmt [%H:%M:%S]) is not reproduced byte-for-byte; see deviations. |
| `const DBIP_ATTRIBUTION: &str + const LONG_VERSION: &str` | new | write fresh | CC BY 4.0 compliance for the bundled DB-IP Country Lite db (locked decision 3, research.md:181). LONG_VERSION is a compile-time concat!(env!("CARGO_PKG_VERSION"), ...) that appends the attribution line ONLY under #[cfg(feature = "geo-bundled")] — attribution is owed for redistributing the data, and --no-default-features ships no data, so the line must not appear then. Surfaced twice: Cli's long_version (so `proxybroker --version` shows it; `-v` short version stays terse) and Cli's after_help (so `--help` shows it). Mirrored in NOTICE/LICENSE-DATA and README, which are not this module's job. |
| `struct OutputSink + impl OutputSink::{new, write, finish}` | cli.py:handle (387-408) + cli.py:outformat (375-384) | merge | The @contextmanager + the consume loop merge into one struct. `outformat` existed only to bracket the JSON array; that's now new()/finish() writing "[\n" and "\n]\n". The `is_first` comma-prefix logic ports exactly, so streamed JSON stays a single valid array (not NDJSON) — wire-compatible. Formats: Default -> write!("{p}\n") using Display (was `f"{proxy!r}\n"`), Txt -> Proxy::as_text() (host:port\n, v6 bracketed), Json -> serde_json::to_string(p). Flushes after every proxy to reproduce Python's `open(..., buffering=1)` line-buffered streaming. Python's `while True: proxy = await proxies.get(); if proxy is None: break` sentinel loop is gone — locked decision 8 terminates by dropping the sender, so this is `while let Some(p) = stream.next().await`. |
| `fn open_outfile(spec: Option<&str>) -> Result<Box<dyn Write>>` | cli.py:463-469 (ExitStack outfile handling) | port | None or "-" -> io::stdout().lock(); else File::create (truncating, matching Python's mode "w"). ExitStack is unnecessary — Drop closes the file. Boxed because stdout and File are different types and this is one dynamic dispatch per line of a network-bound program. |
| `fn read_data(spec: Option<&str>) -> Result<Option<String>>` | cli.py:458-462 (--data / stdin) | port + redesign | "-" -> read stdin to String; else fs::read_to_string. Python passes a live file OBJECT to api.py:_load, which immediately calls .read() on it anyway — so eager read is behavior-identical and lets the Query own a String instead of a lifetime-carrying reader. Only find and serve accept --data, same as Python. |
| `fn resolve_provider_dirs(cli_dirs: &[PathBuf]) -> Option<Vec<PathBuf>>` | cli.py:_resolve_provider_dirs (410-433) | port | Identical 3-tier priority: CLI flags -> $PROXYBROKER_PROVIDER_DIR -> /configs if it is a directory -> None (None means 'Broker keeps default behavior', which is NOT the same as an empty Vec — api.py:_resolve_providers distinguishes them, so keep Option). The merge of the two argparse dests disappears: `global = true` gives one Vec that already contains both positions. |
| `fn build_query(find: &FindOpts, geo: &GeoOpts, data: Option<String>) -> Result<Query>` | cli.py:453-455 (the `types.remove("HTTP"); types.append(("HTTP", anon_lvl))` tuple hack) + api.py:_update_types | port + redesign | Python encodes anonymity by mutating the types list into a heterogeneous list of str-or-(str, list) tuples, then _update_types unpacks it back into a dict. Rust keeps them as two typed fields on Query { types: Vec<Proto>, http_levels: Vec<AnonLevel>, .. } — the tuple-smuggling has no reason to exist once the type isn't a dict-or-list-of-either. Also warns when --lvl is given without HTTP in --types (Python drops it in total silence, since the hack is gated on `"HTTP" in ns.types`). |
| `async fn cmd_find(cli: &Cli, cmd: &FindCmd) -> Result<()>` | cli.py:491-502 + 486-489 + 527-533 | port + redesign | Builds Broker, calls `broker.find(query).await?` -> ProxyStream, applies `--limit N` as `.take(n)` (Python's limit is enforced inside the Broker via _update_limit; StreamExt::take is the free version, and locked decision 8 makes drop = cancel), and drains into OutputSink inside a tokio::select! against tokio::signal::ctrl_c(). The gather-of-two-coroutines (handle + broker.find) is unnecessary: find returns the stream and the consumer IS the loop. Calls print_stats after the loop if --show-stats. |
| `async fn cmd_grab(cli: &Cli, cmd: &GrabCmd) -> Result<()>` | cli.py:503-504 (broker.grab) | port | Identical to cmd_find minus the checker: `broker.grab(countries, limit)` -> ProxyStream -> same OutputSink -> same ctrl_c select -> same optional stats. Kept as its own fn rather than a bool param on cmd_find because the Query types differ. |
| `async fn cmd_serve(cli: &Cli, cmd: &ServeCmd) -> Result<()>` | cli.py:505-525 + 533 (loop.run_forever) | port | Builds ServerConfig from ServeOpts + the find Query, awaits broker.serve(...) to bind, prints `Server started at http://{host}:{port}` to stdout (same string, same order — Python prints after the bind completes), then awaits ctrl_c and shuts down. run_forever/KeyboardInterrupt/broker.stop() -> `tokio::signal::ctrl_c().await` then drop. serve produces no proxy output, so no OutputSink and no --show-stats, as in Python. |
| `fn print_stats(stats: &Stats, verbose: bool)` | cli.py:530-531 (broker.show_stats(verbose=True)) -> api.py:show_stats (525-609) | port + redesign | The CLI half only. Prints working-proxy count, per-proto counts (SOCKS5/SOCKS4/HTTPS/HTTP/CONNECT:80/CONNECT:25 order preserved), and the error histogram — whose keys are ProxyError's #[error("...")] strings, which research.md pins as byte-equal to Python's errmsg values, so the `Errors: Counter(...)` line stays recognizable. Python's classification (`if "Location of proxy" in msgs` / `"Connection: success" in msgs`) greps free-text log strings out of proxy.get_log(); that is replaced by typed counters on Stats. --show-stats therefore maps to verbose=true exactly as today, but the per-negotiator event dump is dropped (see dropped). |
| `fn update_geo_stub() -> ExitCode` | cli.py:124-137 (uparser) + utils.py:update_geoip_db (193-201) | port + redesign | Kept ONLY as a #[command(hide = true)] subcommand so existing scripts/Dockerfiles get a real explanation instead of clap's bare 'unrecognized subcommand'. Prints to stderr: MaxMind retired the endpoint 2019-12-30; this port ships DB-IP Country Lite (CC BY 4.0) instead; refresh with `--geo-db /path/to/dbip-country-lite.mmdb` from https://db-ip.com/db/download/ip-to-country-lite. Exits 2. ~10 lines, no network, no download logic. Python raised RuntimeError with a traceback; we exit cleanly. |

<details><summary><b>Proposed signatures</b></summary>

```rust
// fn main() -> std::process::ExitCode  ← cli.py:cli() + __main__.py
#[tokio::main] async fn main() -> ExitCode
// #[derive(Parser)] pub struct Cli  ← cli.py:create_parser + cli.py:add_broker_args
#[command(name = "proxybroker", about = "Proxy [Finder | Checker | Server]", after_help = ATTRIBUTION, long_version = LONG_VERSION)] struct Cli { #[command(flatten)] broker: BrokerOpts, #[command(subcommand)] command: Command }
// #[derive(Args)] struct BrokerOpts  ← cli.py:add_broker_args (lines 142-202)
struct BrokerOpts { #[arg(long, global=true, default_value_t=200)] max_conn: usize, #[arg(long, global=true, default_value_t=3)] max_tries: u32, #[arg(long, short='t', global=true, value_name="SECONDS", default_value_t=8)] timeout: u64, #[arg(long="judge", global=true, value_parser=clap::value_parser!(Url))] judges: Vec<Url>, #[arg(long="provider", global=true, value_parser=clap::value_parser!(Url))] providers: Vec<Url>, #[arg(long="provider-dir", global=true, value_name="PATH")] provider_dirs: Vec<PathBuf>, #[arg(long, global=true)] verify_ssl: bool, #[arg(long, global=true, value_enum, ignore_case=true, default_value="critical")] log: LogLevel, #[arg(long, global=true, value_name="PATH")] geo_db: Option<PathBuf>, #[arg(short='v', long, action=ArgAction::Version)] version: Option<bool> }
// #[derive(Subcommand)] enum Command  ← cli.py:create_parser subparsers (find/grab/serve/update-geo)
enum Command { Find(FindCmd), Grab(GrabCmd), Serve(ServeCmd), #[command(hide = true)] UpdateGeo }
// #[derive(Args)] struct FindCmd  ← cli.py:create_parser fparser (lines 70-84)
struct FindCmd { #[command(flatten)] find: FindOpts, #[command(flatten)] geo: GeoOpts, #[command(flatten)] out: OutputOpts }
// #[derive(Args)] struct GrabCmd  ← cli.py:create_parser gparser (lines 86-99)
struct GrabCmd { #[command(flatten)] geo: GeoOpts, #[command(flatten)] out: OutputOpts }
// #[derive(Args)] struct ServeCmd  ← cli.py:create_parser sparser (lines 101-122) + add_serve_args
struct ServeCmd { #[command(flatten)] srv: ServeOpts, #[command(flatten)] find: FindOpts, #[command(flatten)] geo: GeoOpts, #[arg(long, short='l', default_value_t=100, value_parser=clap::value_parser!(u32).range(1..))] limit: u32 }
// #[derive(Args)] struct FindOpts  ← cli.py:add_find_args (lines 205-242)
struct FindOpts { #[arg(long, required=true, num_args=1.., value_enum, ignore_case=true)] types: Vec<Proto>, #[arg(long="lvl", num_args=1.., value_enum, ignore_case=true)] anon_lvl: Vec<AnonLevel>, #[arg(long)] data: Option<String>, #[arg(long, num_args=1..)] dnsbl: Vec<String>, #[arg(long)] post: bool, #[arg(long, short='s')] strict: bool }
// #[derive(Args)] struct GeoOpts  ← cli.py:add_grab_args (lines 245-251)
struct GeoOpts { #[arg(long="countries", short='c', num_args=1.., value_parser=parse_country_code)] countries: Vec<CountryCode> }
// #[derive(Args)] struct ServeOpts  ← cli.py:add_serve_args (lines 254-332)
struct ServeOpts { #[arg(long, default_value="127.0.0.1")] host: IpAddr, #[arg(long, default_value_t=8888)] port: u16, #[arg(long="srv-max-tries")] srv_max_tries: Option<u32>, #[arg(long, value_enum, default_value="best")] strategy: Strategy, #[arg(long, default_value_t=5)] min_queue: usize, #[arg(long, default_value_t=5)] min_req_proxy: usize, #[arg(long, default_value_t=0.5)] max_error_rate: f64, #[arg(long, value_name="SECONDS", default_value_t=8)] max_resp_time: u64, #[arg(long)] prefer_connect: bool, #[arg(long, num_args=1..)] http_allowed_codes: Vec<u16>, #[arg(long, default_value_t=100)] backlog: u32 }
// #[derive(Args)] struct OutputOpts  ← cli.py:add_limit_arg + add_outfile_arg + add_format_arg + add_show_stats_arg
struct OutputOpts { #[arg(long, short='l', default_value_t=0)] limit: u32, #[arg(long, short='o')] outfile: Option<String>, #[arg(long, short='f', value_enum, ignore_case=true, default_value="default")] format: OutFormat, #[arg(long)] show_stats: bool }
// #[cfg_attr(feature = "cli", derive(clap::ValueEnum))] pub enum Proto  ← cli.py:add_find_args choices [HTTP, HTTPS, SOCKS4, SOCKS5, CONNECT:80, CONNECT:25]
#[value(name = "CONNECT:80")] Connect80, ...
// #[derive(ValueEnum)] enum LogLevel + fn init_tracing(level: LogLevel)  ← cli.py:add_broker_args --log + cli.py:447-451 logging.basicConfig
fn init_tracing(level: LogLevel) // NOTSET|DEBUG|INFO|WARNING|ERROR|CRITICAL, default CRITICAL
// const DBIP_ATTRIBUTION: &str + const LONG_VERSION: &str  ← new
const DBIP_ATTRIBUTION: &str = "IP Geolocation by DB-IP (https://db-ip.com)";
// struct OutputSink + impl OutputSink::{new, write, finish}  ← cli.py:handle (387-408) + cli.py:outformat (375-384)
struct OutputSink<W: Write> { w: W, format: OutFormat, first: bool } ; fn write(&mut self, p: &Proxy) -> io::Result<()> ; fn finish(self) -> io::Result<()>
// fn build_query(find: &FindOpts, geo: &GeoOpts, data: Option<String>) -> Result<Query>  ← cli.py:453-455 (the `types.remove("HTTP"); types.append(("HTTP", anon_lvl))` tuple hack) + api.py:_update_types
fn build_query(...) -> Result<Query, anyhow::Error>
// async fn cmd_find(cli: &Cli, cmd: &FindCmd) -> Result<()>  ← cli.py:491-502 + 486-489 + 527-533
async fn cmd_find(cli: &Cli, cmd: &FindCmd) -> anyhow::Result<()>
// fn print_stats(stats: &Stats, verbose: bool)  ← cli.py:530-531 (broker.show_stats(verbose=True)) -> api.py:show_stats (525-609)
fn print_stats(stats: &proxybroker::Stats, verbose: bool)
```
</details>

**Open questions**

- clap `global = true` combined with ArgAction::Append: does clap 4.6 MERGE occurrences given on both sides of the subcommand (`proxybroker --provider-dir A find --provider-dir B`), or does one position win? The whole justification for deleting Python's dual-dest hack rests on merge. If clap only propagates one side, --provider-dir needs to stay non-global and be declared on each subcommand, and resolve_provider_dirs regains a (simpler) merge. Verify with a parse test as the FIRST thing implemented.
- Should `update-geo` be resurrected against DB-IP's monthly URL (https://download.db-ip.com/free/dbip-country-lite-YYYY-MM.mmdb.gz) rather than being a stub? It would be ~40 lines (reqwest + flate2 + a cache dir), it makes the bundled db refreshable without a manual download, and it is arguably what users expect the command to do. Against: a new dep (flate2), a network-dependent code path in the CLI, DB-IP's terms on automated download not yet read, and --geo-db already covers the need. Stubbed pending a call.
- Exit code when a run completes with ZERO proxies found. Python exits 0. `proxybroker find --types HTTP -l 10` returning nothing is indistinguishable from success in a shell pipeline. Proposal (NOT taken, needs sign-off): exit 1 when limit > 0 and found == 0.
- Does `--geo-db` belong on the global BrokerOpts, or only on find/serve (the commands that check)? grab does geo filtering too (api.py:_geo_passed runs for grab via --countries), so global is the current call — confirm grab really does resolve country without a checker.
- Python's `--data` is accepted on serve (add_find_args is shared) but serve then feeds it to find internally. Confirm serve+`--data -` (stdin) is a real supported combination worth porting, or whether --data should be find-only.
- `--strategy` is a free-form string in Python (default "best") passed through to server.py's pool. Modeling it as a ValueEnum requires the closed set from server.py — confirm against that module's design map that no user-pluggable strategy exists.

---

### src/resolver.rs + src/geo.rs (ported from proxybroker/resolver.py, 558 LOC)

resolver.py is three unrelated things welded together: a DNS client with a hand-rolled global cache, an external-IP prober, and a GeoIP reader hanging off a module-global mmdb handle. In Rust it splits cleanly: `src/resolver.rs` = `Resolver` (hickory `TokioResolver` + the ext-IP prober), `src/geo.rs` = `GeoDb`/`GeoData` behind `#[cfg(feature = "geo")]`. Roughly half the Python evaporates: the `_cached_hosts` class-attr cache + `_cache_compatible` + the `_QTYPE_DEFAULT`/`_fetch_records`/`_race_a_aaaa` Happy-Eyeballs machinery are all things hickory does natively (`ResponseCache`, `LookupIpStrategy::Ipv4AndIpv6`), and the try/finally task-cancellation dance in `get_real_ext_ips` is `JoinSet`'s abort-on-drop. Everything IP-shaped becomes `IpAddr`, which deletes `canonicalize_ip` from this module's vocabulary entirely — an `IpAddr` is canonical by construction and `Hash + Eq`, so `real_ext_ips` returns a real `HashSet<IpAddr>` instead of a frozenset of hand-canonicalized strings.

**Crates:** `hickory-resolver 0.26.1 (tokio + system-config features; builder-only API: Resolver::builder_tokio(), hickory_resolver::net::runtime::TokioRuntimeProvider, error type NetError)`, `tokio 1 (rt, net, time, macros — JoinSet, timeout, Instant)`, `reqwest 0.13 (default-features = false + rustls; ext-IP probes only — the checker's stack is separate per locked decision 4)`, `rand 0.9 (SliceRandom::shuffle for endpoint order)`, `thiserror 2 (Error / ProxyError enums, #[non_exhaustive])`, `tracing 0.1 (facade only)`, `maxminddb 0.29 (optional, gated on feature "geo"; Reader::from_source / open_readfile, two-stage lookup().decode::<geoip2::City>())`, `NOT taken: public-ip (stuck at 0.2.2 / 2022, drags in pre-rename trust-dns + hyper 0.14), moka (hickory's ResponseCache is sufficient), flate2 (ship the mmdb raw; cargo gzips the .crate), libc (IpFamily enum replaces AF_INET/AF_INET6)`

| Rust item | ← was | Action | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| `pub struct Resolver` | resolver.py:34 Resolver | port + redesign | Holds the hickory resolver plus the two family-pinned reqwest Clients for ext-IP probing. No `_cached_hosts` field: hickory's built-in ResponseCache replaces it (locked decision + research §DNS). No `loop`. Intended to be shared as `Arc<Resolver>` handed down from Broker to Checker/Judge/Server — Python constructs five independent `Resolver()` instances (api.py:83, checker.py:80, judge.py:37, server.py:225, proxy.py:87) that only shared a cache because `_cached_hosts` was a CLASS attribute. Deleting the class attr means we must share the instance instead; that is a strict improvement (bounded, TTL-correct, per-Broker) but it is a wiring requirement on api.rs. |
| `Resolver::new` | resolver.py:53 Resolver.__init__ | port + redesign | `Resolver::builder_tokio()?` (system resolv.conf — mirrors aiodns's default), then `*builder.options_mut()` with `ResolverOpts::default()` mutated (it is `#[non_exhaustive]`, no struct literal): `timeout`, `attempts = 2`, `cache_size`, `ip_strategy = LookupIpStrategy::Ipv4AndIpv6`. `build()` returns `Result` → `Error::Resolver(NetError)` (fatal enum; note it is `NetError`, not `ResolveError`). Also builds the two family-pinned reqwest Clients once here rather than per-probe (Python builds a fresh `aiohttp.TCPConnector` + `ClientSession` on every `_probe_family` call). Drops the whole deferred-construction dance (`self._resolver = None` / `aiodns.DNSResolver(loop=...)` / the get_event_loop RuntimeError guard, lines 53-63 and 547-549) — that exists solely because aiodns grabs an event loop at construction time and Python 3.14 made that raise. Rust has no ambient-loop problem. |
| `Resolver::resolve` | resolver.py:409 Resolver.resolve | port + redesign | Collapses a 60-line method to ~10. Body: `if let Some(ip) = parse_ip_literal(host) { return Ok(ip) }` (keeps Python's IP-literal short-circuit, so the common case never touches DNS), else `self.dns.lookup_ip(host).await` → first address → `Ok`. Empty answer or `NetError` → `Err(ProxyError::Resolve)` + `tracing::debug!`. Every parameter except `host` is dropped: `port` (only ever fed into the addrinfo dicts nobody reads), `family`/`qtype` (NO caller in the entire codebase passes them — verified by grep: proxy.py:89, judge.py:95, server.py:377 all call `resolve(host)`, checker.py:160 calls `resolve(query, logging=False)`), and `logging` (a bool to suppress one warning on the DNSBL path — replaced by logging at debug and letting callers report). Return type is one `IpAddr`, never `None`, never a `list[dict]`. |
| `parse_ip_literal` | resolver.py:65 Resolver.host_is_ip (staticmethod) | port + redesign | Returns the parsed address instead of a bool, because every Python caller of `host_is_ip` immediately wants the address anyway and Python's bool-only contract is why `proxy.py:103` stores the raw un-normalized literal as `self.host`. Two-step, matching Python: (1) `host.parse::<IpAddr>()`; (2) if that fails and `host` contains '.' and no ':', retry with each octet's ASCII leading zeros stripped — this legacy path exists because real provider feeds emit `127.0.0.001` and CPython rejects it since 3.9.5 (CVE-2021-29921); dropping it silently drops proxies. Rust's `Ipv4Addr` parser rejects leading zeros too, so the branch must be carried over. Lives in resolver.rs (not util.rs) because it is a `Resolver` staticmethod in Python and proxy.rs calls it as `Resolver.host_is_ip`; `Resolver::host_is_ip` is NOT kept as an associated fn — a free fn needs no `&self` and no type-name ceremony. |
| `Resolver::real_ext_ips` | resolver.py:267 Resolver.get_real_ext_ips | port + redesign | Keeps the algorithm exactly: filter families by `has_local_route`, error if none routable, probe surviving families concurrently, take first success, give the rest `timeout - elapsed` as a grace window, error if nothing found. `HashSet<IpAddr>` replaces `frozenset[str]` — set semantics come from the type, not from calling `canonicalize_ip` on the way in. Implementation is a `JoinSet<Result<IpAddr, ()>>`: loop `join_next()` until the first `Ok`, then `tokio::time::timeout(grace, drain-remaining)`. This deletes Python's entire try/finally block (lines 312-335: cancel every unfinished task, then `gather(..., return_exceptions=True)` so cancellation actually propagates and HTTP connectors close) — `JoinSet::drop` aborts its tasks, which is the whole point of that 24-line comment-heavy stanza. Called once at startup (api.py:246). |
| `Resolver::probe_family` | resolver.py:178 Resolver._probe_family | port | Shuffle `EXT_IP_ENDPOINTS`, try each with `try_endpoint` until one validates, return it. Uses the pre-built family-pinned Client instead of constructing a connector per call. Deliberately keeps Python's no-family-deadline contract (per-request timeout only, iterate ALL candidates before giving up — the Python comment at 200-213 says a family budget was explicitly rejected in review so a stalled first candidate can't kill the family). Consequence carried over as-is: a single-routable-family host with all 7 endpoints black-holed blocks startup for 7 × timeout (~35s default) before `real_ext_ips` errors. Returns `Option` rather than Python's `raise RuntimeError(f"No external IP for family {family}")` — the caller only ever logs that message at debug (line 368). |
| `Resolver::try_endpoint` | resolver.py:228 Resolver._try_endpoint | port | GET with `.timeout(self.timeout)`; any transport error / non-200 / unparseable body → `None` and move to the next candidate. The non-200 skip is load-bearing and must survive the port: an error page's body can contain IP-shaped strings that aren't the ext-IP. Body `.text()` then `.trim().parse::<IpAddr>()` replaces `canonicalize_ip(text)`; Python's separate `UnicodeDecodeError` arm disappears because reqwest's `text()` is lossy-UTF-8 and a mangled body simply fails to parse. Then `validate_probe_response`. |
| `validate_probe_response` | resolver.py:149 Resolver._validate_probe_response (staticmethod) | port | The six-cell (response-form × family) matrix ports 1:1 and is the real family guard — it is what makes correctness independent of whether socket-level family pinning works (see open question 1). Critical API detail: Python's `addr.ipv4_mapped` is mapped-only (`::ffff:a.b.c.d`), so the Rust must use `Ipv6Addr::to_ipv4_mapped()`, NOT `to_ipv4()` — the latter also converts deprecated IPv4-compatible `::a.b.c.d`, silently widening acceptance. Cells: v4-mapped on a V6 probe → reject (dual-stack actually used v4); v4-mapped on a V4 probe → normalize to pure v4; pure-family mismatch → reject. |
| `has_local_route` | resolver.py:124 Resolver._has_local_route (staticmethod) | port | `std::net::UdpSocket::bind` on the unspecified address of `family`, then `connect` to a documentation address (192.0.2.1:80 / [2001:db8::1]:80). UDP-connect only consults the routing table — no packets, no DNS, microseconds — so it stays a plain blocking std call inside the async fn, no `spawn_blocking`. Keeps v4-only hosts (~half the install base per the Python comment) from paying the v6 probe's timeout. `Err` from either bind or connect → false. |
| `enum IpFamily { V4, V6 }` | new | write fresh | Private to resolver.rs. Replaces `socket.AF_INET` / `socket.AF_INET6` ints threaded through five functions. Avoids a `libc` dependency and makes the `(family == socket.AF_INET6) != is_v6` comparisons in `_validate_probe_response` readable. Not public — no caller outside this module ever names a family. |
| `const EXT_IP_ENDPOINTS: [&str; 7]` | resolver.py:43 Resolver._ip_hosts | port | Verbatim, order-preserved (api64.ipify.org first as the dual-stack-aware one; the rest are v4-only-by-URL fallbacks). A const array, not a config field — Python doesn't let you override it either, and a configurable list is a config-for-a-constant. Shuffled per probe with `rand::seq::SliceRandom::shuffle(&mut rand::rng())`, replacing Python's `secrets.choice`-in-a-while-loop (which is `secrets` only to silence SonarCloud S2245 — the Python comment says so outright; endpoint load-balancing is not security-sensitive). |
| `GeoDb (src/geo.rs)` | resolver.py:19-23 _countrydb / _citydb / _geo_db / _mmdb_reader | port + redesign | Turns four module-level globals + an at-import `maxminddb.open_database()` into an owned handle. `Cow<'static, [u8]>` is the one type that satisfies `S: AsRef<[u8]>` for both the bundled (`Borrowed(&'static [u8])` from `include_bytes!`) and user-supplied (`Owned(Vec<u8>)` from `open_readfile`) cases — no enum, no generic leaking into every caller. Owned by Broker as `Option<Arc<GeoDb>>`; `None` when `--no-default-features` drops `geo-bundled` and the user passes no `--geo-db`. Also kills the `_citydb if exists else _countrydb` startup probe: there is exactly one source now (`--geo-db` path, else bundled). |
| `GeoDb::bundled` | resolver.py:19-21 (_geo_db selection) + proxybroker/data/GeoLite2-Country.mmdb | port + redesign | `Reader::from_source(Cow::Borrowed(include_bytes!("../data/dbip-country-lite.mmdb")))`. Ship the mmdb RAW, not gzipped: cargo already gzips the `.crate` tarball, so the published artifact is ~3.86 MB either way (research §GeoLite licensing measured it), and raw means zero `flate2` dep, zero startup decompress, and a zero-copy `&'static [u8]` reader instead of Python's read-the-file-at-import. Data is DB-IP Country Lite / CC BY 4.0 per locked decision 3 — the 3.1 MB, 2017-vintage GeoLite2-Country.mmdb is not carried over. Attribution obligation (`IP Geolocation by DB-IP (https://db-ip.com)`) lands in NOTICE/LICENSE-DATA/--version, not in this module. |
| `GeoDb::open` | new | write fresh | `Reader::open_readfile(path)` → `Cow::Owned`. Required by locked decision 3 (`--geo-db`): it is how a user brings their own GeoLite2 (legal for them, zero redistribution risk for us) and how anyone gets city/region data at all, since the bundled DB is country-only. Errors are fatal (`Error::Geo`) — a user who explicitly passed a bad `--geo-db` path wants to hear about it, not silently get `--`/Unknown. `open_mmap` is deliberately not used: it needs a non-default feature and its signature is unverified (research open question 4); a few-MB `Vec<u8>` is fine. |
| `GeoDb::lookup` | resolver.py:93 Resolver.get_ip_info (staticmethod) | port + redesign | Infallible, mirroring Python's swallow-everything contract: `self.reader.lookup(ip)` then `.decode::<maxminddb::geoip2::City>()` — any `Err`, or `Ok(None)`, or a miss → `GeoData::unknown()` + `tracing::debug!`. Note the 0.29 two-stage API: `lookup()` returns `LookupResult`, a miss is `Ok(None)` from `decode()`, NOT `Err(AddressNotFound)`. Decoding as `geoip2::City` (not `Country`) for BOTH database types is the lazy unification — City's schema is a superset (country / continent / city / subdivisions) and missing keys deserialize to `None`, so one decode path serves the bundled Country DB and a user's City DB with no db_type sniffing. Field precedence ports exactly: `country` wins, `continent` is the fallback (code + names.en), `city.names.en`, `subdivisions[0]` for region code/name. `iso_code` is `Option<&'a str>` borrowed from the reader's buffer → `.to_owned()` at the lookup site (research's lifetime gotcha: you cannot hold the Reader and a decoded Country in one struct). |
| `pub struct GeoData` | resolver.py:15 GeoData namedtuple | port | Same five fields, same names — proxy.py's `as_json` (lines 295-300) and `__repr__` (155) and api.py's `_geo_passed` (462) all read them, and the JSON output shape is a public contract. Owned `String`s, not `&str`: the decoded values borrow the Reader and `GeoData` outlives every lookup. Country-code-vs-continent-code sharing one `code` field is Python's design and is preserved (a `--countries EU` filter matching a continent code is emergent Python behavior, not a bug worth 'fixing' unilaterally). No `Serialize` derive here — proxy.rs nests these into `{country:{code,name}, region:{code,name}, city}`, so the mapping belongs there. |
| `GeoData::unknown` | resolver.py:109-110 (code, name = "--", "Unknown"; city_name, region_code, region_name = ("Unknown",) * 3) | port | The sentinel values are wire-visible (they appear in `--format json` output and in `<Proxy -- 1.23s ...>` reprs), so they port verbatim rather than becoming `Option`. `Default` rather than a named ctor since it is also the partial-fill base inside `lookup`. With the bundled country-only DB, `region_code`/`region_name`/`city_name` are ALWAYS "Unknown" — which is already true of Python in practice, since `_citydb` is never present in the shipped package. |
| `ProxyError::Resolve` | errors.py:ResolveError | port + redesign | Cross-module, listed because this module is its only producer. Per locked decision 11 it belongs in the per-proxy enum (`#[error("resolve_failed")]`), since every consumer treats it as 'skip this one': proxy.py:89-97 logs and re-raises into Broker's discard path, judge.py:95-97 bare-`return`s to mark the judge dead, server.py:377-379 `return`s the connection, checker.py:160-166 treats it as 'not in DNSBL'. It is NOT in the fatal `Error` enum — resolver *construction* failure (`Error::Resolver(NetError)`) is the fatal one. Python conflates them under a single `ResolveError`. |

<details><summary><b>Proposed signatures</b></summary>

```rust
// pub struct Resolver  ← resolver.py:34 Resolver
pub struct Resolver { dns: hickory_resolver::TokioResolver, http_v4: reqwest::Client, http_v6: reqwest::Client, timeout: Duration }
// Resolver::new  ← resolver.py:53 Resolver.__init__
pub fn new(timeout: Duration) -> Result<Self, Error>

// Resolver::real_ext_ips  ← resolver.py:267 Resolver.get_real_ext_ips

// Resolver::probe_family  ← resolver.py:178 Resolver._probe_family
async fn probe_family(&self, family: IpFamily) -> Option<IpAddr>
// Resolver::try_endpoint  ← resolver.py:228 Resolver._try_endpoint
async fn try_endpoint(&self, client: &reqwest::Client, url: &str, family: IpFamily) -> Option<IpAddr>
// validate_probe_response  ← resolver.py:149 Resolver._validate_probe_response (staticmethod)
fn validate_probe_response(ip: IpAddr, family: IpFamily) -> Option<IpAddr>

fn has_local_route(family: IpFamily) -> bool
// enum IpFamily { V4, V6 }  ← new
#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq)] enum IpFamily { V4, V6 }
// GeoDb (src/geo.rs)  ← resolver.py:19-23 _countrydb / _citydb / _geo_db / _mmdb_reader
#[cfg(feature = "geo")] pub struct GeoDb { reader: maxminddb::Reader<Cow<'static, [u8]>> }
// GeoDb::bundled  ← resolver.py:19-21 (_geo_db selection) + proxybroker/data/GeoLite2-Country.mmdb

// GeoData::unknown  ← resolver.py:109-110 (code, name = "--", "Unknown"; city_name, region_code, region_name = ("Unknown",) * 3)
impl Default for GeoData  // code: "--", everything else: "Unknown"
```
</details>

**Open questions**

- How do we pin a reqwest Client to an address family? Python uses `aiohttp.TCPConnector(family=...)`, which is socket-level and immune to DNS quirks. reqwest 0.13's `ClientBuilder` has no `family` knob. Two candidates, NEITHER verified against docs.rs (research doesn't cover it): (a) `local_address(Ipv4Addr::UNSPECIFIED)` / `local_address(Ipv6Addr::UNSPECIFIED)` — binds a socket of that family, so cross-family connects fail; (b) implement `reqwest::dns::Resolve` to filter answers by family and install via `ClientBuilder::dns_resolver`. (a) is far lazier; verify it actually forces the family in hyper-util's HttpConnector before committing. Mitigation either way: `validate_probe_response` rejects wrong-family answers post-hoc, so imperfect pinning degrades to wasted attempts, not wrong results.
- Does DB-IP Country Lite's mmdb carry `country.names.en` / `continent.names.en`? Research verified `country.iso_code` reads fine but never checked the names map. If absent, `GeoData.name` is always 'Unknown' with the bundled DB — visible in `--format json` and `<Proxy US ...>` reprs. Fallback options: (a) ship a static ISO-3166 code→name table (~250 entries, trivial); (b) set `name = code`. Needs a 5-minute check against the actual file before implementation.
- `maxminddb::geoip2::City<'a>`'s field list is unverified (research open question 3 flags the same for `Country<'a>`; only the nested `country::Country` fields are confirmed). The whole 'decode City against a Country DB, missing keys → None' unification rests on City's fields being `Option`. If they aren't, fall back to two decode paths keyed on `reader.metadata().database_type`.
- hickory `LookupIpStrategy::Ipv4AndIpv6` — is it genuinely concurrent (Python's stated reason for hand-rolling the race: sequential A→AAAA costs a full extra RTT on v6-only names), and what order does `LookupIp::iter()` yield when both families answer? `resolve` takes the first address, so ordering decides the v4/v6 preference for every judge/DNSBL/server-CONNECT resolution. Python's race has no defined preference either (whichever query returns first wins), so there's no contract to break — but the answer determines whether we need an explicit preference. Note the default is `Ipv4thenIpv6` (sequential), which we are explicitly NOT taking.
- Confirm hickory-resolver 0.26.1's feature names — `tokio` and `system-config` are from the 0.25-era manifest and were not re-verified for 0.26. `builder_tokio()` requires whichever feature gates `TokioRuntimeProvider`.
- Ownership wiring: does api.rs agree to construct one `Resolver` and pass `Arc<Resolver>` to Checker/Judge/Server/the Proxy factory? Python constructs five independent instances and gets away with it only because the cache was a class attribute. If they stay independent, each gets its own cold ResponseCache and we lose Python's (accidental) cross-component cache sharing — the judge hostnames in particular are resolved from many concurrent tasks.
- Module boundary with util.rs: `canonicalize_ip` and `get_all_ip` (utils.py:69, 114) are that module's symbols, but they exist to do what `IpAddr` does for free, and `get_all_ip` is the consumer of `real_ext_ips`'s output (checker.py:365-367 canonicalizes both sides before intersecting). Proposal: `get_all_ip` returns `HashSet<IpAddr>`, `canonicalize_ip` ceases to exist, and the anonymity-leak check becomes a set intersection of `IpAddr`s. Needs a joint decision with util.rs's owner — and it's the same decision as the zone-ID deviation above.

---

### src/server/mod.rs + src/server/pool.rs (behind the `server` cargo feature)

Two files. `pool.rs` is a small owned-value store fed by the checker's `mpsc::Receiver<Proxy>`: `Arc<ProxyPool>` with a `std::sync::Mutex<PoolState>` (never held across an await) plus a separate `tokio::sync::Mutex<Receiver>` for the import path, so N connection tasks share it with `&self`. Python's `heapq` is dropped entirely — the pool holds tens of proxies, so a `Vec` + linear `min_by_key` scan is faster than drain-and-repush, makes scheme-filtered selection and `remove()` trivial, and eliminates a latent `TypeError` on heap ties. `mod.rs` is a hyper 1.10 `http1` server: hyper frames the client request (killing `_parse_request`, `parse_headers`, `_check_response`, `_inject_headers`), CONNECT goes through `hyper::upgrade` + `with_upgrades()` into a raw bidirectional copy, and plain HTTP goes through a `hyper::client::conn::http1` handshake over the negotiated upstream stream so `X-Proxy-Info` is a real header rather than a byte splice into (sometimes) a TLS record.

**Crates:** `hyper 1.10 (features: server, client, http1)`, `hyper-util 0.1 (rt::TokioIo, rt::TokioTimer)`, `http-body-util 0.1 (BodyExt, Empty, Full, combinators::BoxBody)`, `http 1 (StatusCode, HeaderValue, Method, Uri)`, `bytes 1`, `tokio 1 (net incl. TcpSocket for backlog, io-util for copy_bidirectional, sync, time, macros)`, `tokio-util 0.7 (sync::CancellationToken)`, `moka 0.12 (sync::Cache — the history TTLCache)`, `tracing 0.1`, `thiserror 2`, `clap (ValueEnum derive on Strategy; behind the cli feature only)`

| Rust item | ← was | Action | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| `pub struct ProxyPool` | server.py:ProxyPool | port + redesign | Shared as Arc<ProxyPool> across all connection tasks, so every method takes &self, not &mut self. Two locks by design: the sync Mutex guards the in-memory vectors and is NEVER held across an await; the tokio Mutex guards the checker's Receiver (recv() needs &mut) and is only taken on the import path. Lock order is never nested, so no deadlock. Python gets away with one object and no locks because asyncio is single-threaded and its awaits are the only yield points; Rust needs the split to keep `get()` on `&self`. |
| `struct PoolState` | server.py:ProxyPool._pool + ProxyPool._newcomers | port + redesign | `_pool` was a heapq of `(avg_resp_time, proxy)` tuples; it becomes a plain Vec (see `pick_best`). `_newcomers` was a list with `.append()` + `.pop(0)` — that is FIFO, so VecDeque with push_back/pop_front, O(1) instead of O(n). Proxies are stored BY VALUE: the server moves one out via `get()` and moves it back via `put()`. No Arc<Mutex<Proxy>> — the Python only shares the Proxy object because it has no ownership to move. |
| `pub struct PoolConfig` | server.py:ProxyPool.__init__ params | port + redesign | Defaults match Python exactly: min_req_proxy=5, max_error_rate=0.5, max_resp_time=8s, min_queue=5, import_timeout=5.0s, max_import_retries=100. `max_resp_time`/`import_timeout` become Duration instead of bare int/float seconds — the CLI still takes `--max-resp-time SECONDS`. `import_timeout`/`max_import_retries` were `kwargs.get()` smuggled through `Server.__init__` (server.py:222-223) and are not CLI-exposed; keep them as struct fields, no CLI flag, matching Python. |
| `pub enum Strategy` | server.py:ProxyPool.__init__ strategy param | port + redesign | One variant, deliberately. server.py:56-57 does `if strategy != 'best': raise ValueError('`strategy` only support `best` for now.')` — `random` does not exist in the source despite the brief mentioning it and despite `--strategy` being a free-form `type=str` CLI arg (cli.py:273). A one-variant enum is normally the abstraction-for-nothing smell, but here it buys a real thing: clap rejects `--strategy random` at parse time with a usage error instead of Python's runtime ValueError deep inside pool construction. Do not invent Random. |
| `fn rank(p: &Proxy) -> (u32, u32)` | proxy.py:Proxy.priority (dead) + server.py:127 heappush key | port + redesign | Resolves a live contradiction. `Proxy.priority` returns `(error_rate, avg_resp_time)` and is never called by anything; the pool actually pushes `(proxy.avg_resp_time, proxy)` — avg_resp_time ONLY. The serve() docstring (api.py:280-282) and the brief both say the choice is 'based on the percentage of errors and average response time'. Rust implements the documented two-key order (see deviations). Returns integers, not floats: f64 is not Ord, and quantizing error_rate to hundredths matches Python's own `round(..., 2)` (proxy.py:222/244), so the key is a total order with no NaN and no PartialOrd dance. |
| `ProxyPool::new` | server.py:ProxyPool.__init__ | port | Takes the checker's receiving half directly (locked decision 8: bounded mpsc inside, backpressure by capacity). The `if strategy != 'best': raise ValueError` guard is gone — `Strategy` makes it unrepresentable, so `new` is infallible and returns Self, not Result. |
| `ProxyPool::get` | server.py:ProxyPool.get | port + redesign | Three-branch structure preserved: (1) if established.len()+newcomers.len() < min_queue -> import; (2) else if a newcomer matching `scheme` exists -> take it; (3) else pick_best(scheme), falling back to import. Python's `scheme.upper()` normalization is gone — Scheme is an enum, the string was only stringly-typed defense. Branch (2) is where Python's bug lives: it does a bare `self._newcomers.pop(0)` with NO scheme check (server.py:63-64), so `get('HTTPS')` can hand back an HTTP-only proxy, which then detonates in `_choice_proto`'s RuntimeError — a path `_handle` does not catch. Rust filters newcomers by scheme (see deviations). |
| `ProxyPool::import` | server.py:ProxyPool._import | port + redesign | Loop up to max_import_retries: `tokio::time::timeout(cfg.import_timeout, rx.lock().await.recv())`.
