Three outcomes map 1:1 to Python: Err(Elapsed) -> NoProxy::Timeout (was `raise NoProxyError(f'Timeout waiting for proxy with scheme {expected_scheme}')`); Ok(None) = sender dropped -> NoProxy::Exhausted (was the `if not proxy: raise NoProxyError('No more available proxies')` None-sentinel check — locked decision 8 replaces the sentinel with channel close); Ok(Some(p)) with wrong scheme -> `self.put(p)` + retry, exactly as Python. `self._proxies.task_done()` is DELETED — it exists only to drive `Queue.join()` backpressure, which the bounded channel now provides structurally. The recv() await happens while holding only the rx lock, never the state lock, so concurrent `get()`s on a populated pool are not blocked behind an import. |
| `ProxyPool::pick_best` | server.py:ProxyPool.get lines 66-84 (the heap drain/re-push loop) | rewrite | `state.established.iter().enumerate().filter(\|(_, p)\| p.supports(scheme)).min_by_key(\|(_, p)\| rank(p)).map(\|(i, _)\| state.established.swap_remove(i))`. Replaces 19 lines of heappop-into-temp_items-then-heappush-back. Justification for dropping the heap: heapq cannot pop a filtered minimum, so Python drains and rebuilds on every scheme miss — the heap gives it nothing here. The pool holds tens of proxies (min_queue defaults to 5); an O(n) scan over a Vec is unmeasurable next to the HTTP round-trip it precedes, and it makes `remove()` and scheme filtering trivial rather than the O(N log N) drain-and-restore the Python apologizes for in a comment (server.py:140-142). swap_remove is O(1) and order in `established` is meaningless since selection is by rank. |
| `ProxyPool::put` | server.py:ProxyPool.put | port | Same three-way policy: stat.requests < min_req_proxy -> newcomers.push_back(); requests >= min_req_proxy AND (error_rate > max_error_rate OR avg_resp_time > max_resp_time) -> DROP (evict, log at debug: '{host}:{port} removed from proxy pool'); else -> established.push(). Note the eviction predicate is strictly `>` on both bounds in Python (server.py:119-121), not `>=`; preserve that. The `if proxy is None: return` guard is deleted — `Proxy` is not nullable in Rust. Python's local is misnamed `is_exceed_time` though it also covers error rate; name it `is_degraded`. |
| `ProxyPool::remove` | server.py:ProxyPool.remove | port + redesign | Searches newcomers first, then established — same order as Python. Collapses to two `iter().position()` + `remove`/`swap_remove` calls. The entire heap-safe-removal apparatus and its performance apology comment vanish with the heap. Returns Option<Proxy>; the sole caller (the proxycontrol API) ignores the value and always answers 204, exactly like Python. `host` is typed IpAddr, not String — Proxy already guarantees its host is an IP (proxy.py:103-107 raises ValueError otherwise), so the control endpoint parses and 400s on garbage instead of comparing strings that can never match. |
| `pub enum NoProxy` | errors.py:NoProxyError | port + redesign | Python has one NoProxyError raised at three sites distinguished only by message text. Split into variants because the server acts differently on them in principle (Exhausted = shut down; Timeout/Retries = arguably transient), even though the current port treats all three as shutdown to match Python. This is the fatal-vs-per-proxy split from locked decision 11: NoProxy is fatal, it reaches the caller; ProxyError is per-proxy and never does. |
| `pub struct ServerConfig` | server.py:Server.__init__ params | port + redesign | Builder per the global preference — 8 fields, most optional. Defaults match Python: timeout=8s, max_tries=3, backlog=100, prefer_connect=false, http_allowed_codes=[]. `host: str, port: int` collapse to one SocketAddr (Python does `int(port)` at runtime and can ValueError; parsing moves to the CLI boundary). `http_allowed_codes or []` -> Vec, empty means 'do not check', same as Python. `loop=None` and the whole `self._loop` fallback dance (server.py:204-208) are deleted — tokio has no loop handle to pass. `**kwargs` is deleted: it exists only to let `Broker.serve()` splat find()'s args through, and it silently swallows typos. |
| `pub struct Server` | server.py:Server | port + redesign | `self._resolver = Resolver(loop=...)` becomes an injected Arc<Resolver> — the server must share the Broker's resolver (and its cache) rather than constructing a second one, same reasoning as locked decision 10 on judges. `history` moves from module-global to instance field (see deviations). `_connections: dict[Future, (reader, writer)]` is replaced by CancellationToken + JoinSet — the dict exists solely so `stop()` can iterate and `.cancel()`, which is exactly what a token does without the bookkeeping. |
| `Server::bind` | server.py:Server.start (the asyncio.start_server call) | port + redesign | Split from `serve()` so bind errors (EADDRINUSE) surface before the caller commits, and so `local_addr()` is available on port 0. `backlog` needs `tokio::net::TcpSocket::new_v4()/new_v6()?.bind(addr)?.listen(backlog)` — the plain `TcpListener::bind` convenience fn hardcodes 1024 and would silently drop the `--backlog` flag on the floor. No socket2 dep needed; tokio's TcpSocket::listen takes the backlog directly. |
| `Server::local_addr` | server.py:234 self._server.sockets[0].getsockname() | port | Python only reaches for this to log 'Listening established on ...'. Rust exposes it as a method — it is the only way to learn the port under `--port 0`, and integration tests need it. |
| `Server::serve` | server.py:Server.start (accept loop) + Server._accept | port + redesign | `loop { tokio::select! { _ = self.cancel.cancelled() => break, r = listener.accept() => { ... } } }`, spawning each conn into a JoinSet. Per connection: `http1::Builder::new().timer(TokioTimer::new()).serve_connection(TokioIo::new(tcp), service_fn(...)).with_upgrades()`. `with_upgrades()` is on Connection, NOT Builder, so it must chain AFTER serve_connection (research §HTTP stack — the hyper 0.14-vs-1.x trap), and it is mandatory since this server relays CONNECT. Replaces `_accept`'s `add_done_callback(_on_completion)` closure: hyper's Connection future closes the socket on drop, so the callback's manual `writer.close()` and `self._connections.pop(f)` are gone. `_on_completion`'s `raise exc` inside a done-callback (server.py:299) — which asyncio can only hand to the loop exception handler — becomes a `tracing::warn!` on the joined task's Err. |
| `Server::shutdown_token` | server.py:Server.stop + Server.aclose + __aenter__/__aexit__ | merge | Four Python lifecycle members collapse to one token. `stop()` (sync, cancels conns, closes, then `self._loop.stop()`) and `aclose()` (async, identical minus the loop kill) are the same operation duplicated because `stop()` is unusable from async context — the async-context-manager pair exists purely to route callers to the non-loop-killing one. In Rust `serve()` is a future: cancel the token or drop the future. The `await asyncio.sleep(0.5)` grace hack in both paths is replaced by awaiting the JoinSet (or a real bounded `graceful_shutdown`), which is deterministic rather than a guess. |
| `async fn handle` | server.py:Server._handle | split | Python's `_handle` is 140 lines doing five jobs: request parsing, control-API dispatch, proto choice, the retry loop, and stream teardown. Split into `control::dispatch` (early return), `identify_scheme`, and the `for attempt in 0..max_tries` loop calling `attempt()`. The hyper service must return a Response, which is a forcing improvement: Python falls off the end of the retry loop and just closes the socket with no response at all when every attempt fails (see deviations). `peer` is passed in from `accept()` — Python reaches through `client_reader._transport.get_extra_info('peername')[0]`, a private-attribute hack it repeats at server.py:338 and 391. |
| `pub enum Scheme` | server.py:Server._identify_scheme return value ('HTTP' \| 'HTTPS') | port + redesign | Two strings that flow through get()/put()/_stream/_check_response/_choice_proto as stringly-typed tags. As an enum, `scheme.upper()` normalization and the `scheme and not checked` truthiness test both evaporate. Shared with pool.rs (Proxy::supports(Scheme)) — Python's `Proxy.schemes` property (proxy.py:225-234) computes the same thing from the types dict. |
| `fn identify_scheme` | server.py:Server._identify_scheme | port | `if method == CONNECT { Https } else { Http }`. Trivially preserved. Reads hyper's typed Method instead of `headers['Method']` from the hand-rolled parser. |
| `fn choose_proto` | server.py:Server._choice_proto | port + redesign | Returns Option, not a RuntimeError. Priority order preserved exactly: HTTP scheme -> [Connect80 if prefer_connect && supported] then [Http, Connect80, Socks5, Socks4]; HTTPS scheme -> [Https, Socks5, Socks4]. Note CONNECT:25 is unreachable here in both languages — it is a checker-only type. Python raises RuntimeError when nothing matches (server.py:471/479), and NOTHING catches it: `_handle`'s except list covers only Proxy*/BadStatus/BadResponse/ErrorOnStream, so it escapes to the done-callback. It is currently only reachable via the newcomers-scheme bug; making it a None that skips to the next attempt means the fix and the crash-proofing are independent. Uses NegotiatorKind (locked decision 6, closed set of 6) rather than the `proxy.ngtr = proto` string-keyed NGTRS[proto] factory. |
| `async fn attempt` | server.py:Server._handle lines 362-446 (the for/try/except/else/finally body) | split | One iteration of the retry loop, extracted so the loop body is readable and testable. Maps Python's try/except/else/finally: the `except (ProxyTimeoutError, ProxyConnError, ProxyRecvError, ProxySendError, ProxyEmptyRecvError, BadStatusError, BadResponseError): continue` block becomes `Err(ProxyError) => continue` at the call site (locked decision 11 — these never reach the caller, they are histogram keys). The `finally: proxy.log(...); proxy.close(); self._proxy_pool.put(proxy)` runs at the call site instead — Rust has no finally, and put() must move the proxy, so it cannot live inside `attempt`. `proxy.close()` is the Drop impl on the upstream stream. |
| `async fn open_upstream` | server.py:Server._handle lines 371-388 (proxy.connect + ngtr.negotiate) + proxy.py:Proxy.connect + negotiators.py:NGTRS dispatch | port + redesign | The one genuinely shared piece with the checker: TcpStream::connect -> tokio-socks connect_with_socket / hand-rolled CONNECT / no-op for HTTP (locked decision 5), returning the negotiated stream ready for TokioIo. This must be ONE function owned by the negotiator module and called from both here and the checker — Python duplicates the sequencing between `checker.py` and `server.py:_handle`. Preserves Python's local DNS resolution for SOCKS/CONNECT protos (server.py:377 `ip = await self._resolver.resolve(host)`) rather than passing a hostname target to the proxy: it means the SOCKS proxy never sees the destination name, and tokio-socks' IntoTargetAddr takes a SocketAddr happily. See open questions on ownership. |
| `async fn tunnel` | server.py:Server._stream (both directions, CONNECT/SOCKS case) + the CONNECTED const write | rewrite | Reply 200 to the client, then `hyper::upgrade::on(&mut res)` -> Upgraded -> `Upgraded::downcast::<TokioIo<TcpStream>>()` -> `tokio::io::copy_bidirectional`. Replaces the two hand-rolled `_stream` tasks + `asyncio.gather` + the manual `for task in stream: task.cancel()` teardown. LOAD-BEARING GOTCHA (research §HTTP stack, verified): `Parts` from downcast carries `read_buf: Bytes` — bytes hyper already read past the CONNECT request — and it MUST be written to the upstream before copying starts or the tunnel silently corrupts. Python cannot hit this because it never parses; hyper porters hit it constantly. The `CONNECTED = b'HTTP/1.1 200 Connection established\r\n\r\n'` const is deleted — hyper serializes the 200 from a typed Response. |
| `async fn forward_http` | server.py:Server._stream (HTTP case) + _check_response + _inject_headers | rewrite | `hyper::client::conn::http1::handshake(TokioIo::new(upstream))` -> spawn the Connection -> `sender.send_request(req)`. Three Python functions die here: (1) `_stream`'s read/write/drain loop -> hyper's Incoming body streams through, and `length=65536` chunking is hyper's problem; (2) `_check_response` -> `res.status().as_u16()`, so parse_status_line/BadStatusLine/BadResponseError are unreachable; (3) `_inject_headers` -> `res.headers_mut().insert("x-proxy-info", proxy_info)` instead of splicing bytes after the first `\r\n`. Request-target: hyper serializes the URI as-is and does not validate it (research, verbatim-verified), so absolute-form for the HTTP-proto path and origin-form through tunnels is a direct choice, not a fight. |
| `fn check_status` | server.py:Server._check_response | port | `if scheme == Http && !allowed.is_empty() && !allowed.contains(&status.as_u16()) { Err(ProxyError::BadStatus) }`. Semantics preserved exactly, including that HTTPS is never checked — the Python docstring says so outright ('Checks only for HTTP protocol, HTTPS not supported at the moment', api.py:336) because through a tunnel there is no status to read. Byte-splitting on `\r\n` and the BadStatusLine->BadResponseError remap are gone; hyper already rejected an unparseable status line. |
| `mod control` | server.py:Server._handle lines 319-360 (the `if headers['Host'] == 'proxycontrol'` block) | split | 40 lines of nested control-plane logic inline in the middle of the relay path becomes its own module. Returns Option: Some = handled, None = fall through to proxying. Routes preserved: `/api/remove/<host>:<port>` -> pool.remove + 204; `/api/history/url:<url>` -> 204 when absent, else 200 with `{"proxy": "h:p"}` + the exact CORS headers (Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *, Access-Control-Allow-Credentials: true). Python's `headers['Path'].split('/', 5)[3:]` + 3-way unpack raises ValueError on any short path, and unknown _api/_operation/query_type values fall THROUGH to the proxy path and try to proxy `http://proxycontrol/...`. Rust matches on path segments and 400/404s (see deviations). |
| `struct History` | server.py:26 `history = TTLCache(maxsize=10000, ttl=600)` (module-global) | port + redesign | moka with max_capacity(10_000) + time_to_live(600s) reproduces TTLCache's exact parameters in three lines. Key is a typed tuple, not the f-string `f'{peer_ip}-{path}'` — which is ambiguous if a path contains '-' and requires the private `_transport` reach-through at both the read (server.py:338) and write (server.py:391) sites. Written just before relay starts, same point as Python. Moves from module-global to a Server field for the same reason locked decision 10 moves Judge.available/ev: two Servers in one process currently share one cache and read each other's entries. |
| `pub enum ServerError` | errors.py:NoProxyError + the un-caught RuntimeError/ValueError paths | port + redesign | The fatal half of locked decision 11 for this module — errors the caller can act on. Per-proxy failures use the shared `ProxyError` (ConnFailed/Timeout/Reset/EmptyRecv/BadStatus/BadResponse/Resolve) from the errors module; server.py catches exactly those seven plus ErrorOnStream. `ErrorOnStream` itself is dropped — it is a wrapper that exists only so `_handle` can distinguish 'failed during relay' from 'failed during setup', which in Rust is just which function returned the Err. |
| `impl Default for ServerConfig + ServerConfigBuilder` | server.py:Server.__init__ default arguments | write fresh | Python gets defaults free from keyword args; Rust needs Default + a builder (global preference: builder for many-optional-field construction). Values are the Python defaults verbatim so `Broker::serve()` with no options behaves identically. |

<details><summary><b>Proposed signatures</b></summary>

```rust
// pub struct ProxyPool  ← server.py:ProxyPool
pub struct ProxyPool { cfg: PoolConfig, state: std::sync::Mutex<PoolState>, rx: tokio::sync::Mutex<mpsc::Receiver<Proxy>> }
// struct PoolState  ← server.py:ProxyPool._pool + ProxyPool._newcomers
struct PoolState { established: Vec<Proxy>, newcomers: VecDeque<Proxy> }
// pub struct PoolConfig  ← server.py:ProxyPool.__init__ params
pub struct PoolConfig { pub strategy: Strategy, pub min_req_proxy: usize, pub max_error_rate: f64, pub max_resp_time: Duration, pub min_queue: usize, pub import_timeout: Duration, pub max_import_retries: usize }
// pub enum Strategy  ← server.py:ProxyPool.__init__ strategy param
#[derive(Default, Clone, Copy, clap::ValueEnum)] pub enum Strategy { #[default] Best }
// fn rank(p: &Proxy) -> (u32, u32)  ← proxy.py:Proxy.priority (dead) + server.py:127 heappush key
fn rank(p: &Proxy) -> (u32, u32)  // (error_rate * 100, avg_resp_time_ms); lower is better
// ProxyPool::new  ← server.py:ProxyPool.__init__
pub fn new(rx: mpsc::Receiver<Proxy>, cfg: PoolConfig) -> Self
// ProxyPool::get  ← server.py:ProxyPool.get
pub async fn get(&self, scheme: Scheme) -> Result<Proxy, NoProxy>
// ProxyPool::import  ← server.py:ProxyPool._import
async fn import_one(&self, want: Scheme) -> Result<Proxy, NoProxy>
// ProxyPool::pick_best  ← server.py:ProxyPool.get lines 66-84 (the heap drain/re-push loop)
fn pick_best(state: &mut PoolState, scheme: Scheme) -> Option<Proxy>
// ProxyPool::put  ← server.py:ProxyPool.put
pub fn put(&self, proxy: Proxy)
// ProxyPool::remove  ← server.py:ProxyPool.remove
pub fn remove(&self, host: IpAddr, port: u16) -> Option<Proxy>
// pub enum NoProxy  ← errors.py:NoProxyError
#[derive(Debug, thiserror::Error)] #[non_exhaustive] pub enum NoProxy { #[error("no more available proxies")] Exhausted, #[error("timeout waiting for proxy with scheme {0:?}")] Timeout(Scheme), #[error("exceeded max retries ({0}) finding proxy")] Retries(usize) }
// pub struct ServerConfig  ← server.py:Server.__init__ params
pub struct ServerConfig { pub addr: SocketAddr, pub timeout: Duration, pub max_tries: usize, pub backlog: u32, pub prefer_connect: bool, pub http_allowed_codes: Vec<u16>, pub pool: PoolConfig }
// pub struct Server  ← server.py:Server
pub struct Server { cfg: Arc<ServerConfig>, pool: Arc<ProxyPool>, resolver: Arc<Resolver>, history: History, listener: TcpListener, cancel: CancellationToken }
// Server::bind  ← server.py:Server.start (the asyncio.start_server call)
pub async fn bind(cfg: ServerConfig, rx: mpsc::Receiver<Proxy>) -> Result<Server, ServerError>
// Server::local_addr  ← server.py:234 self._server.sockets[0].getsockname()
pub fn local_addr(&self) -> SocketAddr
// Server::serve  ← server.py:Server.start (accept loop) + Server._accept
pub async fn serve(self) -> Result<(), ServerError>
// Server::shutdown_token  ← server.py:Server.stop + Server.aclose + __aenter__/__aexit__
pub fn shutdown_token(&self) -> CancellationToken
// async fn handle  ← server.py:Server._handle
async fn handle(req: Request<Incoming>, ctx: Arc<Ctx>, peer: IpAddr) -> Result<Response<BoxBody<Bytes, hyper::Error>>, Infallible>
// pub enum Scheme  ← server.py:Server._identify_scheme return value ('HTTP' | 'HTTPS')
#[derive(Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, Debug)] pub enum Scheme { Http, Https }
// fn identify_scheme  ← server.py:Server._identify_scheme
fn identify_scheme(req: &Request<Incoming>) -> Scheme
// fn choose_proto  ← server.py:Server._choice_proto
fn choose_proto(proxy: &Proxy, scheme: Scheme, prefer_connect: bool) -> Option<NegotiatorKind>
// async fn attempt  ← server.py:Server._handle lines 362-446 (the for/try/except/else/finally body)
async fn attempt(proxy: &mut Proxy, req: ..., scheme: Scheme, ctx: &Ctx) -> Result<Response<...>, ProxyError>
// async fn open_upstream  ← server.py:Server._handle lines 371-388 (proxy.connect + ngtr.negotiate) + proxy.py:Proxy.connect + negotiators.py:NGTRS dispatch
async fn open_upstream(proxy: &Proxy, kind: NegotiatorKind, target: (String, u16), resolver: &Resolver, timeout: Duration) -> Result<TcpStream, ProxyError>
// async fn tunnel  ← server.py:Server._stream (both directions, CONNECT/SOCKS case) + the CONNECTED const write
async fn tunnel(upgraded: Upgraded, upstream: TcpStream, timeout: Duration) -> Result<(), ProxyError>
// async fn forward_http  ← server.py:Server._stream (HTTP case) + _check_response + _inject_headers
async fn forward_http(upstream: TcpStream, req: Request<Incoming>, scheme: Scheme, allowed: &[u16], proxy_info: HeaderValue) -> Result<Response<...>, ProxyError>
// fn check_status  ← server.py:Server._check_response
fn check_status(status: StatusCode, scheme: Scheme, allowed: &[u16]) -> Result<(), ProxyError>
// mod control  ← server.py:Server._handle lines 319-360 (the `if headers['Host'] == 'proxycontrol'` block)
pub(crate) async fn dispatch(req: &Request<Incoming>, peer: IpAddr, pool: &ProxyPool, history: &History) -> Option<Response<...>>
// struct History  ← server.py:26 `history = TTLCache(maxsize=10000, ttl=600)` (module-global)
struct History(moka::sync::Cache<(IpAddr, String), String>)  // key: (peer, path) -> "host:port"
// pub enum ServerError  ← errors.py:NoProxyError + the un-caught RuntimeError/ValueError paths
#[derive(Debug, thiserror::Error)] #[non_exhaustive] pub enum ServerError { #[error("bind failed")] Bind(#[source] std::io::Error), #[error(transparent)] NoProxy(#[from] NoProxy) }
// impl Default for ServerConfig + ServerConfigBuilder  ← server.py:Server.__init__ default arguments
ServerConfig::builder().addr(a).max_tries(3).build()
```
</details>

**Open questions**

- Who owns `open_upstream` (TcpStream::connect -> negotiate -> ready stream)? Both the checker and this server need the identical sequence, and Python duplicates it. It should live in the negotiators module and be called from both, but that module's map is being designed in parallel — needs reconciling so the signature and the ProxyError mapping match. This is the single hardest cross-module contract in the port.
- What is the Proxy mutation API the server calls? Python does `proxy.stat['requests'] += 1` inside `proxy.connect()` (proxy.py:400) and appends runtimes via `proxy.log(msg, stime, err)` (proxy.py:322-335) — so the server records stats as a side effect of connecting, plus one explicit `proxy.log(request.decode(), stime, err=err)` in the finally. The Rust Proxy needs an explicit method (`record_attempt(runtime: Option<Duration>, err: Option<ProxyError>)`) since open_upstream may not own the Proxy. Owned by the proxy module's map. Also note `proxy.log(request.decode(), ...)` can raise UnicodeDecodeError on a binary request line; Rust should log lossily.
- Does the 8s idle timeout stay on tunnels? server.py:488 wraps EVERY read in both directions in `asyncio.wait_for(..., self._timeout)`, so an idle CONNECT tunnel is killed after 8 seconds — websockets, long-poll, and SSE through the local server all die. I have preserved this faithfully rather than deviating, because a tunnel with no timeout is a resource-leak vector. But it is very likely a latent bug rather than a decision, and the fix (separate idle vs. handshake timeouts) is cheap. Want it?
- What mpsc capacity does `serve(limit=100)` map to? Python's `_proxies` queue is UNBOUNDED (api.py:82) — its backpressure is entirely the join()-based pause, and `limit` gates when the pause engages, not how much is buffered. With a bounded channel the two roles merge and I do not have a principled mapping. This is the api/Broker module's call; the pool just holds the Receiver. Flagging because the pause semantics deviation above depends on it.
- Should `Broker::serve()` return a JoinHandle, a future, or block? Python's `serve()` is sync and calls `self._loop.run_until_complete(run_server())`, which starts the server and spawns `find(limit=limit)` — so `serve()` returns while the server runs, and the caller is expected to have started the loop. The Rust equivalent is api's decision; `Server::bind` + `Server::serve` is designed to support any of the three.
- Is evicting on `error_rate > max_error_rate` strictly-greater correct? Python uses `>` (server.py:119-121) while the CLI help says 'the maximum percentage', which reads as `>=` (a proxy at exactly 0.5 survives a --max-error-rate 0.5). Preserved as `>`. Trivially changed if the docs are the intent, but unlike the ranking bug there is no dead code corroborating either reading, so I am not calling it.

---

### src/provider/mod.rs + src/provider/spec.rs + src/provider/registry.rs (+ src/provider/custom/*.rs)

Python's `Provider` base + 28 subclasses collapse into a two-variant runtime enum: `Provider::Spec(ProviderSpec)` — a fully `Deserialize` description (`Plan` = which URLs/how to request them, `Parse` = how to turn a page into (host,port)) — and `Provider::Custom(Arc<dyn CustomProvider>)`, the async-trait escape hatch. After dropping the 8 measured-dead registry entries, exactly 5 custom impls remain (spys.ru, xseo.in, nntime.com, gatherproxy.com, tools.rosinstrument.com) covering 6 registry rows; everything else — including all 18 bare providers, both blogspot crawlers, checkerproxy, webanetlabs, maxiproxies, my-proxy, aliveproxy, proxylistplus, proxy-list.org (base64) and gatherproxy's socks POST — is a YAML row. The bundled registry is one `include_str!`-embedded `providers.yaml` parsed at `Registry::default()`, which doubles as the reference doc and as the file users copy into a `--provider-dir`; `provider_utils.py`'s SimpleProvider/PaginatedProvider/APIProvider/ConfigurableProvider are not four types in Rust, they are `Plan::Single`/`Plan::Pages`/`Plan::Single{headers}+Parse::Json`/`ProviderSpec: Deserialize` respectively.

**Crates:** `reqwest 0.13 (default-features = false; scraping half of the split stack per decision 4)`, `serde 1 (derive)`, `serde_norway 0.9 (YAML; serde_yaml is deprecated/archived — see open_questions)`, `serde_json 1 (Parse::Json, Parse::Auto, .json config files)`, `serde_regex 1.1 (Regex fields in ProviderSpec)`, `regex 1.11`, `url 2.5 (serde feature)`, `base64 0.22 (Parse::Base64HostPort, proxy-list.org)`, `percent-encoding 2.3 (rosinstrument's unquote)`, `html-escape 0.2 (rosinstrument's html.unescape)`, `async-trait 0.1 (CustomProvider — async fn in trait is not dyn-compatible)`, `tokio 1 (sync feature: Semaphore, per decision 9)`, `futures 0.3 (join_all in fetch_pages)`, `thiserror 2 (decision 11)`, `tracing 0.1`

| Rust item | ← was | Action | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| `pub struct ProviderSpec` | providers.py:Provider (the data half of __init__: url, proto, max_conn, max_tries, timeout) | port + redesign | Locked decision 7: a dead provider must be a config edit. Everything Python passed to `Provider(...)` or encoded in a subclass body becomes fields. `name` replaces Python's `domain` attribute (which was derived from urlparse(url).netloc, and which subclasses hand-hacked into uniqueness with the `"blogspot.com^socks"` / `"tools.rosinstrument.com^socks"` caret suffix — see dropped). `deny_unknown_fields` so a typo in a user YAML is an error, not a silently-ignored key. Defaults mirror Python: max_conn=4, max_tries=3, timeout=20s. |
| `pub enum Plan` | providers.py:Provider._pipe + all ~14 subclass _pipe overrides | port + redesign | `_pipe` is a method in Python only because Python has no sum type. Measured against every surviving subclass: Single covers the 18 bare providers + Xseo-style POST-with-form + Gatherproxy_com_socks; Urls covers Aliveproxy_com (16 hardcoded paths) and Proxylistplus_com (3 names x 6 pages cartesian, 18 URLs, expanded at authoring time in the YAML); Pages covers Nntime/rosinstrument/free-proxy.cz-style `tpl % n` AND provider_utils.PaginatedProvider; Crawl covers the 8-way `fetch seed -> regex links -> prefix with base -> fetch all` shape (Blogspot_com, Blogspot_com_socks, Webanetlabs_net, Checkerproxy_net, Maxiproxies_com, My_proxy_com, Proxy_list_org). `seeds: Vec<Url>` (not one seed) because Blogspot_com_base gathers 4 domains; `base: Option<String>` because Blogspot's extracted hrefs are already absolute while webanetlabs'/checkerproxy's are paths needing a prefix; `include_seeds` because Proxy_list_org and My_proxy_com append the seed URL back into the fetch list. `Builtin { id }` is how the escape hatch is spelled in YAML — resolved by Registry against a fixed table, so YAML cannot name arbitrary code. |
| `pub enum Parse` | providers.py:Provider.find_proxies/_find_proxies/_pattern + subclass overrides; provider_utils.py:SimpleProvider.find_proxies/APIProvider.find_proxies | port + redesign | Python's second extension point (`find_proxies`) becomes the second field. Default = the ip:port scanner (Provider.find_proxies). Regex = a 2-capture (host)(port) pattern, replacing `_pattern` overrides and SimpleProvider(pattern=...). Base64HostPort = Proxy_list_org's `Proxy\('([\w=]+)'\)` -> b64decode -> rsplit(':') — the only surviving base64 provider. Json{path} merges APIProvider's proxy_path walk + SimpleProvider._parse_json. Auto = SimpleProvider format="auto": try serde_json, else fall through to Default. IMPORTANT: `regex` has no lookaround, so `Parse::Regex` patterns cannot use Python's `(?=...)` trick — see deviations. |
| `pub fn parse::find_ip_port(page: &str) -> Vec<(String, String)>` | providers.py:Provider.find_proxies + utils.py:IPPortPatternGlobal / IPv6BracketedPortPattern / canonicalize_ip | port + redesign | Hand-written two-pass scanner, NOT a direct regex port. Python's IPPortPatternGlobal is `(?P<ip>v4)(?=.*?(?:(?:v4)\|(?P<port>\d{2,5})))` with DOTALL — it pairs each IPv4 with the next 2-5 digit run occurring BEFORE the next IPv4, and yields an empty port (later dropped by the proxies setter) when another IP comes first. That lookahead is inexpressible in the `regex` crate. Reimplement literally: (1) collect IPv4 match spans and `\d{2,5}` spans with two lookaround-free regexes, (2) for each IP take the first digit-run starting after its end and before the next IP's start. Same semantics, linear, no fancy-regex dep. Keep Python's IPv6 handling: mask `[v6]:port` spans before the IPv4 pass (so `[::ffff:192.0.2.1]:8080` does not also emit a phantom IPv4 entry), then emit the bracketed v6 entries with canonicalize_ip applied. |
| `pub fn parse::pair_hosts_with_ports(text: &str, host_re: &Regex, port_re: &Regex) -> Vec<(String, String)>` | providers.py:Gatherproxy_com._pattern_h, Nntime_com._pattern, Tools_rosinstrument_com_base._pattern | port + redesign | All three custom `_pattern`s are the same lookahead-pairing algorithm as IPPortPatternGlobal with a different host token (rosinstrument also accepts bare hostnames `[a-z0-9\-.]+\.[a-z]{2,6}`) and a different port token (gatherproxy's port is `'[\d\w]+'` hex-in-quotes). Factor the pairing loop out once and let find_ip_port and the three custom providers pass their own token regexes. Without this the same lookaround problem has to be solved four times. |
| `pub trait CustomProvider` | new (the escape hatch for the 5 providers whose _pipe/find_proxies is real code) | write fresh | One method, one hatch, per research.md. `#[async_trait]` is required — async fn in trait is stable since 1.75 but still not dyn-compatible, and this must be `Arc<dyn>` to live in a heterogeneous registry. One Box per provider fetch is unmeasurable next to an HTTP round-trip. Impls get `ProviderCtx` so they reuse the same client/semaphore/retry as the spec driver — a custom provider is a custom _pipe, not a custom HTTP stack. No closure sugar (`impl CustomProvider for FnProvider<F>`) until someone asks: one impl of speculative sugar is the abstraction the brief tells me not to write. |
| `pub enum Provider` | providers.py:Provider (the runtime half) | port + redesign | Replaces Python's class hierarchy. `Clone` is cheap (Arc / regex-Arc-inside). Deliberately NOT `dyn Provider` for everything: 33 of 38 entries are data and must round-trip through YAML, which closures and trait objects cannot do. |
| `impl Provider { pub fn name(&self) -> &str; pub fn proto(&self) -> &[Proto]; pub fn supports(&self, want: &BTreeSet<Proto>) -> bool }` | providers.py:Provider.domain / .proto; api.py:_grab._get_tasks filter `not pr.proto or bool(pr.proto & types.keys())` | port | `supports` returns true when the provider declares no proto (Python's `not pr.proto` — meaning 'unknown, try it') or when the declared protos intersect the requested ones. Lives here rather than in the broker so the intersection is typed (`Proto`, not a str set) — this is what kills the `proto=("SOCKS4")` bug (see deviations). |
| `impl Provider { pub async fn fetch(&self, ctx: &ProviderCtx<'_>) -> Vec<Seed> }` | providers.py:Provider.get_proxies + _pipe + _find_on_page + the `proxies` property/setter | port + redesign | Returns owned deduped seeds instead of Python's mutate-`self._proxies`-then-return-the-same-set-forever. Python's `Provider` accumulates into `self._proxies` across grab cycles and `get_proxies()` re-returns everything ever seen, so in serve mode every cycle re-feeds the checker every proxy it already saw (the broker's `unique_proxies` dict papers over it). Rust: `&self`, no interior state, dedupe via `HashSet<Seed>` scoped to the call. Never returns Err — a whole-provider failure is 'this provider yielded nothing', logged and counted, exactly as in Python where get_proxies cannot meaningfully raise. |
| `pub struct Seed` | providers.py:Provider.proxies setter tuple `(host, port, self.proto)` | port + redesign | `host: String` not `IpAddr` — Tools_rosinstrument's pattern matches bare hostnames (`domainOrIP`) and Python's Proxy.create resolves them; narrowing to IpAddr here would silently drop that provider's output. `port: u16` parsed at the provider boundary (Python kept it a str and let `Proxy.__init__`'s `int(port)` raise downstream); unparseable/out-of-range ports are dropped with a debug log, which is what Python's `if port` filter half-did. `Arc<[Proto]>` so the per-provider proto list is shared across its thousands of seeds instead of cloned. |
| `pub struct ProviderCtx<'a>` | providers.py:Provider._session / _sem_provider / _max_tries / _timeout / _cookies / utils.py:get_headers | port + redesign | Python builds a brand-new `aiohttp.ClientSession` per provider per grab cycle (`async with aiohttp.ClientSession(...) as self._session`), throwing away the connection pool every time. Rust shares ONE `reqwest::Client` (decision 4) across all providers; the per-provider `tokio::sync::Semaphore(max_conn)` is the only per-provider state, which is what Python's `_sem_provider` actually was. `get_headers()` becomes `Client::builder().user_agent(...).default_headers(...)` at construction — it is a constant, not per-request state. |
| `impl ProviderCtx<'_> { pub async fn fetch_page(&self, req: &PageRequest) -> Result<String, FetchError> }` | providers.py:Provider.get + Provider._get | port + redesign | Acquires the semaphore, sends, retries up to max_tries. Python's `get()` loops `for _ in range(max_tries): page = await self._get(...); if page: break` — no backoff, and it retries a legitimate 200-with-empty-body as if it were a failure (3 fetches of an empty page), and with max_tries=0 it raises UnboundLocalError on the unbound `page`. Rust retries only on Err; a 200 with an empty body is a successful empty page. `_get`'s swallow-everything-return-"" becomes a typed `FetchError` the caller decides about. Non-200 -> `FetchError::BadStatus(u16)` (Python's BadStatusError). |
| `impl ProviderCtx<'_> { pub async fn fetch_pages(&self, reqs: Vec<PageRequest>) -> Vec<String> }` | providers.py:Provider._find_on_pages | port | Dedupes reqs (Python does `urls = set(urls)` — but only when the list isn't dicts, so its POST-form URL lists were never deduped; Rust dedupes uniformly via Hash on PageRequest), then `join_all`, dropping and logging failures. Concurrency is bounded by the semaphore inside fetch_page, same as Python. Public so custom providers use the identical fetch path. |
| `pub struct PageRequest` | providers.py: the `{'url':…, 'data':…, 'method':…, 'headers':…}` dicts passed to _find_on_pages | port + redesign | Python overloaded the url list to hold either a str or a kwargs dict and branched on `isinstance(urls[0], dict)` — checking only the FIRST element's type to decide for the whole list. One struct, no isinstance. `form` is always urlencoded (aiohttp's `data=dict` behavior); no provider posts a body of any other kind. |
| `pub enum Method` | providers.py: the `method="GET"`/`"POST"` string params | port + redesign | Closed set of 2 — GET and POST are the only methods any provider uses. Not `reqwest::Method`, because that isn't Deserialize-friendly for a YAML enum and would admit DELETE for a proxy-list scraper. |
| `fn spec::run(spec: &ProviderSpec, ctx: &ProviderCtx<'_>) -> Vec<Seed>` | providers.py:Provider._pipe dispatch | write fresh | The interpreter: match Plan -> build Vec<PageRequest> (for Crawl: fetch seeds, run `link` regex over the concatenation, prefix with `base`, optionally append the seeds), fetch, run Parse over each page, collect Seeds. This function is the whole reason 33 of 38 providers need zero code. |
| `fn spec::expand_pages(url: &str, page_param: &str, start: u32, count: u32, step: u32) -> Result<Vec<Url>, SpecError>` | provider_utils.py:PaginatedProvider._build_page_url / _page_range / _replace_query_param | port | Same three rules: `{page}` placeholder -> substitute (Python used bare `{}`; renamed to `{page}` because `{}` in YAML reads as an empty flow-mapping and needs quoting); existing `?<page_param>=` -> REPLACE the value via `Url::query_pairs_mut().clear()`-rebuild (never append a duplicate param); otherwise append `?<page_param>=N`. Python's `_page_range` is `range(start, start + max_pages*step, step)`; keep, renaming max_pages -> count since it is an exact count, not a max. |
| `fn spec::parse_page(parse: &Parse, page: &str) -> Vec<(String, String)>` | providers.py:Provider.find_proxies; provider_utils.py:SimpleProvider.find_proxies / APIProvider.find_proxies | merge | One match arm per Parse variant. Base64HostPort: for each capture-1, base64::engine::general_purpose::STANDARD decode -> utf8 -> rsplit_once(':') (Python used `.split(':')` and blindly indexed [0],[1], which would IndexError on a decode without a colon — the pipeline's blanket try/except swallowed it and dropped the whole page). Regex: require exactly 2 capture groups, validated at load time. Python's SimpleProvider tolerated 0/1-group patterns by rpartition-ing the whole match on ':' — dropped, a config error should be an error. |
| `fn spec::parse_json(page: &str, path: Option<&str>) -> Vec<(String, String)>` | provider_utils.py:APIProvider._load_api_json/_walk_proxy_path/_resolve_proxy_items/_extract_from_list + SimpleProvider._parse_json/_unwrap_json_proxy_list/_extract_json_proxy_items/_extract_json_proxy_item/_extract_proxy_from_mapping | merge | The two Python implementations of this are near-duplicates that disagree in three places: ip field lists (`ip,host,address,proxy` vs `ip,host,address,proxy_ip`), port field lists (`port,p` vs `port,proxy_port,p`), and wrapper keys (`proxies,data,results,items,list` vs the same minus `list`). Unify on the union of each. `path` is dotted (`data.proxies`); Python's `_walk_proxy_path` did `data = data.get(key, data)` — a missing key silently kept the parent and kept walking, so a typo'd path scraped the whole document instead of erroring. Rust: a missing path segment yields zero seeds and logs a warning. Item may be an object (`{ip, port}`) or a bare `"h:p"` string, per both Python impls. Falls back to the Default scanner over the raw text when the body is not JSON (APIProvider did; SimpleProvider._parse_json returned [] instead — take the more useful behavior). |
| `pub struct Registry` | providers.py:PROVIDERS (module-level list) | port + redesign | Owned value, not a global. Python's PROVIDERS is a list of ALREADY-CONSTRUCTED Provider instances holding an asyncio.Semaphore built at import time against whatever loop happened to exist — the reason `Provider.__init__` has that `try: get_running_loop() except RuntimeError` dance. Registry holds inert descriptions; ctx/semaphores are built per Broker. |
| `impl Default for Registry (via pub fn Registry::bundled() -> Registry)` | providers.py:PROVIDERS literal | port + redesign | `serde_norway::from_str(include_str!("../../data/providers.yaml")).expect("bundled registry is valid")` — the expect is guarded by a unit test that parses it and asserts every regex compiles, every Url parses, every Builtin id resolves, and every Parse::Regex has 2 capture groups, so the panic is unreachable in a shipped build. Chose embedded YAML over build.rs codegen and over a const Rust literal because: (1) the file IS the reference doc for the user-facing config schema — a divergence between the bundled registry format and the --provider-dir format is a bug generator; (2) users copy it, delete rows, and point --provider-dir at it; (3) build.rs is speculative complexity for a ~1ms one-shot parse of 30 rows. The regex compiles dominate that ms and a build.rs would not avoid them. |
| `impl Registry { pub fn load_file(path: &Path) -> Result<Registry, RegistryError> }` | provider_utils.py:ConfigurableProvider.from_config | port + redesign | Dispatch on extension: .yaml/.yml -> serde_norway, .json -> serde_json. Python's from_config took a single-provider mapping and hand-rolled a type switch with per-type kwarg plumbing (`if provider_type == 'simple': SimpleProvider(...) elif 'paginated': ... elif 'api': ... else: raise ValueError`) — 60 lines that `#[serde(tag="kind")]` does for free and better (unknown kind, missing url, and wrong-typed fields all become one typed serde error with a line number). DEVIATION: a file is a LIST of providers, not one (see deviations). |
| `impl Registry { pub fn load_dir(dir: &Path) -> Result<Registry, RegistryError> }` | provider_utils.py:load_provider_configs_from_directory + _iter_provider_config_paths + _load_provider_config | port | Keeps every Python behavior that matters: glob *.yaml/*.yml/*.json only (never executes anything — safe for a Docker bind-mount, which is the documented contract), sorted for determinism, skip files starting with `_` so users disable a config by renaming, a missing directory is a warning + empty result (not an error), and a per-file parse error is logged and skipped so one bad file doesn't kill the run. Rust adds: the error carries the file path and serde's line/column, which the Python log line did not. |
| `impl Registry { pub fn merge(&mut self, other: Registry); pub fn push_custom(&mut self, p: Arc<dyn CustomProvider>); pub fn retain(&mut self, f: impl FnMut(&Provider) -> bool); pub fn iter(&self) -> impl Iterator<Item = &Provider>; pub fn is_empty(&self) -> bool }` | api.py:Broker._resolve_providers (`base_providers = list(PROVIDERS) if providers is None else list(providers)` then `.extend(load_provider_configs_from_directory(d))`) | port + redesign | Python encoded 'use defaults / use exactly this / append dirs' in a None-vs-[] sentinel inside Broker.__init__ and documented the subtlety in an 8-line comment. Rust: `Registry::bundled()` or `Registry::default()`+`merge`, explicit at the call site, no sentinel. `push_custom` is the library-user extension point that replaces load_python_providers_from_directory. `retain` is how a user disables providers programmatically. |
| `fn registry::resolve_builtin(id: &str) -> Option<Arc<dyn CustomProvider>>` | new (needed because Plan::Builtin is a YAML string) | write fresh | A `match` over the 6 builtin ids (spys_ru, xseo_in, nntime_com, gatherproxy_com, rosinstrument, rosinstrument_socks). Closed set — YAML can reference the escape hatches (and disable them by deleting the row) but cannot name arbitrary code. Unknown id -> RegistryError::UnknownBuiltin, listing the valid ids. |
| `pub struct SpysRu (impl CustomProvider)` | providers.py:Spys_ru | port | ESCAPE HATCH 1/5. Needs code on both axes: _pipe scrapes a 32-hex session id out of the seed page and POSTs it back as `xf0` with `xpp=3` (200/page) for `xf1` in {3,4}; find_proxies builds a `charEqNum` table from `[>;](\w{4,})=([a-z0-9^]+)` where values may themselves be `digit^othervar` XOR references resolved against the table being built (order-dependent — a real interpreter, not a regex), then rewrites every `+(a^b)+(c^d)` JS port expression into digits. Port faithfully, keep Python's `\b`-free regexes verbatim. |
| `pub struct XseoIn (impl CustomProvider)` | providers.py:Xseo_in | port | ESCAPE HATCH 2/5. Plan is trivially data (`POST http://xseo.in/proxylist` with form `submit=1`) but find_proxies is a JS char-table deobfuscator: scan `\b([a-z])=(\d);` into a table, then substitute `(""+chars)` -> digits. Shares `custom::js_char_table` with NntimeCom. |
| `pub struct NntimeCom (impl CustomProvider)` | providers.py:Nntime_com | port | ESCAPE HATCH 3/5. Byte-identical algorithm to Xseo_in with two differences: the port expression is `(":"+chars)` instead of `(""+chars)`, and the plan is Pages 1..=30 of `proxy-updated-{:02}.htm`. Kept as a separate impl (rather than one parameterized type) only because the pair reads clearer as two 15-line structs sharing `js_char_table` than as one type with a mode flag; revisit if a third appears. Its `_pattern` override is the same host/port lookahead pairing -> `pair_hosts_with_ports`. |
| `fn custom::js_char_table(page: &str, port_expr: &Regex) -> String` | providers.py:Xseo_in.char_js_port_to_num + Nntime_com.char_js_port_to_num (verbatim duplicates) | merge | The two Python methods are copy-paste identical. One free fn taking the port-expression regex. Also fixes a latent Python bug: `''.join(self.charEqNum[ch] for ch in chars if ch != '+')` KeyErrors on any char not in the table, and both classes store `charEqNum` as INSTANCE state carried across pages of the same grab (Xseo_in even declares it as a class attribute, `charEqNum = {}`, shared by every instance) — the table is per-page and must not leak. Rust builds it per page and skips unknown chars. |
| `pub struct GatherproxyCom (impl CustomProvider)` | providers.py:Gatherproxy_com | port | ESCAPE HATCH 4/5. Custom on both axes: POST `{Type: anonymous\|elite, PageIdx: n}`, discover the page count by regexing `href="#(\d+)"` out of page 1 (so the URL list depends on a response), and ports are hex inside single quotes -> `u16::from_str_radix(p, 16)`. FIXES a Python bug: its `_pipe` assigns `urls = [...]` inside the `for t in ['anonymous','elite']` loop instead of extending, so only the 'elite' URLs ever survive and every 'anonymous' page except the probe is silently never fetched (see deviations). Note Gatherproxy_com_socks is NOT an escape hatch — it is a single POST with no body, i.e. `Plan::Single { method: POST }`, pure YAML. |
| `pub struct Rosinstrument { t: u8 } (impl CustomProvider)` | providers.py:Tools_rosinstrument_com_base + Tools_rosinstrument_com + Tools_rosinstrument_com_socks | merge | ESCAPE HATCH 5/5, one impl, two registry rows (`rosinstrument` t=[1,2] http, `rosinstrument_socks` t=[3] socks). Plan is data (Pages 0..=50 x t) but find_proxies is a decoder: pull `sqrt(N)` out of the page, `x = round(sqrt(N))`, percent-decode the `hideTxt('…')` body, XOR every ODD-indexed char code with x, then HTML-unescape, then run the host/port pairing (its pattern uniquely accepts bare hostnames). Python's `self.bodyPattern.findall(page)[0]` IndexErrors when sqrt is present but hideTxt is not — Rust returns empty. The Python base class was split into 3 classes purely to vary two constants; that is the enum-of-data argument in miniature, but the decoder itself is genuinely code. |
| `pub enum ProviderError` | errors.py:BadStatusError (as raised in Provider._get) | port + redesign | Per decision 11 this is the recoverable side: a provider erroring means 'this source yielded nothing this cycle', never fatal to the broker. Deliberately NOT reusing the checker's per-proxy error enum — a provider is not a proxy. #[non_exhaustive] per decision 11. |
| `pub enum FetchError` | providers.py:Provider._get's except tuple (UnicodeDecodeError, BadStatusError, TimeoutError, ClientOSError, ClientResponseError, ServerDisconnectedError) | port + redesign | Python caught six exception types and collapsed them all to `page = ""` + a debug log — the distinction was thrown away at the catch site. Keep three variants because the retry loop and the log actually want them apart (a 403 is permanent, a timeout is worth the retry). reqwest::Error is opaque (research.md: `is_dns()` does not exist in 0.13.4) but that is tolerable HERE — this is the scraping half of the split stack (decision 4); it is the checker that needed hyper for classifiability. |
| `pub enum RegistryError` | provider_utils.py: the ValueError family in from_config + the (yaml.YAMLError, json.JSONDecodeError, ValueError, OSError) catch in _load_provider_config | port + redesign | Every variant carries the file path — Python's `log.error(f"Error loading provider config {config_path}: {e}")` had it only in the message. The last two are load-time validation that Python deferred to a runtime IndexError/TypeError inside a swallowing try block. |
| `data/providers.yaml (the bundled registry file)` | providers.py:PROVIDERS (lines 695-806) | port + redesign | ~30 rows after the dead ones are cut. Row-for-row: 18 bare Provider(url=...) -> `kind: single`; Proxylistplus_com's 3x6 cartesian and Aliveproxy_com's 16 paths -> `kind: urls` with the list written out (a loop that runs once at authoring time is not worth a Plan variant); Blogspot_com(4 domains)/Blogspot_com_socks(socks24.org)/Webanetlabs_net/Checkerproxy_net/Maxiproxies_com/My_proxy_com/Proxy_list_org -> `kind: crawl`; Gatherproxy_com_socks -> `kind: single, method: POST`; the 5 hatches -> `kind: builtin`. The Python registry's `# 49` / `# 5500` trailing comments are 2018 yield estimates — replace them with the 2026 measured yields from liveness.txt (`# measured 2026-07: 2162 ip:port`), because that is the number that decides whether a row stays. |
| `pub type Proto (re-export)` | providers.py: the `proto=('HTTP','CONNECT:80',…)` string tuples | replace-with-lib | Not defined here — `pub use crate::proxy::Proto`. This module only needs it to be `Deserialize + Eq + Hash + Copy`, with serde renames matching the Python strings exactly (`HTTP`, `HTTPS`, `SOCKS4`, `SOCKS5`, `CONNECT:80`, `CONNECT:25`) so the YAML reads like the Python did. Coordinate with the proxy-module map; this is a cross-module dependency, not a definition. |

<details><summary><b>Proposed signatures</b></summary>

```rust
// pub struct ProviderSpec  ← providers.py:Provider (the data half of __init__: url, proto, max_conn, max_tries, timeout)
#[derive(Debug, Clone, Deserialize)] #[serde(deny_unknown_fields)] pub struct ProviderSpec { pub name: String, #[serde(default)] pub proto: Vec<Proto>, pub plan: Plan, #[serde(default)] pub parse: Parse, #[serde(default = "default_max_conn")] pub max_conn: usize, #[serde(default = "default_max_tries")] pub max_tries: u8, #[serde(default = "default_timeout")] pub timeout: Duration }
// pub enum Plan  ← providers.py:Provider._pipe + all ~14 subclass _pipe overrides
#[derive(Debug, Clone, Deserialize)] #[serde(tag = "kind", rename_all = "snake_case")] pub enum Plan { Single { url: Url, #[serde(default)] method: Method, #[serde(default)] form: BTreeMap<String, String>, #[serde(default)] headers: BTreeMap<String, String> }, Urls { urls: Vec<Url> }, Pages { url: String, #[serde(default = "default_page_param")] page_param: String, #[serde(default = "one")] start: u32, count: u32, #[serde(default = "one")] step: u32 }, Crawl { seeds: Vec<Url>, #[serde(with = "serde_regex")] link: Regex, #[serde(default)] base: Option<String>, #[serde(default)] include_seeds: bool, #[serde(default)] method: Method }, Builtin { id: String } }
// pub enum Parse  ← providers.py:Provider.find_proxies/_find_proxies/_pattern + subclass overrides; provider_utils.py:SimpleProvider.find_proxies/APIProvider.find_proxies
#[derive(Debug, Clone, Default, Deserialize)] #[serde(tag = "kind", rename_all = "snake_case")] pub enum Parse { #[default] Default, Auto, Json { #[serde(default)] path: Option<String> }, Regex { #[serde(with = "serde_regex")] re: Regex }, Base64HostPort { #[serde(with = "serde_regex")] re: Regex } }
// pub fn parse::find_ip_port(page: &str) -> Vec<(String, String)>  ← providers.py:Provider.find_proxies + utils.py:IPPortPatternGlobal / IPv6BracketedPortPattern / canonicalize_ip
pub(crate) fn find_ip_port(page: &str) -> Vec<(String, String)>
// pub fn parse::pair_hosts_with_ports(text: &str, host_re: &Regex, port_re: &Regex) -> Vec<(String, String)>  ← providers.py:Gatherproxy_com._pattern_h, Nntime_com._pattern, Tools_rosinstrument_com_base._pattern
pub(crate) fn pair_hosts_with_ports(text: &str, host_re: &Regex, port_re: &Regex) -> Vec<(String, String)>
// pub trait CustomProvider  ← new (the escape hatch for the 5 providers whose _pipe/find_proxies is real code)
#[async_trait::async_trait] pub trait CustomProvider: Send + Sync + 'static { fn name(&self) -> &str; fn proto(&self) -> &[Proto]; async fn fetch(&self, ctx: &ProviderCtx<'_>) -> Result<Vec<Seed>, ProviderError>; }
// pub enum Provider  ← providers.py:Provider (the runtime half)
#[derive(Clone)] pub enum Provider { Spec(ProviderSpec), Custom(Arc<dyn CustomProvider>) }
// impl Provider { pub async fn fetch(&self, ctx: &ProviderCtx<'_>) -> Vec<Seed> }  ← providers.py:Provider.get_proxies + _pipe + _find_on_page + the `proxies` property/setter
pub async fn fetch(&self, ctx: &ProviderCtx<'_>) -> Vec<Seed>
// pub struct Seed  ← providers.py:Provider.proxies setter tuple `(host, port, self.proto)`
#[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Hash)] pub struct Seed { pub host: String, pub port: u16, pub proto: Arc<[Proto]> }
// pub struct ProviderCtx<'a>  ← providers.py:Provider._session / _sem_provider / _max_tries / _timeout / _cookies / utils.py:get_headers
pub struct ProviderCtx<'a> { client: &'a reqwest::Client, sem: Semaphore, max_tries: u8, timeout: Duration }
// impl ProviderCtx<'_> { pub async fn fetch_page(&self, req: &PageRequest) -> Result<String, FetchError> }  ← providers.py:Provider.get + Provider._get
pub async fn fetch_page(&self, req: &PageRequest) -> Result<String, FetchError>
// pub struct PageRequest  ← providers.py: the `{'url':…, 'data':…, 'method':…, 'headers':…}` dicts passed to _find_on_pages
#[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Hash)] pub struct PageRequest { pub url: Url, pub method: Method, pub form: BTreeMap<String, String>, pub headers: BTreeMap<String, String> }
// pub enum Method  ← providers.py: the `method="GET"`/`"POST"` string params
#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, Default, PartialEq, Eq, Hash, Deserialize)] #[serde(rename_all = "UPPERCASE")] pub enum Method { #[default] Get, Post }
// pub struct Registry  ← providers.py:PROVIDERS (module-level list)
#[derive(Clone, Default)] pub struct Registry { providers: Vec<Provider> }
// impl Default for Registry (via pub fn Registry::bundled() -> Registry)  ← providers.py:PROVIDERS literal
pub fn bundled() -> Registry
// fn registry::resolve_builtin(id: &str) -> Option<Arc<dyn CustomProvider>>  ← new (needed because Plan::Builtin is a YAML string)
fn resolve_builtin(id: &str) -> Option<Arc<dyn CustomProvider>>
// pub struct SpysRu (impl CustomProvider)  ← providers.py:Spys_ru
async fn fetch(&self, ctx: &ProviderCtx<'_>) -> Result<Vec<Seed>, ProviderError>
// pub struct Rosinstrument { t: u8 } (impl CustomProvider)  ← providers.py:Tools_rosinstrument_com_base + Tools_rosinstrument_com + Tools_rosinstrument_com_socks
pub struct Rosinstrument { id: &'static str, t: &'static [u8], proto: Vec<Proto> }
// pub enum ProviderError  ← errors.py:BadStatusError (as raised in Provider._get)
#[derive(Debug, thiserror::Error)] #[non_exhaustive] pub enum ProviderError { #[error("fetch failed: {0}")] Fetch(#[from] FetchError), #[error("parse failed: {0}")] Parse(String) }
// pub enum FetchError  ← providers.py:Provider._get's except tuple (UnicodeDecodeError, BadStatusError, TimeoutError, ClientOSError, ClientResponseError, ServerDisconnectedError)
#[derive(Debug, thiserror::Error)] #[non_exhaustive] pub enum FetchError { #[error("HTTP {0}")] BadStatus(u16), #[error("timeout after {0:?}")] Timeout(Duration), #[error(transparent)] Http(reqwest::Error) }
// pub enum RegistryError  ← provider_utils.py: the ValueError family in from_config + the (yaml.YAMLError, json.JSONDecodeError, ValueError, OSError) catch in _load_provider_config
#[derive(Debug, thiserror::Error)] #[non_exhaustive] pub enum RegistryError { #[error("{path}: {source}")] Yaml { path: PathBuf, source: serde_norway::Error }, #[error("{path}: {source}")] Json { path: PathBuf, source: serde_json::Error }, #[error("{path}: {source}")] Io { path: PathBuf, source: std::io::Error }, #[error("{path}: unsupported extension {ext:?} (expected .yaml, .yml or .json)")] Extension { path: PathBuf, ext: String }, #[error("{path}: provider {name:?}: unknown builtin {id:?} (known: {known})")] UnknownBuiltin { path: PathBuf, name: String, id: String, known: String }, #[error("{path}: provider {name:?}: pattern must have exactly 2 capture groups, found {found}")] BadCaptureCount { path: PathBuf, name: String, found: usize } }
```
</details>

**Open questions**

- Which YAML crate? serde_yaml is deprecated and archived by dtolnay (Mar 2024) and research.md does not cover this. Candidates: serde_norway 0.9 (maintained fork by NAV, closest drop-in, active), serde_yaml_ng (thinner fork, smaller maintainer base), serde_yml (fork with a documented history of sketchy maintainer behavior — avoid). Recommending serde_norway pending a lead call. Fallback that dodges the question entirely: bundle the registry as JSON and support only JSON — but that loses comments in providers.yaml, and the comments (measured yields, why a row is disabled) are the point.
- Liveness for the 5 escape-hatch providers is DOMAIN-level only (liveness_custom.txt is a HEAD/GET against the bare domain: spys.ru 200, xseo.in 200, gatherproxy.com 200, nntime.com 200, tools.rosinstrument.com 200). A 200 on a parked or redirect page is not a yield. gatherproxy.com in particular has been widely reported defunct since ~2018, and every one of these five costs 40-120 lines of JS-deobfuscation code to port. STRONG recommendation: before writing each impl, run a full end-to-end yield probe (the real POST with the real form, count ip:port pairs) exactly as liveness.txt did for the bare providers. Any that yield 0 should be dropped, not ported. This could cut the escape hatch from 5 impls to 1-2 and is the single largest scope lever in this module.
- 8 registry entries measure LIVE-domain / HTTP-200 but yield ZERO proxies (proxylists.net, proxytime.ru, httptunnel.ge, cn-proxy.com, aliveproxy.com, webanetlabs.net, maxiproxies.com, cybersyndrome.net) — their page structure changed under the parser. Keep them as YAML rows (a row costs nothing and yields fluctuate) or delete them (a source that yields nothing is a test-flake generator and a per-cycle wasted request)? Recommendation: keep, with a `# measured 2026-07: 0 ip:port` comment on each, since deleting a row is a one-line config edit for the user and re-adding one is not. Needs a lead call.
- liveness.txt measures two sources that are LIVE and commented OUT in the Python: proxydb.net (61 ip:port) and marcosbl.com/lab/proxies (397 ip:port). Both are `kind: single` YAML rows costing 2 lines each. Add them? This is scope creep past a port — but 458 free measured proxies for 4 lines of YAML is a very good trade. Recommend adding, flagged in the changelog as an addition rather than a port.
- Should ProviderSpec support `${ENV_VAR}` expansion in header values? APIProvider's api_key exists precisely because API keys must not live in a YAML file, and the Python template's own comment tells users to inject it from os.environ in code — advice that is unfollowable through load_provider_configs_from_directory, which has no injection point. Env expansion is the obvious fix and ~10 lines, but it is new surface not present in the Python and no bundled provider needs it. Deferring (no env expansion in v1) unless the lead wants it.
- Module layout: the brief specifies mod.rs + spec.rs + registry.rs. The 5 escape-hatch impls are ~400 lines of unrelated JS-deobfuscation and do not belong in any of the three. Proposing src/provider/custom/{mod,spys_ru,xseo_in,nntime_com,gatherproxy,rosinstrument}.rs, with custom/mod.rs holding js_char_table and the resolve_builtin table. Flagging because it deviates from the stated file list.
- Provider::fetch currently returns Vec<Seed> and only logs page failures. Decision 8 says per-proxy failures are COUNTED — does the broker want per-provider fetch stats surfaced (pages_ok / pages_failed / seeds), e.g. for a `--stats` flag? Python only logs them (`log.debug(f'{added}({len(received)}) proxies added(received) from {url}')`). Not adding a stats struct on spec; needs a call from whoever owns the broker/CLI map.

---

## Critique — adversarial review of this design

A skeptical Rust architect was asked to find what is wrong, inconsistent, or
over-engineered in the design above, and told not to praise. Verbatim:

# Review: proxybroker2 → Rust port design

Verdict up front: **not implementable as written.** Six modules independently invented incompatible types for the same five concepts. Two modules specify contradictory ownership for the socket. One module in the deliverable is a stub. Details below, ranked.

---

## WOULD-NOT-COMPILE / CONTRADICTORY CONTRACTS

**1. `proxy.rs` vs `checker.rs` vs `negotiator.rs` — three mutually exclusive answers to "who owns the stream."**
`proxy.rs` builds an entire subsystem (`ProxyConn<'a>{proxy:&'a mut Proxy, stream}`, `Proxy::connect`, `ProxyConn::{send,recv_exact,recv_head,start_tls,replace_stream_with,into_io}`) and calls it "THE cycle-break." `checker.rs` says "**`Proxy` does not own a socket**; each attempt opens, negotiates, uses, and drops its own `TcpStream`" and lists `Proxy.connect/close/send/recv` in its **dropped** section. `negotiator.rs` says `negotiate` takes `Stream` **by value** and "takes no `&Proxy`."
Net: `ProxyConn` and its eight methods have zero callers. One of these two designs is dead code that someone will spend a week writing.
**Fix:** delete `ProxyConn` and everything under it. `checker.rs`+`negotiator.rs` agree with each other and with locked #8; `proxy.rs` lost. `Proxy` = data + `record_attempt(runtime, err)`. Then `proxy.rs`'s `Stream`, `ConnectOpts`, `replace_stream_with`, `into_io` all evaporate.

**2. `error.rs` vs `negotiator.rs`/`proxy.rs` — the per-proxy error enum has two names and two different variant sets.**
`error.rs`: `ProxyError { …, Reset, … }` (Recv+Send merged, documented at length as a deviation). `negotiator.rs`: `ProxyFailure { BadStatus, BadResponse, **Recv**, **Send**, EmptyRecv, Timeout }`, "defined in src/errors.rs," and `map_socks_error` returns `Recv`. `proxy.rs` uses `ProxyError::Reset`. `checker.rs` uses `ProxyError`.
`negotiator.rs` was written against a version of `error.rs` that no longer exists.
**Fix:** `ProxyError` in `src/error.rs`, `Reset` only. Rewrite negotiator's error entries and `map_socks_error` against it. Also settle `error.rs` vs `errors.rs` — five modules say `errors.rs`, the error map itself says `error.rs`.

**3. `negotiator.rs` and `proxy.rs` both define `enum Stream`.** Same two variants, same `Box<TlsStream>`, two modules, no re-export. `server.rs` needs a third (`TcpStream` only, see #6).
**Fix:** one `Stream` in `negotiator.rs` (its only real consumer post-#1), `pub use`d.

**4. `judge.rs` and `checker.rs` both define `JudgePool` — incompatibly.**
`judge.rs`: `JudgePool{ cell: OnceCell<JudgeSet>, cfg, client, resolver, real_ext_ips }`, lazy, `Arc<JudgePool>`, `JudgeSet{http,https,smtp: Vec<Arc<Judge>>}`, `get_random(NegotiatorKind)`, `warm()`.
`checker.rs`: `JudgePool{http,https,smtp: Vec<Judge>}`, eagerly built in `Checker::probe`, owned **by value** as `Checker.judges`, `random(JudgeScheme)`, no OnceCell, no Arc.
They also disagree on **when** probing happens: `judge.rs` says lazy-on-first-`get()` with a `warm()` overlap; `checker.rs` says probing *is* the constructor and `Checker::check` is "UNCONSTRUCTIBLE before the baseline exists"; `broker.rs` says find() awaits it eagerly. These are three different startup sequences.
**Fix:** `judge.rs` owns `JudgePool`/`JudgeSet`/`Judge`. Pick eager (`checker.rs`'s argument is stronger — it turns the ordering into a type fact and surfaces `NoJudges` as an `Err`), which makes the `OnceCell` and `warm()` unnecessary. `Checker` holds `Arc<JudgePool>`.

**5. `Proto` / `ProxyType` / `NegotiatorKind` are the same closed set of 6, named three ways.**
`proxy.rs` defines `ProxyType` (and stores `types: BTreeMap<ProxyType, Option<AnonLevel>>`). `negotiator.rs` defines `NegotiatorKind` and asserts "proxy.rs holds `HashMap<NegotiatorKind, Option<AnonLevel>>`." `checker.rs` uses `NegotiatorKind` throughout, including for `proxy.types`. `provider/` re-exports `crate::proxy::Proto`. `broker.rs` and `cli` use `Proto`. `server.rs` uses `NegotiatorKind`.
**Fix:** one enum, one name (`Proto` — providers and CLI are the user-facing surface), defined in `proxy.rs`, with `Proto::{check_anon_lvl, use_full_path, target_port, judge_scheme, ALL}` living wherever, but the *type* is one type.

**6. `server.rs::open_upstream -> Result<TcpStream, ProxyError>` cannot be "the one function shared with the checker."** The checker needs `Stream` (the HTTPS negotiator returns a TLS stream). `server.rs` explicitly claims this is the single shared negotiation entry point. It isn't; the return types differ.
**Fix:** shared fn returns `Stream`; `server.rs` matches on it (its paths never produce `Tls`, so `Stream::Plain(tcp) => tcp, Tls(_) => unreachable`).

**7. `AnonLevel` (proxy.rs, cli) vs `Anonymity` (checker.rs).** Same 3-variant enum, two names, both `Ord`-worst-to-best.
**Fix:** `AnonLevel`.

**8. `Scheme` defined twice** — `proxy.rs` (`Http|Https`, for `supports_scheme`) and `server.rs` (`Http|Https`, for pool lookup). Plus `JudgeScheme` (`Http|Https|Smtp`) defined in *both* `judge.rs` and `checker.rs`.
**Fix:** `Scheme` in `proxy.rs`, `JudgeScheme` in `judge.rs`, delete the duplicates.

**9. `proxy.rs::ProxyConn::into_io(self) -> TokioIo<Stream>` will not compile.** You cannot move a field out of a type that implements `Drop`. (Moot if #1 lands; flagging in case it doesn't.)

**10. `negotiator.rs::read_head` uses `AsyncBufRead::read_until` on `Stream`, which only implements `AsyncRead`.** Wrapping in `BufReader` to get it either borrows the stream (can't return it) or buffers bytes past the CRLFCRLF that must survive into the tunnel — the same read-buf-loss bug `server.rs` correctly calls out for `hyper::upgrade`.
**Fix:** hand-rolled byte loop over `read`, or `BufReader` whose `into_parts().1` residue is explicitly carried forward.

**11. `resolver.rs::real_ext_ips` and `judge.rs::probe_all` spawn `&self`-borrowing futures into a `JoinSet`.** `JoinSet::spawn` requires `'static`. Neither is.
**Fix:** `futures::future::join_all` (no spawn needed — `judge.rs`'s own `probe_all` entry already says join_all; `resolver.rs`'s entry contradicts it by relying on JoinSet's abort-on-drop, which then isn't available). Or `Arc<Self>`.

**12. `broker.rs::BrokerInner{ resolver: Resolver }` (by value) but `checker.rs`, `server.rs` require `Arc<Resolver>`, and `resolver.rs` insists on `Arc<Resolver>` shared from Broker or the cache-sharing rationale collapses.** You cannot hand out `Arc<Resolver>` from `Arc<BrokerInner>`.
**Fix:** `BrokerInner{ resolver: Arc<Resolver> }`.

**13. `checker.rs` holds `judges: JudgePool` by value; `judge.rs` specifies `Arc<JudgePool>`; `Checker` is shared as `Arc<Checker>`.** Pick one (Arc<JudgePool> is redundant if Checker is already in an Arc — take it by value and delete the Arc).

---

## WRONG BEHAVIOR

**14. `broker.rs` — "drop = cancel" is false for the check tasks.** `ProxyStream` holds `_tasks: JoinSet<()>` and `find()` spawns "the source task" (singular) into it. Per-proxy `check_and_emit` tasks are spawned from inside `grab_loop` — if via `tokio::spawn`, they are detached and survive `ProxyStream` drop, still holding permits and sockets. The entire locked-#8 cancellation story rests on this.
**Fix:** `Run` owns a `JoinSet`/`TaskTracker` + `CancellationToken`; `ProxyStream::drop` cancels the token; `grab_loop` spawns into the tracked set.

**15. `broker.rs` — `take_limit_slot` doesn't stop anything.** It returns `true` on exhaustion and the note says "the caller returns, dropping its Sender clone." That's *one* check task. Every other in-flight task still holds `Arc<Run>` (and its `tx`) and keeps emitting. Python's `_done()` cancels the fleet. Meanwhile `cli::cmd_find` *also* applies `.take(n)`. Two half-enforcements, neither authoritative.
**Fix:** on exhaustion, fire the CancellationToken from #14. Then decide whether the CLI's `.take(n)` is redundant (it is).

**16. `cli` — `--limit 0` means unlimited, but `Query::limit: Option<usize>` and `StreamExt::take(0)` yields nothing.** The mapping `0 → None` is never stated in `build_query`/`cmd_find`. A literal implementation makes the *default* `find` return zero proxies.

**17. `cli::OutputSink` calls `Proxy::as_text()`; `proxy.rs` dropped `as_text()`.** Pick: keep it, or CLI writes `writeln!(w, "{}", p.addr())`.

**18. Three incompatible spellings of the type/level query.**
`broker.rs`: `Query{ types: Vec<TypeSpec> }`, `TypeSpec{proto, levels: Option<Vec<AnonLevel>>}`.
`cli::build_query`: "Query { types: Vec<Proto>, http_levels: Vec<AnonLevel> }".
`checker.rs::CheckerBuilder::new`: `impl IntoIterator<Item=(NegotiatorKind, BTreeSet<Anonymity>)>`.
**Fix:** one type (`Vec<TypeSpec>`), `Checker` takes it, CLI builds it.

**19. Three incompatible spellings of judge config.** `broker.rs`: `judges: Option<Vec<JudgeSpec>>`. `judge.rs`: `JudgeConfig{ urls: Vec<String>, timeout, verify_ssl }`. `checker.rs::CheckerBuilder::judges(Vec<Url>)`. `cli`: `Vec<Url>`.

**20. `error.rs` dropped `Error::NoJudges` as "speculative, no Python grounding" — the grounding is `checker.py:137 raise RuntimeError('Not found judges')`.** `error.rs`'s justification cites the *graceful per-protocol degradation* path (checker.py:106-123) and misses the all-empty fatal at :137. `checker.rs` and `broker.rs` both specify `Error::NoJudges`. `error.rs` is factually wrong here and its `open_questions` entry compounds it.
**Fix:** add `NoJudges`, `NoTypes`, `NoProviders`, `ExtIpUnknown` to `Error`. `error.rs` is not the authority on what the other modules need in the shared enum.

**21. `server.rs::NoProxy` + `ServerError` vs `error.rs::Error::NoProxy` + `broker.rs::serve -> Result<_, Error>`.** Two error taxonomies for the same failure, and `broker.rs::serve` returns `Error` while `server.rs::bind` returns `ServerError`. Also `broker.rs` says `serve` returns a `ServerHandle` "defined in server.rs" — **`server.rs` never defines `ServerHandle`.** It defines `Server::{bind, serve, shutdown_token}`.
**Fix:** `ServerError` as `#[from]`-able source under `Error`, or collapse. Define `ServerHandle` somewhere or change `broker.rs`.

**22. `server.rs::ProxyPool::import_one` serializes every waiter behind one `tokio::Mutex<Receiver>` with a 5s timeout.** N concurrent client connections on a cold pool each wait up to `import_timeout` *in series* — worst case N×5s, and each losing waiter re-enters the loop up to `max_import_retries`=100. Python's `asyncio.Queue.get()` supports multiple concurrent waiters and wakes them fairly. This is a real, load-dependent latency regression with a plausible livelock (100 retries × N tasks all re-queuing wrong-scheme proxies to each other).
**Fix:** one dedicated importer task owning the `Receiver`, pushing into `PoolState` and firing a `Notify`; `get()` waits on the `Notify`. Removes the tokio Mutex entirely.

**23. Unbounded per-`Proxy` log growth in `serve` mode.** `proxy.rs::Proxy{ log: Vec<LogEntry> }` with `Event::{Request{head:String}, Received{head:Vec<u8>}}`, and `server.rs` records an event per proxied request. `broker.rs` explicitly deleted `unique_proxies` retention *because* of unbounded growth — then re-created it inside every pooled `Proxy`. `checker.rs`'s open question ("is `get_log` worth porting at all") is the unresolved cross-cutting decision.
**Fix:** decide now. Recommend: drop the `log` vec entirely (`tracing` span per proxy), keep `Stats` + `runtimes`. Then `Event` shrinks to the `is_timeout()` predicate `record()` needs.

**24. `proxy.rs` and `checker.rs` disagree on the type-display order, and `checker.rs` is wrong.** `checker.rs`'s open question asserts Python's `(len(tp), tp[-1])` key yields `… CONNECT:25, CONNECT:80`. Both are length 10; last chars `'0' < '5'`; the key yields **CONNECT:80 first**, exactly as `proxy.rs` claims. `cli::print_stats` states a third order (`SOCKS5/SOCKS4/HTTPS/HTTP/CONNECT:80/CONNECT:25`).
**Fix:** `proxy.rs` is right. Kill the open question; fix the CLI's stated order.

**25. `judge.rs` — `smtp://smtp.gmail.com` has no port and `url::Url` returns `None` for non-special schemes.** `Judge{ port: u16 }` is non-optional and `JudgeSpec::check` early-returns for SMTP after resolving. No default-port rule is specified anywhere.
**Fix:** `port: url.port().unwrap_or(scheme.default_port())` — 80/443/25.

**26. `judge.rs::Judge::parse` contradicts itself within one entry.** Signature: `fn parse(url) -> Result<Judge, ConfigError>`. Notes: "Concrete design: `Judge::parse` returns `JudgeSpec`." The signature line is stale.

**27. `resolver.rs` — reqwest family pinning is unverified and the whole ext-IP design depends on it.** The open question admits neither `local_address(UNSPECIFIED)` nor a custom `dns::Resolve` was checked against docs.rs. `validate_probe_response` is claimed as the mitigation, which is true — but if pinning silently doesn't work, every v6 probe on a dual-stack host returns a v4 answer, gets rejected, and `real_ext_ips` returns v4-only after burning 7×timeout on the v6 family. That's a 35s startup stall, not a graceful degrade.
**Fix:** verify before committing; if unverifiable, drop family pinning and just probe `api64.ipify.org` + validate.

**28. `error.rs::ProxyError::BadStatusLine` is a variant that, by its own notes, "will never appear in the histogram."** Dead variant kept because `parse_status_line` "needs SOME error type" — but `checker.rs` and `negotiator.rs` both replace status-line parsing with hyper / `Option<u16>`. Nothing constructs it.
**Fix:** delete.

---

## OVER-ENGINEERED (named, as asked)

**29. `server::StreamFailure { cause: ProxyError }`** — a newtype wrapping exactly one field, justified as "not a taxonomy." Return `Result<(), ProxyError>` and compare `err == ProxyError::Timeout`. The `ErrorOnStream` counter bump is the caller's one-liner either way.

**30. `provider::Plan::Builtin { id: String }` + `resolve_builtin(id) -> Option<Arc<dyn CustomProvider>>`** — a string-keyed indirection table so YAML can name 6 hardcoded Rust types. The registry already merges `Provider::Custom` values via `push_custom`. The stated benefit ("users can delete the row") is served by `Registry::retain`. This is a plugin system for a closed set that ships in the same binary.

**31. `proxy.rs::Proxy::with_expected_types`** — described as "two-item mini-builder." It's one setter on a struct whose constructor takes one arg. Just `Proxy::new(addr, expected_types)` or a public field.

**32. `server::Strategy` — one variant.** Defended as "clap rejects `--strategy random` at parse time." A `#[arg(value_parser = ["best"])]` does that without an enum. (Weakest of the over-engineering calls; the map's own reasoning is half-right.)

**33. `server::NoProxy` — three variants that the same map says are all treated identically ("the current port treats all three as shutdown to match Python").** Three variants for a distinction with no consumer, justified "in principle."

**34. `Registry::{merge, push_custom, retain, iter, is_empty}` + `Provider::{name, proto, supports}`** — a general-purpose collection API where `broker.rs` needs exactly `Vec<Provider>` + a filter. `retain`/`merge`/`is_empty` have no named caller in any map.

**35. `judge::JudgeProbe<'a> { client, resolver, real_ext_ips }`** — a 3-borrow bag passed to one function. Fine, but note `resolver` is used once and `real_ext_ips` once; three params would do.

**36. `provider::Parse::Auto`** — try-JSON-then-scan, for zero bundled providers, justified by `SimpleProvider(format="auto")` which the same map's `dropped` section argues nobody needs because the default scanner subsumes every text format.

**37. `provider::Plan::{Single, Urls}`** — `Urls{urls: vec![u]}` *is* `Single` minus method/form/headers. Two variants where `Urls{ reqs: Vec<PageRequest> }` covers both. (`Pages` and `Crawl` earn their keep; these two don't.)

**38. `negotiator.rs` "pin-project the inner"** for `AsyncRead`/`AsyncWrite` on `Stream`. `TcpStream` and `TlsStream<TcpStream>` are both `Unpin`, so `Stream` is `Unpin` and the impls are a plain `match`. No pin-project, no dep.

---

## MISSING

**39. `src/utils.rs` is a stub** — the map is literally `[{rust_item:"test", action:"port", notes:"probe"}]`. Meanwhile it owes: `get_headers(rv)` (judge, checker, negotiator), `REFERER`/`COOKIE` consts (checker), `get_all_ip` (judge, checker), `canonicalize_ip` (resolver defers to it, provider defers to it), `parse_status_line`/`parse_headers`/`get_status_code` (error.rs cites it, others drop it). Three modules have open questions pointing *at* utils.rs for the zone-ID / `IpAddr`-as-canonical decision. **This is the module every other module assumed someone else wrote.**

**40. IP-scanning logic is specified twice.** `provider::parse::find_ip_port` (hand-written two-pass, IPv6 masking) and `utils::get_all_ip` (used by judge + checker for body scanning) and `broker::load_data`'s "IPv6-masking parse" which the map says "belongs in `crate::parse::find_addrs`". Three homes, one algorithm. Pick `crate::parse`, have `utils` re-export or die.

---

## VERDICT

**Not coherent enough to implement from.** The per-module reasoning is unusually good — the Python bug archaeology (`proto=("SOCKS4")` missing comma, the `'SMTP'`/`'CONNECT:25'` disable no-op, the `\r\n`-splice into a TLS record, the heapq tie `TypeError`, the dead `Content-Length: b'25'` branch) is genuinely valuable and worth preserving verbatim. But the maps were written in parallel against a drifting shared vocabulary and never reconciled. An implementer handed all nine will write `ProxyFailure` in one file and `ProxyError` in the next.

**The three things most likely to sink it:**

1. **Type identity chaos.** Five concepts, thirteen names: `Proto`/`ProxyType`/`NegotiatorKind`; `ProxyError`/`ProxyFailure`; `AnonLevel`/`Anonymity`; `Stream`×2; `JudgePool`×2; `Scheme`×2; `JudgeScheme`×2; `GeoData`/`Geo`/`Country`/`CountryCode`; `Error::GeoDb`/`Error::Geo`. **Fix before any code:** write `src/types.rs` (or the lib.rs prelude) as one page naming every shared type and its home, and re-cut every map's signatures against it. This is a half-day and it is the highest-leverage half-day in the project.

2. **The socket-ownership contradiction (#1).** `proxy.rs` designed a whole `ProxyConn` transport layer that `checker.rs` and `negotiator.rs` both explicitly deleted. Someone will implement it. Resolve now, in writing, and delete ~8 entries from `proxy.rs`.

3. **Cancellation and the limit (#14/#15/#16).** The headline API promise — "drop the stream, the fleet stops" — has no mechanism behind it, the limit doesn't stop anything, and `--limit 0` plausibly yields nothing. This is the feature users will hit in the first five minutes.

Runners-up worth fixing before implementation, not during: the `utils.rs` void (#39), the judge-probe timing three-way (#4), the pool importer serialization (#22), and the unbounded `Proxy.log` (#23).
